[←7.5. Example Declarations](Definitions/Example-Declarations/#The-Lean-Language-Reference--Definitions--Example-Declarations "7.5. Example Declarations")[8. Axioms→](Axioms/#axioms "8. Axioms")
#  7.6. Recursive Definitions[🔗](find/?domain=Verso.Genre.Manual.section&name=recursive-definitions "Permalink")
Allowing arbitrary recursive function definitions would make Lean's logic inconsistent. General recursion makes it possible to write circular proofs: “[proposition](The-Type-System/Propositions/#--tech-term-Propositions) `PPP` is true because proposition `PPP` is true”. Outside of proofs, an infinite loop could be assigned the type `[Empty](Basic-Types/The-Empty-Type/#Empty "Documentation for Empty")`, which can be used with ``Lean.Parser.Term.nomatch : term`
Empty match/ex falso. `nomatch e` is of arbitrary type `α : Sort u` if Lean can show that an empty set of patterns is exhaustive given `e`'s type, e.g. because it has no constructors.
`[`nomatch`](Terms/Pattern-Matching/#Lean___Parser___Term___nomatch) or `Empty.rec` to prove any theorem.
Banning recursive function definitions outright would render Lean far less useful: [inductive types](The-Type-System/Inductive-Types/#--tech-term-Inductive-types) are key to defining both predicates and data, and they have a recursive structure. Furthermore, most useful recursive functions do not threaten soundness, and infinite loops usually indicate mistakes in definitions rather than intentional behavior. Instead of banning recursive functions, Lean requires that each recursive function is defined safely. While elaborating recursive definitions, the Lean elaborator also produces a justification that the function being defined is safe.The section on [the elaborator's output](Elaboration-and-Compilation/#elaboration-results) in the overview of elaboration contextualizes the elaboration of recursive definitions in the overall context of the elaborator.
There are five main kinds of recursive functions that can be defined: 

Structurally recursive functions
    
Structurally recursive functions take an argument such that the function makes recursive calls only on strict sub-components of said argument.Strictly speaking, arguments whose types are [indexed families](The-Type-System/Inductive-Types/#--tech-term-indexed-families) are grouped together with their indices, with the whole collection considered as a unit. The elaborator translates the recursion into uses of the argument's [recursor](The-Type-System/Inductive-Types/#--tech-term-recursor). Because every type-correct use of a recursor is guaranteed to avoid infinite regress, this translation is evidence that the function terminates. Applications of functions defined via recursors are definitionally equal to the result of the recursion, and are typically relatively efficient inside the kernel. 

Recursion over well-founded relations
    
Many functions are also difficult to convert to structural recursion; for instance, a function may terminate because the difference between an array index and the size of the array decreases as the index increases, but `Nat.rec` isn't applicable because the index that increases is the function's argument. Here, there is a [measure](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#--tech-term-measure) of termination that decreases at each recursive call, but the measure is not itself an argument to the function. In these cases, [well-founded recursion](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#--tech-term-well-founded-recursion) can be used to define the function. Well-founded recursion is a technique for systematically transforming recursive functions with a decreasing measure into recursive functions over proofs that every sequence of reductions to the measure eventually terminates at a minimum. Applications of functions defined via well-founded recursion are not necessarily definitionally equal to their return values, but this equality can be proved as a proposition. Even when definitional equalities exist, these functions are frequently slow to compute with because they require reducing proof terms that are often very large. 

Recursive functions as partial fixpoints
    
The definition of a function can be understood as an equation that specifies its behavior. In certain cases, the existence of a function that satisfies this specification can be proven even when the recursive function does not necessarily terminate for all inputs. This strategy is even applicable in some cases where the function definition does not necessarily terminate for all inputs. These partial functions emerge as fixed points of these equations are called [_partial fixpoints_](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#--tech-term-partial-fixpoint).
In particular, any function whose return type is in certain monads (e.g. `[Option](Basic-Types/Optional-Values/#Option___none "Documentation for Option")`) can be defined using this strategy. Lean generates additional partial correctness theorems for these monadic functions. As with well-founded recursion, applications of functions defined as partial fixpoints are not definitionally equal to their return values, but Lean generates theorems that propositionally equate the function to its unfolding and to the reduction behavior specified in its definition. 

Partial functions with nonempty codomains
    
For many applications, it's not important to reason about the implementation of certain functions. A recursive function might be used only as part of the implementation of proof automation steps, or it might be an ordinary program that will never be formally proved correct. In these cases, the Lean kernel does not need either definitional or propositional equalities to hold for the definition; it suffices that soundness is maintained. Functions marked ``Lean.Parser.Command.declaration : command```partial` are treated as opaque constants by the kernel and are neither unfolded nor reduced. All that is required for soundness is that their return type is inhabited. Partial functions may still be used in compiled code as usual, and they may appear in propositions and proofs; their equational theory in Lean's logic is simply very weak. 

Unsafe recursive definitions
    
Unsafe definitions have none of the restrictions of partial definitions. They may freely make use of general recursion, and they may use features of Lean that break assumptions about its equational theory, such as primitives for casting (`[unsafeCast](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#unsafeCast "Documentation for unsafeCast")`), checking pointer equality (`[ptrAddrUnsafe](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#ptrAddrUnsafe "Documentation for ptrAddrUnsafe")`), and observing [reference counts](Run-Time-Code/Reference-Counting/#--tech-term-reference-counting) (`[isExclusiveUnsafe](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#isExclusiveUnsafe "Documentation for isExclusiveUnsafe")`). However, any declaration that refers to an unsafe definition must itself be marked ``Lean.Parser.Command.declaration : command```unsafe`, making it clear when logical soundness is not guaranteed. Unsafe operations can be used to replace the implementations of other functions with more efficient variants in compiled code, while the kernel still uses the original definition. The replaced function may be opaque, which results in the function name having a trivial equational theory in the logic, or it may be an ordinary function, in which case the function is used in the logic. Use this feature with care: logical soundness is not at risk, but the behavior of programs written in Lean may diverge from their verified logical models if the unsafe implementation is incorrect.
As described in the [overview of the elaborator's output](Elaboration-and-Compilation/#elaboration-results), elaboration of recursive functions proceeds in two phases:
  1. The definition is elaborated as if Lean's core type theory had recursive definitions. Aside from using recursion, this provisional definition is fully elaborated. The compiler generates code from these provisional definitions.
  2. A termination analysis attempts to use the five techniques to justify the function to Lean's kernel. If the definition is marked ``Lean.Parser.Command.declaration : command```unsafe` or ``Lean.Parser.Command.declaration : command```partial`, then that technique is used. If an explicit ``Lean.Parser.Command.declaration : command```termination_by` or ``Lean.Parser.Command.declaration : command```partial_fixpoint` clause is present, then the indicated technique is the only one attempted. If there is no such clause, then the elaborator performs a search, testing each parameter to the function as a candidate for structural recursion, and attempting to find a measure with a well-founded relation that decreases at each recursive call.


This section describes the rules that govern recursive functions. After a description of mutual recursion, each of the five kinds of recursive definitions is specified, along with the tradeoffs between reasoning power and flexibility that go along with each.
##  7.6.1. Mutual Recursion[🔗](find/?domain=Verso.Genre.Manual.section&name=mutual-syntax "Permalink")
Just as a recursive definition is one that mentions the name being defined in the body of the definition, _mutually recursive_ definitions are definitions that may be recursive or mention one another. To use mutual recursion between multiple declarations, they must be placed in a mutual block.
syntaxMutual Declaration Blocks
The general syntax for mutual recursion is:

```
command ::= ...
    | mutual
        declaration*
      end
```

where the declarations must be definitions or theorems.
The declarations in a mutual block are not in scope in each others' signatures, but they are in scope in each others' bodies. Even though the names are not in scope in signatures, they will not be inserted as auto-bound implicit parameters.
Mutual Block Scope
Names defined in a mutual block are not in scope in each others' signatures.
`[mutual](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#Lean___Parser___Command___mutual "Documentation for syntax")   abbrev NaturalNum : Type := [Nat](Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat")   def n : `Unknown identifier `NaturalNum``NaturalNum := 5 [end](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#Lean___Parser___Command___mutual "Documentation for syntax") `
```
Unknown identifier `NaturalNum`
```

Without the mutual block, the definition succeeds:
`abbrev NaturalNum : Type := [Nat](Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat") def n : NaturalNum := 5 `
[Live ↪](javascript:openLiveLink\("IYIxCcFMDcAIDlgBcCu5gBt4oLawFywAqAngA6QEC8CyAUACaQBmsAdgbaulrtbAFYgA"\))
Mutual Block Scope and Automatic Implicit Parameters
Names defined in a mutual block are not in scope in each others' signatures. Nonetheless, they cannot be used as automatic implicit parameters:
`[mutual](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#Lean___Parser___Command___mutual "Documentation for syntax")   abbrev α : Type := [Nat](Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat")   def identity (x : `Unknown identifier `α``α) : `Unknown identifier `α``α := x [end](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#Lean___Parser___Command___mutual "Documentation for syntax") `
```
Unknown identifier `α`
```

With a different name, the implicit parameter is automatically added:
`[mutual](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#Lean___Parser___Command___mutual "Documentation for syntax")   abbrev α : Type := [Nat](Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat")   def identity (x : β) : β := x [end](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#Lean___Parser___Command___mutual "Documentation for syntax") `
[Live ↪](javascript:openLiveLink\("LYVwLiCGA2BQAE9ICNkCcCmA3ehG4HgFzwAqAngA4aEC88AcpGAvACYYBm8AlmwHZhcwpeAAoAHoXiAm4ACUkqTXhjYGXiyA"\))
Elaborating recursive definitions always occurs at the granularity of mutual blocks, as if there were a singleton mutual block around every declaration that is not itself part of such a block. Local definitions introduced via ``Lean.Parser.Term.letrec : term```let rec` and ``Lean.Parser.Command.declaration : command```where` are lifted out of their context, introducing parameters for captured free variables as necessary, and treated as if they were separate definitions within the ``Lean.Parser.Command.mutual : command``[`mutual`](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#Lean___Parser___Command___mutual) block as well. Thus, helpers defined in a ``Lean.Parser.Command.declaration : command```where` block may use mutual recursion both with one another and with the definition in which they occur, but they may not mention each other in their type signatures.
After the first step of elaboration, in which definitions are still recursive, and before translating recursion using the techniques above, Lean identifies the actually (mutually) recursive cliques among the definitions in the mutual block and processes them separately and in dependency order.
##  7.6.2. Structural Recursion[🔗](find/?domain=Verso.Genre.Manual.section&name=structural-recursion "Permalink")
Structurally recursive functions are those in which each recursive call is on a structurally smaller term than the argument. The same parameter must decrease in all recursive calls; this parameter is called the _decreasing parameter_. Structural recursion is stronger than the primitive recursion that recursors provide, because the recursive call can use more deeply nested sub-terms of the argument, rather than only an immediate sub-term. The constructions used to implement structural recursion are, however, implemented using the recursor; these helper constructions are described in the [section on inductive types](The-Type-System/Inductive-Types/#recursor-elaboration-helpers).
The rules that govern structural recursion are fundamentally _syntactic_ in nature. There are many recursive definitions that exhibit structurally recursive computational behavior, but which are not accepted by these rules; this is a fundamental consequence of the analysis being fully automatic. [Well-founded recursion](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#--tech-term-well-founded-recursion) provides a semantic approach to demonstrating termination that can be used in situations where a recursive function is not structurally recursive, but it can also be used when a function that computes according to structural recursion doesn't satisfy the syntactic requirements.
Structural Recursion vs Subtraction
The function `[countdown](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#countdown-_LPAR_in-Structural-Recursion-vs-Subtraction_RPAR_ "Definition of example")` is structurally recursive. The parameter `n` was matched against the pattern `n' + 1`, which means that `n'` is a direct subterm of `n` in the second branch of the pattern match:
`def countdown (n : [Nat](Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat")) : [List](Basic-Types/Linked-Lists/#List___nil "Documentation for List") [Nat](Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat") :=   [match](Terms/Pattern-Matching/#Lean___Parser___Term___match "Documentation for syntax") n [with](Terms/Pattern-Matching/#Lean___Parser___Term___match "Documentation for syntax")   | 0 => []   | n' + 1 => n' :: [countdown](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#countdown-_LPAR_in-Structural-Recursion-vs-Subtraction_RPAR_ "Definition of example") n' `
Replacing pattern matching with an equivalent Boolean test and subtraction results in an error:
`def `fail to show termination for   countdown' with errors failed to infer structural recursion: Cannot use parameter n:   failed to eliminate recursive application     countdown' n'   failed to prove termination, possible solutions:   - Use `have`-expressions to prove the remaining goals   - Use `termination_by` to specify a different well-founded relation   - Use `decreasing_by` to specify your own tactic for discharging this kind of goal n:[Nat](Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat")h✝:[¬](Basic-Propositions/Logical-Connectives/#Not "Documentation for Not")[(](Type-Classes/Basic-Classes/#BEq___mk "Documentation for BEq.beq")n [==](Type-Classes/Basic-Classes/#BEq___mk "Documentation for BEq.beq") 0[)](Type-Classes/Basic-Classes/#BEq___mk "Documentation for BEq.beq") [=](Basic-Propositions/Propositional-Equality/#Eq___refl "Documentation for Eq") [true](Basic-Types/Booleans/#Bool___false "Documentation for Bool.true")n':[Nat](Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat") := n [-](Type-Classes/Basic-Classes/#HSub___mk "Documentation for HSub.hSub") 1⊢ n [-](Type-Classes/Basic-Classes/#HSub___mk "Documentation for HSub.hSub") 1 [<](Type-Classes/Basic-Classes/#LT___mk "Documentation for LT.lt") n`countdown' (n : [Nat](Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat")) : [List](Basic-Types/Linked-Lists/#List___nil "Documentation for List") [Nat](Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat") := [if](Terms/Conditionals/#termIfThenElse "Documentation for syntax") n == 0 [then](Terms/Conditionals/#termIfThenElse "Documentation for syntax") [] [else](Terms/Conditionals/#termIfThenElse "Documentation for syntax") let n' := n - 1 n' :: countdown' n' `
```
fail to show termination for
  countdown'
with errors
failed to infer structural recursion:
Cannot use parameter n:
  failed to eliminate recursive application
    countdown' n'


failed to prove termination, possible solutions:
  - Use `have`-expressions to prove the remaining goals
  - Use `termination_by` to specify a different well-founded relation
  - Use `decreasing_by` to specify your own tactic for discharging this kind of goal
n:[Nat](Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat")h✝:[¬](Basic-Propositions/Logical-Connectives/#Not "Documentation for Not")[(](Type-Classes/Basic-Classes/#BEq___mk "Documentation for BEq.beq")n [==](Type-Classes/Basic-Classes/#BEq___mk "Documentation for BEq.beq") 0[)](Type-Classes/Basic-Classes/#BEq___mk "Documentation for BEq.beq") [=](Basic-Propositions/Propositional-Equality/#Eq___refl "Documentation for Eq") [true](Basic-Types/Booleans/#Bool___false "Documentation for Bool.true")n':[Nat](Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat") := n [-](Type-Classes/Basic-Classes/#HSub___mk "Documentation for HSub.hSub") 1⊢ n [-](Type-Classes/Basic-Classes/#HSub___mk "Documentation for HSub.hSub") 1 [<](Type-Classes/Basic-Classes/#LT___mk "Documentation for LT.lt") n
```

This is because there was no pattern matching on the parameter `n`. While this function indeed terminates, the argument that it does so is based on properties of if, the equality test, and subtraction, rather than being a generic feature of `[Nat](Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat")` being an [inductive type](The-Type-System/Inductive-Types/#--tech-term-Inductive-types). These arguments are expressed using [well-founded recursion](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#--tech-term-well-founded-recursion), and a slight change to the function definition allows Lean's automatic support for well-founded recursion to construct an alternative termination proof. This version branches on the decidability of [propositional equality](Basic-Propositions/Propositional-Equality/#--tech-term-Propositional-equality) for `[Nat](Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat")` rather than the result of a Boolean equality test:
`def countdown' (n : [Nat](Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat")) : [List](Basic-Types/Linked-Lists/#List___nil "Documentation for List") [Nat](Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat") :=   [if](Terms/Conditionals/#termIfThenElse "Documentation for syntax") n = 0 [then](Terms/Conditionals/#termIfThenElse "Documentation for syntax") []   [else](Terms/Conditionals/#termIfThenElse "Documentation for syntax")     let n' := n - 1     n' :: countdown' n' `
Here, Lean's automation automatically constructs a termination proof from facts about propositional equality and subtraction. It uses well-founded recursion rather than structural recursion behind the scenes.
[Live ↪](javascript:openLiveLink\("CYUwZgBAxg9grgOwC7BgdwRAFJgXBAOQEMkBKCfAGQEsBnJQkigXgCgIIBbEqACwkxpqSXuwgAfCAAYIzAHwQA2gF0xkhAHIIAaggBGWQs0V8sRCnSZNrVqEhnkqDFpwVGZNzXruWY6pExmaQgREEwVMRAAG1oQMQ4okAZjXCDMAFp9eIEtXFN4R0stTSA"\))
Structural recursion may be used explicitly or automatically. With explicit structural recursion, the function definition declares which parameter is the [decreasing parameter](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#--tech-term-decreasing-parameter). If no termination strategy is explicitly declared, Lean performs a search for a decreasing parameter as well as a decreasing measure for use with [well-founded recursion](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#--tech-term-well-founded-recursion). Explicitly annotating structural recursion has the following benefits:
  * It can speed up elaboration, because no search occurs.
  * It documents the termination argument for readers.
  * In situations where structural recursion is explicitly desired, it prevents the accidental use of well-founded recursion.


###  7.6.2.1. Explicit Structural Recursion[🔗](find/?domain=Verso.Genre.Manual.section&name=The-Lean-Language-Reference--Definitions--Recursive-Definitions--Structural-Recursion--Explicit-Structural-Recursion "Permalink")
To explicitly use structural recursion, a function or theorem definition can be annotated with a ``Lean.Parser.Command.declaration : command```termination_by structural` clause that specifies the [decreasing parameter](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#--tech-term-decreasing-parameter). The decreasing parameter may be a reference to a parameter named in the signature. When the signature specifies a function type, the decreasing parameter may additionally be a parameter not named in the signature; in this case, names for the remaining parameters may be introduced by writing them before an arrow (``Lean.Parser.Command.declaration : command```=>`).
Specifying Decreasing Parameters
When the decreasing parameter is a named parameter to the function, it can be specified by referring to its name.
`def half (n : [Nat](Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat")) : [Nat](Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat") :=   [match](Terms/Pattern-Matching/#Lean___Parser___Term___match "Documentation for syntax") n [with](Terms/Pattern-Matching/#Lean___Parser___Term___match "Documentation for syntax")   | 0 | 1 => 0   | n + 2 => half n + 1 termination_by structural n `
When the decreasing parameter is not named in the signature, a name can be introduced locally in the ``Lean.Parser.Command.declaration : command```termination_by` clause.
`def half : [Nat](Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat") → [Nat](Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat")   | 0 | 1 => 0   | n + 2 => half n + 1 termination_by structural n => n `
syntaxExplicit Structural Recursion
The `termination_by structural` clause introduces a decreasing parameter.

```



Specify a termination measure for recursive functions.


```
termination_by a - b

```

indicates that termination of the currently defined recursive function follows because the difference between the arguments `a` and `b` decreases.
If the function takes further argument after the colon, you can name them as follows:

```
def example (a : Nat) : Nat → Nat → Nat :=
termination_by b c => a - b

```

By default, a `termination_by` clause will cause the function to be constructed using well-founded recursion. The syntax `termination_by structural a` (or `termination_by structural _ c => c`) indicates the function is expected to be structural recursive on the argument. In this case the body of the `termination_by` clause must be one of the function's parameters.
If omitted, a termination measure will be inferred. If written as `termination_by?`, the inferred termination measure will be suggested.
`terminationBy ::= ... | `
 
Specify a termination measure for recursive functions.
 
```
termination_by a - b

```
 
indicates that termination of the currently defined recursive function follows because the difference between the arguments `a` and `b` decreases.
If the function takes further argument after the colon, you can name them as follows:

```
def example (a : Nat) : Nat → Nat → Nat :=
termination_by b c => a - b

```

By default, a `termination_by` clause will cause the function to be constructed using well-founded recursion. The syntax `termination_by structural a` (or `termination_by structural _ c => c`) indicates the function is expected to be structural recursive on the argument. In this case the body of the `termination_by` clause must be one of the function's parameters.
If omitted, a termination measure will be inferred. If written as `termination_by?`, the inferred termination measure will be suggested.
`termination_by structural (ident* =>)? term
```

The identifiers before the optional `=>` can bring function parameters into scope that are not already bound in the declaration header, and the mandatory term must indicate one of the function's parameters, whether introduced in the header or locally in the clause.
The decreasing parameter must satisfy the following conditions:
  * Its type must be an [inductive type](The-Type-System/Inductive-Types/#--tech-term-Inductive-types).
  * If its type is an [indexed family](The-Type-System/Inductive-Types/#--tech-term-indexed-families), then all indices must be parameters of the function.
  * If the inductive or indexed family of the decreasing parameter has data type parameters, then these data type parameters may themselves only depend on function parameters that are part of the [fixed prefix](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#--tech-term-fixed-prefix).


A _fixed parameter_ is a function parameter that is passed unmodified in all recursive calls and is not an index of the recursive parameter's type. The _fixed prefix_ is the longest prefix of the function's parameters in which all are fixed.
Ineligible decreasing parameters
The decreasing parameter's type must be an inductive type. In `[notInductive](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#notInductive-_LPAR_in-Ineligible-decreasing-parameters_RPAR_ "Definition of example")`, a function is specified as the decreasing parameter:
`def notInductive (x : [Nat](Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat") → [Nat](Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat")) : [Nat](Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat") :=   [notInductive](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#notInductive-_LPAR_in-Ineligible-decreasing-parameters_RPAR_ "Definition of example") (fun n => x (n+1)) `cannot use specified measure for structural recursion:   its type is not an inductive`termination_by structural x `
```
cannot use specified measure for structural recursion:
  its type is not an inductive
```

If the decreasing parameter is an indexed family, all the indices must be variables. In `[constantIndex](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#constantIndex-_LPAR_in-Ineligible-decreasing-parameters_RPAR_ "Definition of example")`, the indexed family `[Fin'](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#Fin___-_LPAR_in-Ineligible-decreasing-parameters_RPAR_ "Definition of example")` is instead applied to a constant value:
`inductive Fin' : [Nat](Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat") → Type where   | zero : [Fin'](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#Fin___-_LPAR_in-Ineligible-decreasing-parameters_RPAR_ "Definition of example") (n+1)   | succ : [Fin'](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#Fin___-_LPAR_in-Ineligible-decreasing-parameters_RPAR_ "Definition of example") n → [Fin'](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#Fin___-_LPAR_in-Ineligible-decreasing-parameters_RPAR_ "Definition of example") (n+1)  def constantIndex (x : [Fin'](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#Fin___-_LPAR_in-Ineligible-decreasing-parameters_RPAR_ "Definition of example") 100) : [Nat](Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat") := [constantIndex](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#constantIndex-_LPAR_in-Ineligible-decreasing-parameters_RPAR_ "Definition of example") [.zero](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#Fin______zero-_LPAR_in-Ineligible-decreasing-parameters_RPAR_ "Definition of example") `cannot use specified measure for structural recursion:   its type Fin' is an inductive family and indices are not variables     [Fin'](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#Fin___-_LPAR_in-Ineligible-decreasing-parameters_RPAR_ "Definition of example") 100`termination_by structural x `
```
cannot use specified measure for structural recursion:
  its type Fin' is an inductive family and indices are not variables
    [Fin'](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#Fin___-_LPAR_in-Ineligible-decreasing-parameters_RPAR_ "Definition of example") 100
```

The parameters of the decreasing parameter's type must not depend on function parameters that come after varying parameters or indices. In `[afterVarying](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#afterVarying-_LPAR_in-Ineligible-decreasing-parameters_RPAR_ "Definition of example")`, the [fixed prefix](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#--tech-term-fixed-prefix) is empty, because the first parameter `n` varies, so `p` is not part of the fixed prefix:
`inductive WithParam' (p : [Nat](Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat")) : [Nat](Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat") → Type where   | zero : [WithParam'](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#WithParam___-_LPAR_in-Ineligible-decreasing-parameters_RPAR_ "Definition of example") p (n+1)   | succ : [WithParam'](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#WithParam___-_LPAR_in-Ineligible-decreasing-parameters_RPAR_ "Definition of example") p n → [WithParam'](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#WithParam___-_LPAR_in-Ineligible-decreasing-parameters_RPAR_ "Definition of example") p (n+1)  `failed to infer structural recursion: Cannot use parameter x:   failed to eliminate recursive application     [afterVarying](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#afterVarying-_LPAR_in-Ineligible-decreasing-parameters_RPAR_ "Definition of example") [(](Type-Classes/Basic-Classes/#HAdd___mk "Documentation for HAdd.hAdd")n [+](Type-Classes/Basic-Classes/#HAdd___mk "Documentation for HAdd.hAdd") 1[)](Type-Classes/Basic-Classes/#HAdd___mk "Documentation for HAdd.hAdd") p [WithParam'.zero](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#WithParam______zero-_LPAR_in-Ineligible-decreasing-parameters_RPAR_ "Definition of example") `def afterVarying (n : [Nat](Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat")) (p : [Nat](Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat")) (x : [WithParam'](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#WithParam___-_LPAR_in-Ineligible-decreasing-parameters_RPAR_ "Definition of example") p n) : [Nat](Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat") := [afterVarying](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#afterVarying-_LPAR_in-Ineligible-decreasing-parameters_RPAR_ "Definition of example") (n+1) p [.zero](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#WithParam______zero-_LPAR_in-Ineligible-decreasing-parameters_RPAR_ "Definition of example") termination_by structural x `
```
failed to infer structural recursion:
Cannot use parameter x:
  failed to eliminate recursive application
    [afterVarying](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#afterVarying-_LPAR_in-Ineligible-decreasing-parameters_RPAR_ "Definition of example") [(](Type-Classes/Basic-Classes/#HAdd___mk "Documentation for HAdd.hAdd")n [+](Type-Classes/Basic-Classes/#HAdd___mk "Documentation for HAdd.hAdd") 1[)](Type-Classes/Basic-Classes/#HAdd___mk "Documentation for HAdd.hAdd") p [WithParam'.zero](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#WithParam______zero-_LPAR_in-Ineligible-decreasing-parameters_RPAR_ "Definition of example")

```

Furthermore, every recursive call of the functions must be on a _strict sub-term_ of the decreasing parameter.
  * The decreasing parameter itself is a sub-term, but not a strict sub-term.
  * If a sub-term is the [discriminant](Terms/Pattern-Matching/#--tech-term-match-discriminants) of a ``Lean.Parser.Term.match : term`
Pattern matching. `match e, ... with | p, ... => f | ...` matches each given term `e` against each pattern `p` of a match alternative. When all patterns of an alternative match, the `match` term evaluates to the value of the corresponding right-hand side `f` with the pattern variables bound to the respective matched values. If used as `match h : e, ... with | p, ... => f | ...`, `h : e = p` is available within `f`.
When not constructing a proof, `match` does not automatically substitute variables matched on in dependent variables' types. Use `match (generalizing := true) ...` to enforce this.
Syntax quotations can also be used in a pattern match. This matches a `Syntax` value against quotations, pattern variables, or `_`.
Quoted identifiers only match identical identifiers - custom matching such as by the preresolved names only should be done explicitly.
`Syntax.atom`s are ignored during matching by default except when part of a built-in literal. For users introducing new atoms, we recommend wrapping them in dedicated syntax kinds if they should participate in matching. For example, in

```
syntax "c" ("foo" <|> "bar") ...

```

`foo` and `bar` are indistinguishable during matching, but in

```
syntax foo := "foo"
syntax "c" (foo <|> "bar") ...

```

they are not.
`[`match`](Terms/Pattern-Matching/#Lean___Parser___Term___match) expression or other pattern-matching syntax, the pattern that matches the discriminant is a sub-term in the [right-hand side](Terms/Pattern-Matching/#--tech-term-right-hand-side) of each [match alternative](Terms/Pattern-Matching/#--tech-term-match-alternatives). In particular, the rules of [match generalization](Terms/Pattern-Matching/#match-generalization) are used to connect the discriminant to the occurrences of the pattern term in the right-hand side; thus, it respects [definitional equality](The-Type-System/#--tech-term-definitional-equality). The pattern is a _strict_ sub-term if and only if the discriminant is a strict sub-term.
  * If a sub-term is a constructor applied to arguments, then its recursive arguments are strict sub-terms.

Nested Patterns and Sub-Terms
In the following example, the decreasing parameter `n` is matched against the nested pattern `[.succ](Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat.succ") ([.succ](Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat.succ") n)`. Therefore `[.succ](Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat.succ") ([.succ](Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat.succ") n)` is a (non-strict) sub-term of `n`, and consequently both `n` and `[.succ](Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat.succ") n` are strict sub-terms, and the definition is accepted.
`def fib : [Nat](Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat") → [Nat](Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat")   | 0 | 1 => 1   | [.succ](Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat.succ") ([.succ](Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat.succ") n) =>  [fib](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#fib-_LPAR_in-Nested-Patterns-and-Sub-Terms_RPAR_ "Definition of example") n + [fib](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#fib-_LPAR_in-Nested-Patterns-and-Sub-Terms_RPAR_ "Definition of example") ([.succ](Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat.succ") n) termination_by structural n => n `
For clarity, this example uses `[.succ](Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat.succ") n` and `[.succ](Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat.succ") ([.succ](Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat.succ") n)` instead of the equivalent `[Nat](Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat")`-specific `n+1` and `n+2`.
[Live ↪](javascript:openLiveLink\("CYUwZgBGCWBGEC4IDkCGAXCgkwhRgUBBAD4QAMxEAjBALwB8VBFAdAM4CuAxpxABRtceAOwCUtBlDgQhEANST4/Dt2ki86EACcAttCEZoAeyEB9WAE8IrdJq7p2m1ABtp46UA"\))
Matching on Complex Expressions Can Prevent Elaboration
In the following example, the decreasing parameter `n` is not directly the [discriminant](Terms/Pattern-Matching/#--tech-term-match-discriminants) of the ``Lean.Parser.Term.match : term`
`[`match`](Terms/Pattern-Matching/#Lean___Parser___Term___match) expression. Therefore, `n'` is not considered a sub-term of `n`.
``failed to infer structural recursion: Cannot use parameter n:   failed to eliminate recursive application     half n' `def half (n : [Nat](Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat")) : [Nat](Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat") := [match](Terms/Pattern-Matching/#Lean___Parser___Term___match "Documentation for syntax") [Option.some](Basic-Types/Optional-Values/#Option___none "Documentation for Option.some") n [with](Terms/Pattern-Matching/#Lean___Parser___Term___match "Documentation for syntax") | [.some](Basic-Types/Optional-Values/#Option___none "Documentation for Option.some") (n' + 2) => half n' + 1 | _ => 0 termination_by structural n `
```
failed to infer structural recursion:
Cannot use parameter n:
  failed to eliminate recursive application
    half n'

```

Using [well-founded recursion](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#--tech-term-well-founded-recursion), and explicitly connecting the discriminant to the pattern of the match, this definition can be accepted.
`def half (n : [Nat](Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat")) : [Nat](Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat") :=   [match](Terms/Pattern-Matching/#Lean___Parser___Term___match "Documentation for syntax") h : [Option.some](Basic-Types/Optional-Values/#Option___none "Documentation for Option.some") n [with](Terms/Pattern-Matching/#Lean___Parser___Term___match "Documentation for syntax")   | [.some](Basic-Types/Optional-Values/#Option___none "Documentation for Option.some") (n' + 2) => half n' + 1   | _ => 0 termination_by n decreasing_by [simp_all](Tactic-Proofs/Tactic-Reference/#simp_all "Documentation for tactic")n:[Nat](Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat")n':[Nat](Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat")h:n [=](Basic-Propositions/Propositional-Equality/#Eq___refl "Documentation for Eq") n' [+](Type-Classes/Basic-Classes/#HAdd___mk "Documentation for HAdd.hAdd") 1 [+](Type-Classes/Basic-Classes/#HAdd___mk "Documentation for HAdd.hAdd") 1⊢ n' [<](Type-Classes/Basic-Classes/#LT___mk "Documentation for LT.lt") n' [+](Type-Classes/Basic-Classes/#HAdd___mk "Documentation for HAdd.hAdd") 1 [+](Type-Classes/Basic-Classes/#HAdd___mk "Documentation for HAdd.hAdd") 1; [omega](Tactic-Proofs/Tactic-Reference/#omega "Documentation for tactic")All goals completed! 🐙 `
Similarly, the following example fails: although `xs.[tail](Basic-Types/Linked-Lists/#List___tail "Documentation for List.tail")` would reduce to a strict sub-term of `xs`, this is not visible to Lean according to the rules above. In particular, `xs.[tail](Basic-Types/Linked-Lists/#List___tail "Documentation for List.tail")` is not [definitionally equal](The-Type-System/#--tech-term-definitional-equality) to a strict sub-term of `xs`.
``failed to infer structural recursion: Cannot use parameter #2:   failed to eliminate recursive application     [listLen](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#listLen-_LPAR_in-Matching-on-Complex-Expressions-Can-Prevent-Elaboration_RPAR_ "Definition of example") xs.[tail](Basic-Types/Linked-Lists/#List___tail "Documentation for List.tail") `def listLen : [List](Basic-Types/Linked-Lists/#List___nil "Documentation for List") α → [Nat](Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat") | [] => 0 | xs => [listLen](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#listLen-_LPAR_in-Matching-on-Complex-Expressions-Can-Prevent-Elaboration_RPAR_ "Definition of example") xs.[tail](Basic-Types/Linked-Lists/#List___tail "Documentation for List.tail") + 1 termination_by structural xs => xs `
[Live ↪](javascript:openLiveLink\("CYUwZgBAFghgNpAFAOwgLggORgFwJTpa7oC8AUBBALa4DGU0hA8gA44CWA9sgHQDOnKiAioA7uxxQKEAD4R+g4SgDkEANQQATARIA+aPEjJVGgIzS5AfQh6IABjI4QAJyrtkuLsksAjAJ4iZKC0ziAwfO4A5r4BEVQslvBwANwQipEwQA"\))
Simultaneous Matching vs Matching Pairs for Structural Recursion
An important consequence of the strategies that are used to prove termination is that **simultaneous matching of two[discriminants](Terms/Pattern-Matching/#--tech-term-match-discriminants) is not equivalent to matching a pair**. Simultaneous matching maintains the connection between the discriminants and the patterns, allowing the pattern matching to refine the types of the assumptions in the local context as well as the expected type of the ``Lean.Parser.Term.match : term`
`[`match`](Terms/Pattern-Matching/#Lean___Parser___Term___match). Essentially, the elaboration rules for ``Lean.Parser.Term.match : term`
`[`match`](Terms/Pattern-Matching/#Lean___Parser___Term___match) treat the discriminants specially, and changing discriminants in a way that preserves the run-time meaning of a program does not necessarily preserve the compile-time meaning.
This function that finds the minimum of two natural numbers is defined by structural recursion on its first parameter:
`def min' (n k : [Nat](Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat")) : [Nat](Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat") :=   [match](Terms/Pattern-Matching/#Lean___Parser___Term___match "Documentation for syntax") n, k [with](Terms/Pattern-Matching/#Lean___Parser___Term___match "Documentation for syntax")   | 0, _ => 0   | _, 0 => 0   | n' + 1, k' + 1 => min' n' k' + 1 termination_by structural n `
Replacing the simultaneous pattern match on both parameters with a match on a pair causes termination analysis to fail:
``failed to infer structural recursion: Cannot use parameter n:   failed to eliminate recursive application     min' n' k' `def min' (n k : [Nat](Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat")) : [Nat](Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat") := [match](Terms/Pattern-Matching/#Lean___Parser___Term___match "Documentation for syntax") (n, k) [with](Terms/Pattern-Matching/#Lean___Parser___Term___match "Documentation for syntax") | (0, _) => 0 | (_, 0) => 0 | (n' + 1, k' + 1) => min' n' k' + 1 termination_by structural n `
```
failed to infer structural recursion:
Cannot use parameter n:
  failed to eliminate recursive application
    min' n' k'

```

This is because the analysis only considers direct pattern matching on parameters when matching recursive calls to strictly-smaller argument values. Wrapping the discriminants in a pair breaks the connection.
Structural Recursion Under Pairs
This function that finds the minimum of the two components of a pair can't be elaborated via structural recursion.
``failed to infer structural recursion: Cannot use parameter nk:   the type [Nat](Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat") [×](Basic-Types/Tuples/#Prod___mk "Documentation for Prod") [Nat](Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat") does not have a `.brecOn` recursor `def min' (nk : [Nat](Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat") × [Nat](Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat")) : [Nat](Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat") := [match](Terms/Pattern-Matching/#Lean___Parser___Term___match "Documentation for syntax") nk [with](Terms/Pattern-Matching/#Lean___Parser___Term___match "Documentation for syntax") | (0, _) => 0 | (_, 0) => 0 | (n' + 1, k' + 1) => min' (n', k') + 1 termination_by structural nk `
```
failed to infer structural recursion:
Cannot use parameter nk:
  the type [Nat](Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat") [×](Basic-Types/Tuples/#Prod___mk "Documentation for Prod") [Nat](Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat") does not have a `.brecOn` recursor

```

This is because the parameter's type, `[Prod](Basic-Types/Tuples/#Prod___mk "Documentation for Prod")`, is not recursive. Thus, its constructor has no recursive parameters that can be exposed by pattern matching.
This definition is accepted using [well-founded recursion](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#--tech-term-well-founded-recursion), however:
`def min' (nk : [Nat](Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat") × [Nat](Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat")) : [Nat](Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat") :=   [match](Terms/Pattern-Matching/#Lean___Parser___Term___match "Documentation for syntax") nk [with](Terms/Pattern-Matching/#Lean___Parser___Term___match "Documentation for syntax")   | (0, _) => 0   | (_, 0) => 0   | (n' + 1, k' + 1) => min' (n', k') + 1 termination_by nk `
[Live ↪](javascript:openLiveLink\("CYUwZgBAtglgdgcggCjgawgLggOQIYAuEA67oQJRZlGYC8AUBNIQMYAWE6EA7jAW4wgAfFAAYANBAD6lWgD4IowSORTJo2QqVMViCAGoIARklokho5ujwkqBKYSUL9AiABOsOIRgB7OFIAjAE9ONCA"\))
Structural Recursion and Definitional Equality
Even though the recursive occurrence of `[countdown](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#countdown-_LPAR_in-Structural-Recursion-and-Definitional-Equality_RPAR_ "Definition of example")` is applied to a term that is not a strict sub-term of the decreasing parameter, the following definition is accepted:
`def countdown (n : [Nat](Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat")) : [List](Basic-Types/Linked-Lists/#List___nil "Documentation for List") [Nat](Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat") :=   [match](Terms/Pattern-Matching/#Lean___Parser___Term___match "Documentation for syntax") n [with](Terms/Pattern-Matching/#Lean___Parser___Term___match "Documentation for syntax")   | 0 => []   | n' + 1 => n' :: [countdown](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#countdown-_LPAR_in-Structural-Recursion-and-Definitional-Equality_RPAR_ "Definition of example") (n' + 0) termination_by structural n `
This is because `n' + 0` is [definitionally equal](The-Type-System/#--tech-term-definitional-equality) to `n'`, which is a strict sub-term of `n`. [Sub-terms](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#--tech-term-strict-sub-term) that result from pattern matching are connected to the [discriminant](Terms/Pattern-Matching/#--tech-term-match-discriminants) using the rules for [match generalization](Terms/Pattern-Matching/#match-generalization), which respect definitional equality.
In `[countdown'](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#countdown___-_LPAR_in-Structural-Recursion-and-Definitional-Equality_RPAR_ "Definition of example")`, the recursive occurrence is applied to `0 + n'`, which is not definitionally equal to `n'` because addition on natural numbers is structurally recursive in its second parameter:
``failed to infer structural recursion: Cannot use parameter n:   failed to eliminate recursive application     [countdown'](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#countdown___-_LPAR_in-Structural-Recursion-and-Definitional-Equality_RPAR_ "Definition of example") [(](Type-Classes/Basic-Classes/#HAdd___mk "Documentation for HAdd.hAdd")0 [+](Type-Classes/Basic-Classes/#HAdd___mk "Documentation for HAdd.hAdd") n'[)](Type-Classes/Basic-Classes/#HAdd___mk "Documentation for HAdd.hAdd") `def countdown' (n : [Nat](Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat")) : [List](Basic-Types/Linked-Lists/#List___nil "Documentation for List") [Nat](Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat") := [match](Terms/Pattern-Matching/#Lean___Parser___Term___match "Documentation for syntax") n [with](Terms/Pattern-Matching/#Lean___Parser___Term___match "Documentation for syntax") | 0 => [] | n' + 1 => n' :: [countdown'](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#countdown___-_LPAR_in-Structural-Recursion-and-Definitional-Equality_RPAR_ "Definition of example") (0 + n') termination_by structural n `
```
failed to infer structural recursion:
Cannot use parameter n:
  failed to eliminate recursive application
    [countdown'](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#countdown___-_LPAR_in-Structural-Recursion-and-Definitional-Equality_RPAR_ "Definition of example") [(](Type-Classes/Basic-Classes/#HAdd___mk "Documentation for HAdd.hAdd")0 [+](Type-Classes/Basic-Classes/#HAdd___mk "Documentation for HAdd.hAdd") n'[)](Type-Classes/Basic-Classes/#HAdd___mk "Documentation for HAdd.hAdd")

```

[Live ↪](javascript:openLiveLink\("CYUwZgBAxg9grgOwC7BgdwRAFJgXBAOQEMkBKCfAGQEsBnJQkigXgCgIIBbEqACwkxpqSXuwgAfCAAYIzAHwQA2gF0xkhAHIIAaggBGWQs0V8sRCnSYcW3VNKskIAE6dqCEtRgIA+gCMAnhD0TnBQSHBORAA2AkA"\))
###  7.6.2.2. Mutual Structural Recursion[🔗](find/?domain=Verso.Genre.Manual.section&name=mutual-structural-recursion "Permalink")
Lean supports the definition of [mutually recursive](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#--tech-term-mutually-recursive) functions using structural recursion. Mutual recursion may be introduced using a [mutual block](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#--tech-term-mutual-block), but it also results from ``Lean.Parser.Term.letrec : term```let rec` expressions and ``Lean.Parser.Command.declaration : command```where` blocks. The rules for mutual structural recursion are applied to a group of actually mutually recursive, lifted definitions, that results from the [elaboration steps](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#mutual-syntax) for mutual groups. If every function in the mutual group has a `termination_by structural` annotation indicating that function’s decreasing argument, then structural recursion is used to translate the definitions.
The requirements on the decreasing argument above are extended:
  * All the types of all the decreasing arguments must be from the same inductive type, or more generally from the same [mutual group of inductive types](The-Type-System/Inductive-Types/#mutual-inductive-types).
  * The parameters of the decreasing parameter's types must be the same for all functions, and may depend only on the _common_ fixed prefix of function arguments.


The functions do not have to be in a one-to-one correspondence to the mutual inductive types. Multiple functions can have a decreasing argument of the same type, and not all types that are mutually recursive with the decreasing argument need have a corresponding function.
Mutual Structural Recursion Over Non-Mutual Types
The following example demonstrates mutual recursion over a non-mutual inductive data type:
`[mutual](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#Lean___Parser___Command___mutual "Documentation for syntax")   def even : [Nat](Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat") → Prop     | 0 => [True](Basic-Propositions/Truth/#True___intro "Documentation for True")     | n+1 => [odd](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#odd-_LPAR_in-Mutual-Structural-Recursion-Over-Non-Mutual-Types_RPAR_ "Definition of example") n   termination_by structural n => n    def odd : [Nat](Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat") → Prop     | 0 => [False](Basic-Propositions/Truth/#False "Documentation for False")     | n+1 => [even](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#even-_LPAR_in-Mutual-Structural-Recursion-Over-Non-Mutual-Types_RPAR_ "Definition of example") n   termination_by structural n => n [end](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#Lean___Parser___Command___mutual "Documentation for syntax") `
[Live ↪](javascript:openLiveLink\("LYVwLiCGA2BQAE8AmBTAZvFA3FA7eAXPAHKRjyBJhPAAoBOA9gA4KLwA+8ADPALwB88ACq0QKFog64A1AEZeA+kiTxcLMClrAAlrjJb6uAPoAjAJ7wAzmBEBjCLRgr5K2C1QZFyoqXJU6TcXYuZwAxGAsxViDpOX5MHHxVRHVNHT0DE3MrW3tHfDjVPCQgA"\))
Mutual Structural Recursion Over Mutual Types
The following example demonstrates recursion over mutually inductive types. The functions `[Exp.size](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#Exp___size-_LPAR_in-Mutual-Structural-Recursion-Over-Mutual-Types_RPAR_ "Definition of example")` and `[App.size](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#App___size-_LPAR_in-Mutual-Structural-Recursion-Over-Mutual-Types_RPAR_ "Definition of example")` are mutually recursive.

The definition of `[App.numArgs](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#App___numArgs-_LPAR_in-Mutual-Structural-Recursion-Over-Mutual-Types_RPAR_ "Definition of example")` is structurally recursive over type `[App](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#App-_LPAR_in-Mutual-Structural-Recursion-Over-Mutual-Types_RPAR_ "Definition of example")`. It demonstrates that not all inductive types in the mutual group need to be handled.
`def App.numArgs : [App](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#App-_LPAR_in-Mutual-Structural-Recursion-Over-Mutual-Types_RPAR_ "Definition of example") → [Nat](Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat")   | [.fn](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#App___fn-_LPAR_in-Mutual-Structural-Recursion-Over-Mutual-Types_RPAR_ "Definition of example") _ => 0   | [.app](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#App___app-_LPAR_in-Mutual-Structural-Recursion-Over-Mutual-Types_RPAR_ "Definition of example") a _ => a.[numArgs](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#App___numArgs-_LPAR_in-Mutual-Structural-Recursion-Over-Mutual-Types_RPAR_ "Definition of example") + 1 termination_by structural a => a `

###  7.6.2.3. Inferring Structural Recursion[🔗](find/?domain=Verso.Genre.Manual.section&name=inferring-structural-recursion "Permalink")
If no `termination_by` clauses are present in a recursive or mutually recursive function definition, then Lean attempts to infer a suitable structurally decreasing argument, effectively by trying all suitable parameters in sequence. If this search fails, Lean then attempts to infer [well-founded recursion](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#--tech-term-well-founded-recursion).
For mutually recursive functions, all combinations of parameters are tried, up to a limit to avoid combinatorial explosion. If only some of the mutually recursive functions have `termination_by structural` clauses, then only those parameters are considered, while for the other functions all parameters are considered for structural recursion.
A `termination_by?` clause causes the inferred termination annotation to be shown. It can be automatically added to the source file using the offered suggestion or code action.
Inferred Termination Annotations
Lean automatically infers that the function `[half](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#half-_LPAR_in-Inferred-Termination-Annotations_RPAR_ "Definition of example")` is structurally recursive. The `termination_by?` clause causes the inferred termination annotation to be displayed, and it can be automatically added to the source file with a single click.
`def half : [Nat](Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat") → [Nat](Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat")   | 0 | 1 => 0   | n + 2 => [half](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#half-_LPAR_in-Inferred-Termination-Annotations_RPAR_ "Definition of example") n + 1 `Try this:   [apply] termination_by structural x => x`termination_by? `
```
Try this:
  [apply] termination_by structural x => x
```

[Live ↪](javascript:openLiveLink\("CYUwZgBAFghgNpAXBAcjALhQSYSowKAggB8IAGYiARggF4A+MgigOwgGoIAmWh2BCVh0p50IAE4BbAJbMMUgPbMA+gCMAngH4gA"\))
###  7.6.2.4. Elaboration Using Course-of-Values Recursion[🔗](find/?domain=Verso.Genre.Manual.section&name=elab-as-course-of-values "Permalink")
In this section, the construction used to elaborate structurally recursive functions is explained in more detail. This elaboration uses the [`below` and `brecOn` constructions](The-Type-System/Inductive-Types/#recursor-elaboration-helpers) that are automatically generated from inductive types' recursors.
Recursion vs Recursors
Addition of natural numbers can be defined via recursion on the second argument. This function is straightforwardly structurally recursive.
`def add (n : [Nat](Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat")) : [Nat](Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat") → [Nat](Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat")   | [.zero](Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat.zero") => n   | [.succ](Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat.succ") k => [.succ](Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat.succ") ([add](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#add-_LPAR_in-Recursion-vs-Recursors_RPAR_ "Definition of example") n k) `
Defined using `Nat.rec`, it is much further from the notations that most people are used to.
`def add' (n : [Nat](Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat")) :=   Nat.rec (motive := fun _ => [Nat](Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat"))     n     (fun k soFar => [.succ](Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat.succ") soFar) `
Structural recursive calls made on data that isn't the immediate child of the function parameter requires either creativity or a complex yet systematic encoding.
`def half : [Nat](Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat") → [Nat](Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat")   | 0 | 1 => 0   | n + 2 => [half](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#half-_LPAR_in-Recursion-vs-Recursors_RPAR_ "Definition of example") n + 1 `
One way to think about this function is as a structural recursion that flips a bit at each call, only incrementing the result when the bit is set.
`def helper : [Nat](Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat") → [Bool](Basic-Types/Booleans/#Bool___false "Documentation for Bool") → [Nat](Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat") :=   Nat.rec (motive := fun _ => [Bool](Basic-Types/Booleans/#Bool___false "Documentation for Bool") → [Nat](Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat"))     (fun _ => 0)     (fun _ soFar =>       fun b =>         ([if](Terms/Conditionals/#termIfThenElse "Documentation for syntax") b [then](Terms/Conditionals/#termIfThenElse "Documentation for syntax") [Nat.succ](Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat.succ") [else](Terms/Conditionals/#termIfThenElse "Documentation for syntax") id) (soFar !b))  def half' (n : [Nat](Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat")) : [Nat](Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat") := [helper](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#helper-_LPAR_in-Recursion-vs-Recursors_RPAR_ "Definition of example") n [false](Basic-Types/Booleans/#Bool___false "Documentation for Bool.false") ```[[](Basic-Types/Linked-Lists/#List___nil "Documentation for List.cons")0[,](Basic-Types/Linked-Lists/#List___nil "Documentation for List.cons") 0[,](Basic-Types/Linked-Lists/#List___nil "Documentation for List.cons") 1[,](Basic-Types/Linked-Lists/#List___nil "Documentation for List.cons") 1[,](Basic-Types/Linked-Lists/#List___nil "Documentation for List.cons") 2[,](Basic-Types/Linked-Lists/#List___nil "Documentation for List.cons") 2[,](Basic-Types/Linked-Lists/#List___nil "Documentation for List.cons") 3[,](Basic-Types/Linked-Lists/#List___nil "Documentation for List.cons") 3[,](Basic-Types/Linked-Lists/#List___nil "Documentation for List.cons") 4[]](Basic-Types/Linked-Lists/#List___nil "Documentation for List.cons")`[#eval](Interacting-with-Lean/#Lean___Parser___Command___eval "Documentation for syntax") [0, 1, 2, 3, 4, 5, 6, 7, 8].[map](Basic-Types/Linked-Lists/#List___map "Documentation for List.map") [half'](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#half___-_LPAR_in-Recursion-vs-Recursors_RPAR_ "Definition of example") `
```
[[](Basic-Types/Linked-Lists/#List___nil "Documentation for List.cons")0[,](Basic-Types/Linked-Lists/#List___nil "Documentation for List.cons") 0[,](Basic-Types/Linked-Lists/#List___nil "Documentation for List.cons") 1[,](Basic-Types/Linked-Lists/#List___nil "Documentation for List.cons") 1[,](Basic-Types/Linked-Lists/#List___nil "Documentation for List.cons") 2[,](Basic-Types/Linked-Lists/#List___nil "Documentation for List.cons") 2[,](Basic-Types/Linked-Lists/#List___nil "Documentation for List.cons") 3[,](Basic-Types/Linked-Lists/#List___nil "Documentation for List.cons") 3[,](Basic-Types/Linked-Lists/#List___nil "Documentation for List.cons") 4[]](Basic-Types/Linked-Lists/#List___nil "Documentation for List.cons")
```

Instead of creativity, a general technique called course-of-values recursion can be used. Course-of-values recursion uses helpers that can be systematically derived for every inductive type, defined in terms of the recursor; Lean derives them automatically. For every `[Nat](Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat")` `n`, the type `n.below (motive := mot)` provides a value of type `mot k` for all `k < n`, represented as an iterated dependent pair type. The course-of-values recursor `Nat.brecOn` allows a function to use the result for any smaller `[Nat](Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat")`. Using it to define the function is inconvenient:
`noncomputable def half'' (n : [Nat](Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat")) : [Nat](Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat") :=   Nat.brecOn n (motive := fun _ => [Nat](Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat"))     fun k soFar =>       [match](Terms/Pattern-Matching/#Lean___Parser___Term___match "Documentation for syntax") k, soFar [with](Terms/Pattern-Matching/#Lean___Parser___Term___match "Documentation for syntax")       | 0, _ | 1, _ => 0       | _ + 2, ⟨_, ⟨h, _⟩⟩ => h + 1 `
The function is marked ``Lean.Parser.Command.declaration : command```noncomputable` because the compiler doesn't support generating code for course-of-values recursion, which is intended for reasoning rather that efficient code. The kernel can still be used to test the function, however:
``[[](Basic-Types/Linked-Lists/#List___nil "Documentation for List.cons")0[,](Basic-Types/Linked-Lists/#List___nil "Documentation for List.cons") 0[,](Basic-Types/Linked-Lists/#List___nil "Documentation for List.cons") 1[,](Basic-Types/Linked-Lists/#List___nil "Documentation for List.cons") 1[,](Basic-Types/Linked-Lists/#List___nil "Documentation for List.cons") 2[,](Basic-Types/Linked-Lists/#List___nil "Documentation for List.cons") 2[,](Basic-Types/Linked-Lists/#List___nil "Documentation for List.cons") 3[,](Basic-Types/Linked-Lists/#List___nil "Documentation for List.cons") 3[,](Basic-Types/Linked-Lists/#List___nil "Documentation for List.cons") 4[]](Basic-Types/Linked-Lists/#List___nil "Documentation for List.cons")`[#reduce](Interacting-with-Lean/#Lean___reduceCmd "Documentation for syntax") [0,1,2,3,4,5,6,7,8].[map](Basic-Types/Linked-Lists/#List___map "Documentation for List.map") [half''](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#half______-_LPAR_in-Recursion-vs-Recursors_RPAR_ "Definition of example") `
```
[[](Basic-Types/Linked-Lists/#List___nil "Documentation for List.cons")0[,](Basic-Types/Linked-Lists/#List___nil "Documentation for List.cons") 0[,](Basic-Types/Linked-Lists/#List___nil "Documentation for List.cons") 1[,](Basic-Types/Linked-Lists/#List___nil "Documentation for List.cons") 1[,](Basic-Types/Linked-Lists/#List___nil "Documentation for List.cons") 2[,](Basic-Types/Linked-Lists/#List___nil "Documentation for List.cons") 2[,](Basic-Types/Linked-Lists/#List___nil "Documentation for List.cons") 3[,](Basic-Types/Linked-Lists/#List___nil "Documentation for List.cons") 3[,](Basic-Types/Linked-Lists/#List___nil "Documentation for List.cons") 4[]](Basic-Types/Linked-Lists/#List___nil "Documentation for List.cons")
```

The dependent pattern matching in the body of `[half''](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#half______-_LPAR_in-Recursion-vs-Recursors_RPAR_ "Definition of example")` can also be encoded using recursors (specifically, `Nat.casesOn`), if necessary:
`noncomputable def half''' (n : [Nat](Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat")) : [Nat](Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat") :=   n.brecOn (motive := fun _ => [Nat](Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat"))     fun k =>       k.casesOn         (motive :=           fun k' =>             (k'.below (motive := fun _ => [Nat](Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat"))) →             [Nat](Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat"))         (fun _ => 0)         (fun k' =>           k'.casesOn             (motive :=               fun k'' =>                 (k''.[succ](Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat.succ").below (motive := fun _ => [Nat](Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat"))) →                 [Nat](Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat"))             (fun _ => 0)             (fun _ soFar => soFar.2.1.[succ](Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat.succ"))) `
This definition still works.
``[[](Basic-Types/Linked-Lists/#List___nil "Documentation for List.cons")0[,](Basic-Types/Linked-Lists/#List___nil "Documentation for List.cons") 0[,](Basic-Types/Linked-Lists/#List___nil "Documentation for List.cons") 1[,](Basic-Types/Linked-Lists/#List___nil "Documentation for List.cons") 1[,](Basic-Types/Linked-Lists/#List___nil "Documentation for List.cons") 2[,](Basic-Types/Linked-Lists/#List___nil "Documentation for List.cons") 2[,](Basic-Types/Linked-Lists/#List___nil "Documentation for List.cons") 3[,](Basic-Types/Linked-Lists/#List___nil "Documentation for List.cons") 3[,](Basic-Types/Linked-Lists/#List___nil "Documentation for List.cons") 4[]](Basic-Types/Linked-Lists/#List___nil "Documentation for List.cons")`[#reduce](Interacting-with-Lean/#Lean___reduceCmd "Documentation for syntax") [0,1,2,3,4,5,6,7,8].[map](Basic-Types/Linked-Lists/#List___map "Documentation for List.map") [half''](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#half______-_LPAR_in-Recursion-vs-Recursors_RPAR_ "Definition of example") `
```
[[](Basic-Types/Linked-Lists/#List___nil "Documentation for List.cons")0[,](Basic-Types/Linked-Lists/#List___nil "Documentation for List.cons") 0[,](Basic-Types/Linked-Lists/#List___nil "Documentation for List.cons") 1[,](Basic-Types/Linked-Lists/#List___nil "Documentation for List.cons") 1[,](Basic-Types/Linked-Lists/#List___nil "Documentation for List.cons") 2[,](Basic-Types/Linked-Lists/#List___nil "Documentation for List.cons") 2[,](Basic-Types/Linked-Lists/#List___nil "Documentation for List.cons") 3[,](Basic-Types/Linked-Lists/#List___nil "Documentation for List.cons") 3[,](Basic-Types/Linked-Lists/#List___nil "Documentation for List.cons") 4[]](Basic-Types/Linked-Lists/#List___nil "Documentation for List.cons")
```

However, it is now far from the original definition and it has become difficult for most people to understand. Recursors are an excellent logical foundation, but not an easy way to write programs or proofs.
[Live ↪](javascript:openLiveLink\("CYUwZgBAhswQFAOwgLggOSgFwJSo9hIEmEBWAUBBAD4QB0AXiAE4D2EAvAHwSIXV0BnAK4BjERADWHbrWFiEMOMgk4yZUJEUByBMjSZcqdnwO0mIcfAC2LLAEsAbiCMQwQ5AH1ppVZUq8/BDdlCAEWADEoJm9ZUXEwyKZVdXAIAAsoABtIfUISAz4aAAZ+AEZvIsKeCABqCAAmbwzs6rrStQ10kEyAB2Z8A2IIACEWFkyhwZRjSlNzSxt7JxdgiC8uEbGJ/OxfP3hV9e4ivcoD9zXQiKjpPkDVgCNbwMD4O0gnrDSQZFM5cW6AmcdmAeHgCRuAEIHjhkp1mmAdEgBrsUVgXN9ev1kGAskC1ABiEAOLIQADaRQANBBStT6tSAMzUgAs1IArNSAGzUgDs1IAHABdWhWKA9dJZRFqRAsRAiFhWHpCLBQB6ZZzwyVaJF6HxoowmbC0B7zADyyGQ1lsjmc01cFyOPju9pCEOiXGdlFFWBEaUk1LdEAA7nYvp7+FTLjRaZcNpUXvwvHV6RBABfkHmpqbS1I8gEvyXNNWo0wnmYCiZwUym0+lM1kc7l8oUisUS7La6Wy+WK5Wq9UQTVt7W6NF4XLo6Z8RDGs2WxY2lYO7wGU4uyTPF4SWgiKBAgTm8NnOfLCcJ+4XCQ6D2nl7wC/G7osIMII+29irx3LvBEA8vZc/86eBUK6vKsF7rted7bru+7Xq8L4GrBLygUOV6ITeF5aLEYj3pkj7Ptax5vocS67F+P7Xn+aFBIucbAaeAGXIGGxurQ9S0KUWEiLCJYgGWIgVlS1aUrWlL1pSjbCqK4oItqQA"\))
The structural recursion analysis attempts to translate the recursive [pre-definition](Elaboration-and-Compilation/#--tech-term-pre-definition) into a use of the appropriate structural recursion constructions. At this step, pattern matching has already been translated into the use of matcher functions; these are treated specially by the termination checker. Next, for each group of parameters, a translation using `brecOn` is attempted.
Course-of-Values Tables
This definition is equivalent to `List.below`:
`def List.below' {α : Type u} {motive : [List](Basic-Types/Linked-Lists/#List___nil "Documentation for List") α → Sort u} :     [List](Basic-Types/Linked-Lists/#List___nil "Documentation for List") α → Sort (max (u + 1) u)   | [] => [PUnit](Basic-Types/The-Unit-Type/#PUnit___unit "Documentation for PUnit")   | _ :: xs => motive xs ×' xs.[below'](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#List___below___-_LPAR_in-Course-of-Values-Tables_RPAR_ "Definition of example") (motive := motive) `
In other words, for a given [motive](The-Type-System/Inductive-Types/#--tech-term-motive), `[List.below'](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#List___below___-_LPAR_in-Course-of-Values-Tables_RPAR_ "Definition of example")` is a type that contains a realization of the motive for all suffixes of the list.
More recursive arguments require further nested iterations of the product type. For instance, binary trees have two recursive occurrences.
`inductive Tree (α : Type u) : Type u where   | leaf   | branch (left : [Tree](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#Tree-_LPAR_in-Course-of-Values-Tables_RPAR_ "Definition of example") α) (val : α) (right : [Tree](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#Tree-_LPAR_in-Course-of-Values-Tables_RPAR_ "Definition of example") α) `
Its corresponding course-of-values table contains the realizations of the motive for all subtrees:
`def Tree.below' {α : Type u} {motive : [Tree](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#Tree-_LPAR_in-Course-of-Values-Tables_RPAR_ "Definition of example") α → Sort u} :     [Tree](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#Tree-_LPAR_in-Course-of-Values-Tables_RPAR_ "Definition of example") α → Sort (max (u + 1) u)   | [.leaf](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#Tree___leaf-_LPAR_in-Course-of-Values-Tables_RPAR_ "Definition of example") => [PUnit](Basic-Types/The-Unit-Type/#PUnit___unit "Documentation for PUnit")   | [.branch](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#Tree___branch-_LPAR_in-Course-of-Values-Tables_RPAR_ "Definition of example") left _val right =>     (motive left ×' left.[below'](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#Tree___below___-_LPAR_in-Course-of-Values-Tables_RPAR_ "Definition of example") (motive := motive)) ×'     (motive right ×' right.[below'](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#Tree___below___-_LPAR_in-Course-of-Values-Tables_RPAR_ "Definition of example") (motive := motive)) `
For both lists and trees, the `brecOn` operator expects just a single case, rather than one per constructor. This case accepts a list or tree along with a table of results for all smaller values; from this, it should satisfy the motive for the provided value. Dependent case analysis of the provided value automatically refines the type of the memo table, providing everything needed.
The following definitions are equivalent to `List.brecOn` and `Tree.brecOn`, respectively. The primitive recursive helpers `[List.brecOnTable](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#List___brecOnTable-_LPAR_in-Course-of-Values-Tables_RPAR_ "Definition of example")` and `[Tree.brecOnTable](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#Tree___brecOnTable-_LPAR_in-Course-of-Values-Tables_RPAR_ "Definition of example")` compute the course-of-values tables along with the final results, and the actual definitions of the `brecOn` operators simply project out the result.
`def List.brecOnTable {α : Type u}     {motive : [List](Basic-Types/Linked-Lists/#List___nil "Documentation for List") α → Sort u}     (xs : [List](Basic-Types/Linked-Lists/#List___nil "Documentation for List") α)     (step :       (ys : [List](Basic-Types/Linked-Lists/#List___nil "Documentation for List") α) → xs.[below'](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#List___below___-_LPAR_in-Course-of-Values-Tables_RPAR_ "Definition of example") (motive := motive) := [PUnit.unit](Basic-Types/The-Unit-Type/#PUnit___unit "Documentation for PUnit.unit"), [PUnit.unit](Basic-Types/The-Unit-Type/#PUnit___unit "Documentation for PUnit.unit")⟩   | x :: xs =>     let res := xs.[brecOnTable](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#List___brecOnTable-_LPAR_in-Course-of-Values-Tables_RPAR_ "Definition of example") (motive := motive) step     let val := step (x :: xs) res [.leaf](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#Tree___leaf-_LPAR_in-Course-of-Values-Tables_RPAR_ "Definition of example") => ⟨step [.leaf](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#Tree___leaf-_LPAR_in-Course-of-Values-Tables_RPAR_ "Definition of example") [PUnit.unit](Basic-Types/The-Unit-Type/#PUnit___unit "Documentation for ``def List.brecOn' {α : Type u}     {motive : [List](Basic-Types/Linked-Lists/#List___nil "Documentation for List") α → Sort u}     (xs : [List](Basic-Types/Linked-Lists/#List___nil "Documentation for (t.[brecOnTable](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#Tree___brecOnTable-_LPAR_in-Course-of-Values-Tables_RPAR_ "Definition of example") (motive := motive) step).1 `
[Live ↪](javascript:openLiveLink\("CYUwZgBAMglgzgFwHQCMQBsD2B3A5BAb0EbgCALggBUBPABxAgFcBfQgW0wRgDd7zZEIJQEmEEAMqYATgkYtSAKAiLo8acLGTpAClYBDAB4RNDCAGoIARgCUjSwogAfCAG0AuhAC8APggAFAKoAdjAIdo4A+mTkenAe3uycPBDREADr+NGoGDj42hzcvO4Q8fm2cggAFiCSIKzKiJlY2GEgAI5haI345AAC/MgdOB4QvSoN2WSFKFR2YAwBIHqqRXmJ0XYwAcAMAMacmAFJMQA8ANzecDCsNM4DeC522/sA5hJychtbu/mUEiD0miRyNQ6DYyJRaPRjNhKr9QhB0CAdGA4SgJDoAttyoYEWBpEDfvQiNZNFwdOgwUTDBIYE9ynifn9BKVQJAKASxnhCIDwSDmGwVrwGYSICJxFIZGQ7Io2Yy1GKtLoDEZTBZrAxbIpHEgEUjYr5AsE4ag0RisTjpGFSeTqbTpF4pYZiolzal8OaOTknQVlgkQJZrGkHblfRAbXTXaGaXSPY6BRMfSVShUqr9ajKQBzmm1bl1humOUNuvmc/GpjM5gsll6ICFFB8dnsDrWIPNFrEHRcrs5i1k7nZW9IYOVyUOJO2lBBO9cnD3OgAaCBD9AL0f3OQsur9X7bADyAQoOhQCK5YOBkKYDoI1b4KkEIvU4uYQeSN4ERKDiBA13kE8UmioMSvqo1hCA6igATGwbfKQhReiBYEJokAHWD+SjVskaSHJB16wQKKHuHYugIJihwQNgwTlHCrh6oAF+SftObj+EEyBzMEC5McESCsQggCX5HCBikFEMT2hOCLSL8gGFBkqIgLu+6HseUGJDBiF+pOCBfg6YkQFa8b0YYAlCdYEkOjRVoLhJfHruAQrGrJe4Hke9DEKeEIyJe15CneooaO5E6aPS6ZMh+Gnfgh/6AV5lKgb+EAQSWSnenBIoIdWyGShO1bSJh/S9p6cYqclMGEToxFYtI5EVEaOqQF4EB0aFEDaoikAcSxzHsQa7XBHxmpNai6IkS6ulhnanhaSA4kgHAUDgHihTujJcmOYpOGqdY9ETVNcAAEpRvNka2nZy0Kf8a3JZtomTRAA2mjt03xjREmzbiFnTXttq9Uo2m6Sp+maMag1mnNOlkoddLWLdmL3XApnmTdJrQ9NVkbn0x17vgLlAm5T4TleBWbt5D7SLjSiaC+hPvv5+mof5AFgn0TIpbF8V5bGIaFXhzO/mlcAoQ66GSXY5NwOj8lOez0G4b6G2hZYSDmG8G7FtuGMntjvIXnjnlBXKvmk3+gUEsF1ONbTZP0/isrwSzosJedXMxTzcbpebWUTMLW72eLq0FdLJTqV+8vmEAA"\))
The `below` construction is a mapping from each value of a type to the results of some function call on _all_ smaller values; it can be understood as a memoization table that already contains the results for all smaller values. The notion of “smaller value” that is expressed in the `below` construction corresponds directly to the definition of [strict sub-terms](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#--tech-term-strict-sub-term).
Recursors expect an argument for each of the inductive type's constructors; these arguments are called with the constructor's arguments (and the result of recursion on recursive parameters) during [ι-reduction](The-Type-System/Inductive-Types/#--tech-term-___-reduction). The course-of-values recursion operator `brecOn`, on the other hand, expects just a single case that covers all constructors at once. This case is provided with a value and a `below` table that contains the results of recursion on all values smaller than the given value; it should use the contents of the table to satisfy the motive for the provided value. If the function is structurally recursive over a given parameter (or parameter group), then the results of all recursive calls will be present in this table already.
When the body of the recursive function is transformed into an invocation of `brecOn` on one of the function's parameters, the parameter and its course-of-values table are in scope. The analysis traverses the body of the function, looking for recursive calls. If the parameter is matched against, then its occurrences in the local context are [generalized](Terms/Pattern-Matching/#match-generalization) and then instantiated with the pattern; this is also true for the type of the course-of-values table. Typically, this pattern matching results in the type of the course-of-values table becoming more specific, which gives access to the recursive results for smaller values. This generalization process implements the rule that patterns are [sub-terms](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#--tech-term-strict-sub-term) of match discriminants. When an recursive occurrence of the function is detected, the course-of-values table is consulted to see whether it contains a result for the argument being checked. If so, the recursive call can be replaced with a projection from the table. If not, then the parameter in question doesn't support structural recursion.
Elaboration Walkthrough
The first step in walking through the elaboration of `half` is to manually desugar it to a simpler form. This doesn't match the way Lean works, but its output is much easier to read when there are fewer `[OfNat](Terms/Numeric-Literals/#OfNat___mk "Documentation for OfNat")` instances present. This readable definition:
`def half : [Nat](Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat") → [Nat](Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat")   | 0 | 1 => 0   | n + 2 => half n + 1 `
can be rewritten to this somewhat lower-level version:
