The final case contains a recursive call. It should be translated into a lookup into the course-of-values table. A more readable representation of the last hole's type is:
`(n : [Nat](Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat")) → Nat.below (motive := fun _ => [Nat](Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat")) n.[succ](Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat.succ").[succ](Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat.succ") → [Nat](Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat")`
which is equivalent to
`(n : [Nat](Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat")) → [Nat](Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat") ×' ([Nat](Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat") ×' Nat.below (motive := fun _ => [Nat](Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat")) n) → [Nat](Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat")`
The first `[Nat](Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat")` in the course-of-values table is the result of recursion on `n + 1`, and the second is the result of recursion on `n`. The recursive call can thus be replaced by a lookup, and the elaboration is successful:
`noncomputable def half'' : [Nat](Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat") → [Nat](Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat") :=   fun (x : [Nat](Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat")) =>     x.brecOn fun n table =>       (half.match_1         (motive :=           fun k =>             k.below (motive := fun _ => [Nat](Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat")) →             [Nat](Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat"))         n         (fun () _ => [.zero](Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat.zero"))         (fun () _ => [.zero](Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat.zero"))         (fun _ table => [Nat.succ](Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat.succ") table.2.1)       table `unexpected end of input; expected ')', ',' or ':'``
The actual elaborator keeps track of the relationship between the parameter being checked for structural recursion and the positions in the course-of-values tables by inserting sentinel types with fresh names into the motive.

##  7.6.3. Well-Founded Recursion[🔗](find/?domain=Verso.Genre.Manual.section&name=well-founded-recursion "Permalink")
Functions defined by _well-founded recursion_ are those in which each recursive call has arguments that are _smaller_ (in a [suitable sense](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#wf-rel)) than the functions' parameters. In contrast to [structural recursion](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#structural-recursion), in which recursive definitions must satisfy particular _syntactic_ requirements, definitions that use well-founded recursion employ _semantic_ arguments. This allows a larger class of recursive definitions to be accepted. Furthermore, when Lean's automation fails to construct a termination proof, it is possible to specify one manually.
All definitions are treated identically by the Lean compiler. In Lean's logic, definitions that use well-founded recursion typically do not reduce [definitionally](The-Type-System/#--tech-term-definitional-equality). The reductions do hold as propositional equalities, however, and Lean automatically proves them. This does not typically make it more difficult to prove properties of definitions that use well-founded recursion, because the propositional reductions can be used to reason about the behavior of the function. It does mean, however, that using these functions in types typically does not work well. Even when the reduction behavior happens to hold definitionally, it is often much slower than structurally recursive definitions in the kernel, which must unfold the termination proof along with the definition. When possible, recursive function that are intended for use in types or in other situations where definitional equality is important should be defined with structural recursion.
To explicitly use well-founded recursion, a function or theorem definition can be annotated with a ``Lean.Parser.Command.declaration : command```termination_by` clause that specifies the _measure_ by which the function terminates. The measure should be a term that decreases at each recursive call; it may be one of the function's parameters or a tuple of the parameters, but it may also be any other term. The measure's type must be equipped with a [well-founded relation](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#--tech-term-well-founded-relation), which determines what it means for the measure to decrease.
syntaxExplicit Well-Founded Recursion
The ``Lean.Parser.Command.declaration : command```termination_by` clause introduces the termination argument.

```



Specify a termination measure for recursive functions.


```
termination_by a - b

```

indicates that termination of the currently defined recursive function follows because the difference between the arguments `a` and `b` decreases.
If the function takes further argument after the colon, you can name them as follows:

```
def example (a : Nat) : Nat → Nat → Nat :=
termination_by b c => a - b

```

By default, a `termination_by` clause will cause the function to be constructed using well-founded recursion. The syntax `termination_by structural a` (or `termination_by structural _ c => c`) indicates the function is expected to be structural recursive on the argument. In this case the body of the `termination_by` clause must be one of the function's parameters.
If omitted, a termination measure will be inferred. If written as `termination_by?`, the inferred termination measure will be suggested.
`terminationBy ::= ... | `
 
Specify a termination measure for recursive functions.
 
```
termination_by a - b

```
 
indicates that termination of the currently defined recursive function follows because the difference between the arguments `a` and `b` decreases.
If the function takes further argument after the colon, you can name them as follows:

```
def example (a : Nat) : Nat → Nat → Nat :=
termination_by b c => a - b

```

By default, a `termination_by` clause will cause the function to be constructed using well-founded recursion. The syntax `termination_by structural a` (or `termination_by structural _ c => c`) indicates the function is expected to be structural recursive on the argument. In this case the body of the `termination_by` clause must be one of the function's parameters.
If omitted, a termination measure will be inferred. If written as `termination_by?`, the inferred termination measure will be suggested.
`termination_by (ident* =>)? term
```

The identifiers before the optional `=>` can bring function parameters into scope that are not already bound in the declaration header, and the mandatory term must indicate one of the function's parameters, whether introduced in the header or locally in the clause.
Division by Iterated Subtraction
Division can be specified as the number of times the divisor can be subtracted from the dividend. This operation cannot be elaborated using structural recursion because subtraction is not pattern matching. The value of `n` does decrease with each recursive call, so well-founded recursion can be used to justify the definition of division by iterated subtraction.
`def div (n k : [Nat](Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat")) : [Nat](Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat") :=   [if](Terms/Conditionals/#termIfThenElse "Documentation for syntax") k = 0 [then](Terms/Conditionals/#termIfThenElse "Documentation for syntax") 0   [else](Terms/Conditionals/#termIfThenElse "Documentation for syntax") [if](Terms/Conditionals/#termIfThenElse "Documentation for syntax") k > n [then](Terms/Conditionals/#termIfThenElse "Documentation for syntax") 0   [else](Terms/Conditionals/#termIfThenElse "Documentation for syntax") 1 + [div](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#div-_LPAR_in-Division-by-Iterated-Subtraction_RPAR_ "Definition of example") (n - k) k termination_by n `

###  7.6.3.1. Well-Founded Relations[🔗](find/?domain=Verso.Genre.Manual.section&name=wf-rel "Permalink")
A relation `≺` is a _well-founded relation_ if there exists no infinitely descending chain
`x0≻x1≻⋯ x_0 ≻ x_1 ≻ \cdotsx0​≻x1​≻⋯`
In Lean, types that are equipped with a canonical well-founded relation are instances of the `[WellFoundedRelation](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#WellFoundedRelation___mk "Documentation for WellFoundedRelation")` type class.
[🔗](find/?domain=Verso.Genre.Manual.doc&name=WellFoundedRelation.wf "Permalink")type class
```


WellFoundedRelation.{u} (α : Sort u) : Sort (max 1 u)


WellFoundedRelation.{u} (α : Sort u) :
  Sort (max 1 u)


```

A type that has a standard well-founded relation.
Instances are used to prove that functions terminate using well-founded recursion by showing that recursive calls reduce some measure according to a well-founded relation. This relation can combine well-founded relations on the recursive function's parameters.
#  Instance Constructor

```
[WellFoundedRelation.mk](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#WellFoundedRelation___mk "Documentation for WellFoundedRelation.mk").{u}
```

#  Methods

```
rel : α → α → Prop
```

A well-founded relation on `α`.

```
wf : [WellFounded](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#WellFounded___intro "Documentation for WellFounded") [WellFoundedRelation.rel](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#WellFoundedRelation___mk "Documentation for WellFoundedRelation.rel")
```

A proof that `rel` is, in fact, well-founded.
The most important instances are:
  * `[Nat](Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat")`, ordered by `(· < ·)`.
  * `[Prod](Basic-Types/Tuples/#Prod___mk "Documentation for Prod")`, ordered lexicographically: `(a₁, b₁) ≺ (a₂, b₂)` if and only if `a₁ ≺ a₂` or `a₁ = a₂` and `b₁ ≺ b₂`.
  * Every type that is an instance of the `[SizeOf](The-Type-System/Inductive-Types/#SizeOf___mk "Documentation for SizeOf")` type class, which provides a method `[SizeOf.sizeOf](The-Type-System/Inductive-Types/#SizeOf___mk "Documentation for SizeOf.sizeOf")`, has a well-founded relation. For these types, `x₁ ≺ x₂` if and only if `[sizeOf](The-Type-System/Inductive-Types/#SizeOf___mk "Documentation for SizeOf.sizeOf") x₁ < [sizeOf](The-Type-System/Inductive-Types/#SizeOf___mk "Documentation for SizeOf.sizeOf") x₂`. For [inductive types](The-Type-System/Inductive-Types/#--tech-term-Inductive-types), a `[SizeOf](The-Type-System/Inductive-Types/#SizeOf___mk "Documentation for SizeOf")` instance is automatically derived by Lean.


Note that there exists a low-priority instance `instSizeOfDefault` that provides a `[SizeOf](The-Type-System/Inductive-Types/#SizeOf___mk "Documentation for SizeOf")` instance for any type, and always returns `0`. This instance cannot be used to prove that a function terminates using well-founded recursion because `0 < 0` is false.
Default Size Instance
Function types in general do not have a well-founded relation that's useful for termination proofs. [Instance synthesis](Type-Classes/Instance-Synthesis/#instance-synth) thus selects `instSizeOfDefault` and the corresponding well-founded relation. If the measure is a function, the default `[SizeOf](The-Type-System/Inductive-Types/#SizeOf___mk "Documentation for SizeOf")` instance is selected and the proof cannot succeed.
`def `declaration uses `sorry``fooInst (b : [Bool](Basic-Types/Booleans/#Bool___false "Documentation for Bool") → [Bool](Basic-Types/Booleans/#Bool___false "Documentation for Bool")) : [Unit](Basic-Types/The-Unit-Type/#Unit "Documentation for Unit") := [fooInst](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#fooInst-_LPAR_in-Default-Size-Instance_RPAR_ "Definition of example") (b ∘ b) ###  7.6.3.2. Termination proofs[🔗](find/?domain=Verso.Genre.Manual.section&name=The-Lean-Language-Reference--Definitions--Recursive-Definitions--Well-Founded-Recursion--Termination-proofs "Permalink")
Once a [measure](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#--tech-term-measure) is specified and its [well-founded relation](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#--tech-term-well-founded-relation) is determined, Lean determines the termination proof obligation for every recursive call.
The proof obligation for each recursive call is of the form `g a₁ a₂ … ≺ g p₁ p₂ …`, where:
  * `g` is the measure as a function of the parameters,
  * `[≺](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#WellFoundedRelation___mk "Documentation for WellFoundedRelation.rel")` is the inferred well-founded relation,
  * `a₁` `a₂` `…` are the arguments of the recursive call and
  * `p₁` `p₂` `…` are the parameters of the function definition.


The context of the proof obligation is the local context of the recursive call. In particular, local assumptions (such as those introduced by `if h : _`, `match h : _ with ` or `have`) are available. If a function parameter is the [discriminant](Terms/Pattern-Matching/#--tech-term-match-discriminants) of a pattern match (e.g. by a ``Lean.Parser.Term.match : term`
Pattern matching. `match e, ... with | p, ... => f | ...` matches each given term `e` against each pattern `p` of a match alternative. When all patterns of an alternative match, the `match` term evaluates to the value of the corresponding right-hand side `f` with the pattern variables bound to the respective matched values. If used as `match h : e, ... with | p, ... => f | ...`, `h : e = p` is available within `f`.
When not constructing a proof, `match` does not automatically substitute variables matched on in dependent variables' types. Use `match (generalizing := true) ...` to enforce this.
Syntax quotations can also be used in a pattern match. This matches a `Syntax` value against quotations, pattern variables, or `_`.
Quoted identifiers only match identical identifiers - custom matching such as by the preresolved names only should be done explicitly.
`Syntax.atom`s are ignored during matching by default except when part of a built-in literal. For users introducing new atoms, we recommend wrapping them in dedicated syntax kinds if they should participate in matching. For example, in

```
syntax "c" ("foo" <|> "bar") ...

```

`foo` and `bar` are indistinguishable during matching, but in

```
syntax foo := "foo"
syntax "c" (foo <|> "bar") ...

```

they are not.
`[`match`](Terms/Pattern-Matching/#Lean___Parser___Term___match) expression), then this parameter is refined to the matched pattern in the proof obligation.
The overall termination proof obligation consists of one goal for each recursive call. By default, the tactic `[decreasing_trivial](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#decreasing_trivial "Documentation for tactic")` is used to prove each proof obligation. A custom tactic script can be provided using the optional ``Lean.Parser.Command.declaration : command```decreasing_by` clause, which comes after the ``Lean.Parser.Command.declaration : command```termination_by` clause. This tactic script is run once, with one goal for each proof obligation, rather than separately on each proof obligation.
Termination Proof Obligations
The following recursive definition of the Fibonacci numbers has two recursive calls, which results in two goals in the termination proof.
`def fib (n : [Nat](Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat")) :=   [if](Terms/Conditionals/#termDepIfThenElse "Documentation for syntax") h : n ≤ 1 [then](Terms/Conditionals/#termDepIfThenElse "Documentation for syntax")     1   [else](Terms/Conditionals/#termDepIfThenElse "Documentation for syntax")     fib (n - 1) + fib (n - 2) termination_by n `unsolved goals n:[Nat](Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat")h:[¬](Basic-Propositions/Logical-Connectives/#Not "Documentation for Not")n [≤](Type-Classes/Basic-Classes/#LE___mk "Documentation for LE.le") 1⊢ n [-](Type-Classes/Basic-Classes/#HSub___mk "Documentation for HSub.hSub") 1 [<](Type-Classes/Basic-Classes/#LT___mk "Documentation for LT.lt") n  n:[Nat](Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat")h:[¬](Basic-Propositions/Logical-Connectives/#Not "Documentation for Not")n [≤](Type-Classes/Basic-Classes/#LE___mk "Documentation for LE.le") 1⊢ n [-](Type-Classes/Basic-Classes/#HSub___mk "Documentation for HSub.hSub") 2 [<](Type-Classes/Basic-Classes/#LT___mk "Documentation for LT.lt") n`decreasing_by [skip](Tactic-Proofs/Tactic-Reference/#skip "Documentation for tactic")n:[Nat](Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat")h:[¬](Basic-Propositions/Logical-Connectives/#Not "Documentation for Not")n [≤](Type-Classes/Basic-Classes/#LE___mk "Documentation for LE.le") 1⊢ n [-](Type-Classes/Basic-Classes/#HSub___mk "Documentation for HSub.hSub") 1 [<](Type-Classes/Basic-Classes/#LT___mk "Documentation for LT.lt") nn:[Nat](Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat")h:[¬](Basic-Propositions/Logical-Connectives/#Not "Documentation for Not")n [≤](Type-Classes/Basic-Classes/#LE___mk "Documentation for LE.le") 1⊢ n [-](Type-Classes/Basic-Classes/#HSub___mk "Documentation for HSub.hSub") 2 [<](Type-Classes/Basic-Classes/#LT___mk "Documentation for LT.lt") n `
n:[Nat](Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat")h:[¬](Basic-Propositions/Logical-Connectives/#Not "Documentation for Not")n [≤](Type-Classes/Basic-Classes/#LE___mk "Documentation for LE.le") 1⊢ n [-](Type-Classes/Basic-Classes/#HSub___mk "Documentation for HSub.hSub") 1 [<](Type-Classes/Basic-Classes/#LT___mk "Documentation for LT.lt") nn:[Nat](Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat")h:[¬](Basic-Propositions/Logical-Connectives/#Not "Documentation for Not")n [≤](Type-Classes/Basic-Classes/#LE___mk "Documentation for LE.le") 1⊢ n [-](Type-Classes/Basic-Classes/#HSub___mk "Documentation for HSub.hSub") 2 [<](Type-Classes/Basic-Classes/#LT___mk "Documentation for LT.lt") n
Here, the [measure](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#--tech-term-measure) is simply the parameter itself, and the well-founded order is the less-than relation on natural numbers. The first proof goal requires the user to prove that the argument of the first recursive call, namely `n - 1`, is strictly smaller than the function's parameter, `n`.
Both termination proofs can be easily discharged using the `[omega](Tactic-Proofs/Tactic-Reference/#omega "Documentation for tactic")` tactic.
`def fib (n : [Nat](Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat")) :=   [if](Terms/Conditionals/#termDepIfThenElse "Documentation for syntax") h : n ≤ 1 [then](Terms/Conditionals/#termDepIfThenElse "Documentation for syntax")     1   [else](Terms/Conditionals/#termDepIfThenElse "Documentation for syntax")     fib (n - 1) + fib (n - 2) termination_by n decreasing_by   ·n:[Nat](Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat")h:[¬](Basic-Propositions/Logical-Connectives/#Not "Documentation for Not")n [≤](Type-Classes/Basic-Classes/#LE___mk "Documentation for LE.le") 1⊢ n [-](Type-Classes/Basic-Classes/#HSub___mk "Documentation for HSub.hSub") 1 [<](Type-Classes/Basic-Classes/#LT___mk "Documentation for LT.lt") n [omega](Tactic-Proofs/Tactic-Reference/#omega "Documentation for tactic")All goals completed! 🐙   ·n:[Nat](Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat")h:[¬](Basic-Propositions/Logical-Connectives/#Not "Documentation for Not")n [≤](Type-Classes/Basic-Classes/#LE___mk "Documentation for LE.le") 1⊢ n [-](Type-Classes/Basic-Classes/#HSub___mk "Documentation for HSub.hSub") 2 [<](Type-Classes/Basic-Classes/#LT___mk "Documentation for LT.lt") n [omega](Tactic-Proofs/Tactic-Reference/#omega "Documentation for tactic")All goals completed! 🐙 `
Refined Parameters
If a parameter of the function is the [discriminant](Terms/Pattern-Matching/#--tech-term-match-discriminants) of a pattern match, then the proof obligations mention the refined parameter.
`def fib : [Nat](Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat") → [Nat](Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat")   | 0 | 1 => 1   | n:[Nat](Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat")⊢ n [+](Type-Classes/Basic-Classes/#HAdd___mk "Documentation for HAdd.hAdd") 1 [<](Type-Classes/Basic-Classes/#LT___mk "Documentation for LT.lt") n.[succ](Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat.succ").[succ](Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat.succ")n:[Nat](Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat")⊢ n [<](Type-Classes/Basic-Classes/#LT___mk "Documentation for LT.lt") n.[succ](Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat.succ").[succ](Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat.succ")
Additionally, the context is enriched with additional assumptions that can make it easier to prove termination. Some examples include:
  * In the branches of an [if-then-else](Terms/Conditionals/#if-then-else) expression, a hypothesis that asserts the current branch's condition is added, much as if the dependent if-then-else syntax had been used.
  * In the function argument to certain higher-order functions, the context of the function's body is enriched with assumptions about the argument.


This list is not exhaustive, and the mechanism is extensible. It is described in detail in [the section on preprocessing](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#well-founded-preprocessing).
Enriched Proof Obligation Contexts
Here, the ``termIfThenElse : term`
`[`if`](Terms/Conditionals/#termIfThenElse) does not add a local assumption about the condition (that is, whether `n ≤ 1`) to the local contexts in the branches.
`def fib (n : [Nat](Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat")) :=   [if](Terms/Conditionals/#termIfThenElse "Documentation for syntax") n ≤ 1 [then](Terms/Conditionals/#termIfThenElse "Documentation for syntax")     1   [else](Terms/Conditionals/#termIfThenElse "Documentation for syntax")     [fib](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#fib-_LPAR_in-Enriched-Proof-Obligation-Contexts_RPAR_ "Definition of example") (n - 1) + [fib](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#fib-_LPAR_in-Enriched-Proof-Obligation-Contexts_RPAR_ "Definition of example") (n - 2) termination_by n `unsolved goals n:[Nat](Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat")h✝:[¬](Basic-Propositions/Logical-Connectives/#Not "Documentation for Not")n [≤](Type-Classes/Basic-Classes/#LE___mk "Documentation for LE.le") 1⊢ n [-](Type-Classes/Basic-Classes/#HSub___mk "Documentation for HSub.hSub") 1 [<](Type-Classes/Basic-Classes/#LT___mk "Documentation for LT.lt") n  n:[Nat](Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat")h✝:[¬](Basic-Propositions/Logical-Connectives/#Not "Documentation for Not")n [≤](Type-Classes/Basic-Classes/#LE___mk "Documentation for LE.le") 1⊢ n [-](Type-Classes/Basic-Classes/#HSub___mk "Documentation for HSub.hSub") 2 [<](Type-Classes/Basic-Classes/#LT___mk "Documentation for LT.lt") n`decreasing_by [skip](Tactic-Proofs/Tactic-Reference/#skip "Documentation for tactic")n:[Nat](Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat")h✝:[¬](Basic-Propositions/Logical-Connectives/#Not "Documentation for Not")n [≤](Type-Classes/Basic-Classes/#LE___mk "Documentation for LE.le") 1⊢ n [-](Type-Classes/Basic-Classes/#HSub___mk "Documentation for HSub.hSub") 1 [<](Type-Classes/Basic-Classes/#LT___mk "Documentation for LT.lt") nn:[Nat](Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat")h✝:[¬](Basic-Propositions/Logical-Connectives/#Not "Documentation for Not")n [≤](Type-Classes/Basic-Classes/#LE___mk "Documentation for LE.le") 1⊢ n [-](Type-Classes/Basic-Classes/#HSub___mk "Documentation for HSub.hSub") 2 [<](Type-Classes/Basic-Classes/#LT___mk "Documentation for LT.lt") n `

Similarly, in the following (contrived) example, the termination proof contains an additional assumption showing that `x ∈ xs`.
`def f (n : [Nat](Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat")) (xs : [List](Basic-Types/Linked-Lists/#List___nil "Documentation for List") [Nat](Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat")) : [Nat](Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat") :=   [List.sum](Basic-Types/Linked-Lists/#List___sum "Documentation for List.sum") (xs.[map](Basic-Types/Linked-Lists/#List___map "Documentation for List.map") (fun x => f x [])) termination_by xs `unsolved goals n:[Nat](Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat")xs:[List](Basic-Types/Linked-Lists/#List___nil "Documentation for List") [Nat](Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat")x:[Nat](Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat")h✝:x ∈ xs⊢ [sizeOf](The-Type-System/Inductive-Types/#SizeOf___mk "Documentation for SizeOf.sizeOf") [[](Basic-Types/Linked-Lists/#List___nil "Documentation for List.nil")[]](Basic-Types/Linked-Lists/#List___nil "Documentation for List.nil") [<](Type-Classes/Basic-Classes/#LT___mk "Documentation for LT.lt") [sizeOf](The-Type-System/Inductive-Types/#SizeOf___mk "Documentation for SizeOf.sizeOf") xs`decreasing_by [skip](Tactic-Proofs/Tactic-Reference/#skip "Documentation for tactic")n:[Nat](Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat")xs:[List](Basic-Types/Linked-Lists/#List___nil "Documentation for List") [Nat](Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat")x:[Nat](Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat")h✝:x ∈ xs⊢ [sizeOf](The-Type-System/Inductive-Types/#SizeOf___mk "Documentation for SizeOf.sizeOf") [[](Basic-Types/Linked-Lists/#List___nil "Documentation for List.nil")[]](Basic-Types/Linked-Lists/#List___nil "Documentation for List.nil") [<](Type-Classes/Basic-Classes/#LT___mk "Documentation for LT.lt") [sizeOf](The-Type-System/Inductive-Types/#SizeOf___mk "Documentation for SizeOf.sizeOf") xs `

###  7.6.3.3. Default Termination Proof Tactic[🔗](find/?domain=Verso.Genre.Manual.section&name=The-Lean-Language-Reference--Definitions--Recursive-Definitions--Well-Founded-Recursion--Default-Termination-Proof-Tactic "Permalink")
If no ``Lean.Parser.Command.declaration : command```decreasing_by` clause is given, then the `[decreasing_tactic](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#decreasing_tactic "Documentation for tactic")` is used implicitly, and applied to each proof obligation separately.
[🔗](find/?domain=Verso.Genre.Manual.doc.tactic&name=tacticDecreasing_tactic "Permalink")tactic
```
[decreasing_tactic](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#decreasing_tactic "Documentation for tactic")
```

The tactic `[decreasing_tactic](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#decreasing_tactic "Documentation for tactic")` mainly deals with lexicographic ordering of tuples, applying `Prod.Lex.right` if the left components of the product are [definitionally equal](The-Type-System/#--tech-term-definitional-equality), and `Prod.Lex.left` otherwise. After preprocessing tuples this way, it calls the `[decreasing_trivial](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#decreasing_trivial "Documentation for tactic")` tactic.
[🔗](find/?domain=Verso.Genre.Manual.doc.tactic&name=tacticDecreasing_trivial "Permalink")tactic
```
[decreasing_trivial](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#decreasing_trivial "Documentation for tactic")
```

Extensible helper tactic for `[decreasing_tactic](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#decreasing_tactic "Documentation for tactic")`. This handles the "base case" reasoning after applying lexicographic order lemmas. It can be extended by adding more macro definitions, e.g.

```
macro_rules | `(tactic| decreasing_trivial) => `(tactic| linarith)

```

The tactic `[decreasing_trivial](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#decreasing_trivial "Documentation for tactic")` is an extensible tactic that applies a few common heuristics to solve a termination goal. In particular, it tries the following tactics and theorems:
  * `[simp_arith](Tactic-Proofs/Tactic-Reference/#simp_arith "Documentation for tactic")`
  * `[assumption](Tactic-Proofs/Tactic-Reference/#assumption "Documentation for tactic")`
  * theorems `Nat.sub_succ_lt_self`, `Nat.pred_lt_of_lt`, and `Nat.pred_lt`, which handle common arithmetic goals
  * `[omega](Tactic-Proofs/Tactic-Reference/#omega "Documentation for tactic")`
  * `array_get_dec` and `array_mem_dec`, which prove that the size of array elements is less than the size of the array
  * `sizeOf_list_dec` that the size of list elements is less than the size of the list
  * `String.Legacy.Iterator.sizeOf_next_lt_of_hasNext` and `String.Legacy.Iterator.sizeOf_next_lt_of_atEnd`, to handle iteration through a string using ``Lean.Parser.Term.doFor : doElem`
`for x in e do s` iterates over `e` assuming `e`'s type has an instance of the `ForIn` typeclass. `break` and `continue` are supported inside `for` loops. `for x in e, x2 in e2, ... do s` iterates of the given collections in parallel, until at least one of them is exhausted. The types of `e2` etc. must implement the `Std.ToStream` typeclass.
``for`


This tactic is intended to be extended with further heuristics using ``Lean.Parser.Command.macro_rules : command``[`macro_rules`](Notations-and-Macros/Macros/#Lean___Parser___Command___macro_rules).
No Backtracking of Lexicographic Order
A classic example of a recursive function that needs a more complex [measure](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#--tech-term-measure) is the Ackermann function:
`def ack : [Nat](Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat") → [Nat](Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat") → [Nat](Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat")   | 0,     n     => n + 1   | m + 1, 0     => [ack](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#ack-_LPAR_in-No-Backtracking-of-Lexicographic-Order_RPAR_ "Definition of example") m 1   | m + 1, n + 1 => [ack](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#ack-_LPAR_in-No-Backtracking-of-Lexicographic-Order_RPAR_ "Definition of example") m ([ack](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#ack-_LPAR_in-No-Backtracking-of-Lexicographic-Order_RPAR_ "Definition of example") (m + 1) n) termination_by m n => (m, n) `
The measure is a tuple, so every recursive call has to be on arguments that are lexicographically smaller than the parameters. The default `[decreasing_tactic](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#decreasing_tactic "Documentation for tactic")` can handle this.
In particular, note that the third recursive call has a second argument that is smaller than the second parameter and a first argument that is definitionally equal to the first parameter. This allowed `[decreasing_tactic](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#decreasing_tactic "Documentation for tactic")` to apply `Prod.Lex.right`.
`Prod.Lex.right {α β} {ra : α → α → Prop} {rb : β → β → Prop}   (a : α) {b₁ b₂ : β}   (h : rb b₁ b₂) :   Prod.Lex ra rb (a, b₁) (a, b₂)`
It fails, however, with the following modified function definition, where the third recursive call's first argument is provably smaller or equal to the first parameter, but not syntactically equal:
`def synack : [Nat](Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat") → [Nat](Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat") → [Nat](Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat")   | 0,     n     => n + 1   | m + 1, 0     => synack m 1   | m + 1, n + 1 => synack m (`failed to prove termination, possible solutions:   - Use `have`-expressions to prove the remaining goals   - Use `termination_by` to specify a different well-founded relation   - Use `decreasing_by` to specify your own tactic for discharging this kind of goal hm n:[Nat](Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat")⊢ m [/](Type-Classes/Basic-Classes/#HDiv___mk "Documentation for HDiv.hDiv") 2 [+](Type-Classes/Basic-Classes/#HAdd___mk "Documentation for HAdd.hAdd") 1 [<](Type-Classes/Basic-Classes/#LT___mk "Documentation for LT.lt") m [+](Type-Classes/Basic-Classes/#HAdd___mk "Documentation for HAdd.hAdd") 1`synack (m / 2 + 1) n) termination_by m n => (m, n) `
```
failed to prove termination, possible solutions:
  - Use `have`-expressions to prove the remaining goals
  - Use `termination_by` to specify a different well-founded relation
  - Use `decreasing_by` to specify your own tactic for discharging this kind of goal
hm n:[Nat](Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat")⊢ m [/](Type-Classes/Basic-Classes/#HDiv___mk "Documentation for HDiv.hDiv") 2 [+](Type-Classes/Basic-Classes/#HAdd___mk "Documentation for HAdd.hAdd") 1 [<](Type-Classes/Basic-Classes/#LT___mk "Documentation for LT.lt") m [+](Type-Classes/Basic-Classes/#HAdd___mk "Documentation for HAdd.hAdd") 1
```

Because `Prod.Lex.right` is not applicable, the tactic used `Prod.Lex.left`, which resulted in the unprovable goal above.
This function definition may require a manual proof that uses the more general theorem `Prod.Lex.right'`, which allows the first component of the tuple (which must be of type `[Nat](Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat")`) to be less or equal instead of strictly equal:
`Prod.Lex.right' {β} (rb : β → β → Prop)   {a₂ : [Nat](Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat")} {b₂ : β} {a₁ : [Nat](Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat")} {b₁ : β}   (h₁ : a₁ ≤ a₂) (h₂ : rb b₁ b₂) :   Prod.Lex [Nat.lt](Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___lt "Documentation for Nat.lt") rb (a₁, b₁) (a₂, b₂)``def synack : [Nat](Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat") → [Nat](Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat") → [Nat](Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat")   | 0, n => n + 1   | m + 1, 0 => synack m 1   | m + 1, n + 1 => synack m (synack (m / 2 + 1) n) termination_by m n => (m, n) decreasing_by The `[decreasing_tactic](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#decreasing_tactic "Documentation for tactic")` tactic does not use the stronger `Prod.Lex.right'` because it would require backtracking on failure.
###  7.6.3.4. Inferring Well-Founded Recursion[🔗](find/?domain=Verso.Genre.Manual.section&name=inferring-well-founded-recursion "Permalink")
If a recursive function definition does not indicate a termination [measure](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#--tech-term-measure), Lean will attempt to discover one automatically. If neither ``Lean.Parser.Command.declaration : command```termination_by` nor ``Lean.Parser.Command.declaration : command```decreasing_by` is provided, Lean will try to [infer structural recursion](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#inferring-structural-recursion) before attempting well-founded recursion. If a ``Lean.Parser.Command.declaration : command```decreasing_by` clause is present, only well-founded recursion is attempted.
To infer a suitable termination [measure](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#--tech-term-measure), Lean considers multiple _basic termination measures_ , which are termination measures of type `[Nat](Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat")`, and then tries all tuples of these measures.
The basic termination measures considered are:
  * all parameters whose type have a non-trivial `[SizeOf](The-Type-System/Inductive-Types/#SizeOf___mk "Documentation for SizeOf")` instance
  * the expression `e₂ - e₁` whenever the local context of a recursive call has an assumption of type `e₁ < e₂` or `e₁ ≤ e₂`, where `e₁` and `e₂` are of type `[Nat](Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat")` and depend only on the function's parameters. This approach is based on work by Panagiotis Manolios and Daron Vroon, 2006. [“Termination Analysis with Calling Context Graphs”](https://doi.org/10.1007/11817963_36). In  _Proceedings of the International Conference on Computer Aided Verification (CAV 2006)._ (LNCS 4144).
  * in a mutual group, an additional basic measure is used to distinguish between recursive calls to other functions in the group and recursive calls to the function being defined (for details, see [the section on mutual well-founded recursion](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#mutual-well-founded-recursion))


_Candidate measures_ are basic measures or tuples of basic measures. If any of the candidate measures allow all proof obligations to be discharged by the termination proof tactic (that is, the tactic specified by ``Lean.Parser.Command.declaration : command```decreasing_by`, or `[decreasing_trivial](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#decreasing_trivial "Documentation for tactic")` if there is no ``Lean.Parser.Command.declaration : command```decreasing_by` clause), then an arbitrary such candidate measure is selected as the automatic termination measure.
A `termination_by?` clause causes the inferred termination annotation to be shown. It can be automatically added to the source file using the offered suggestion or code action.
To avoid the combinatorial explosion of trying all tuples of measures, Lean first tabulates all [basic termination measures](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#--tech-term-basic-termination-measures), determining whether the basic measure is decreasing, strictly decreasing, or non-decreasing. A decreasing measure is smaller for at least one recursive call and never increases at any recursive call, while a strictly decreasing measure is smaller at all recursive calls. A non-decreasing measure is one that the termination tactic could not show to be decreasing or strictly decreasing. A suitable tuple is chosen based on the table.This approach is based on Lukas Bulwahn, Alexander Krauss, and Tobias Nipkow, 2007. [“Finding Lexicographic Orders for Termination Proofs in Isabelle/HOL”](https://doi.org/10.1007/978-3-540-74591-4_5). In  _Proceedings of the International Conference on Theorem Proving in Higher Order Logics (TPHOLS 2007)._ (LNTCS 4732). This table shows up in the error message when no automatic measure could be found.
Termination failure
If there is no ``Lean.Parser.Command.declaration : command```termination_by` clause, Lean attempts to infer a measure for well-founded recursion. If it fails, then it prints the table mentioned above. In this example, the ``Lean.Parser.Command.declaration : command```decreasing_by` clause simply prevents Lean from also attempting structural recursion; this keeps the error message specific.
``Could not find a decreasing measure. The basic measures relate at each recursive call as follows: (<, ≤, =: relation proved, ? all proofs failed, _: no proof attempted)            n m l 1) 32:6-25 = = = 2) 33:6-23 = < _ 3) 34:6-23 < _ _ Please use `termination_by` to specify a decreasing measure.`def f : (n m l : [Nat](Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat")) → [Nat](Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat") | n+1, m+1, l+1 => [ [f](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#f-_LPAR_in-Termination-failure_RPAR_ "Definition of example") (n+1) (m+1) (l+1), [f](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#f-_LPAR_in-Termination-failure_RPAR_ "Definition of example") (n+1) (m-1) (l), [f](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#f-_LPAR_in-Termination-failure_RPAR_ "Definition of example") (n) (m+1) (l) ].[sum](Basic-Types/Linked-Lists/#List___sum "Documentation for List.sum") | _, _, _ => 0 decreasing_by [all_goals](Tactic-Proofs/The-Tactic-Language/#all_goals "Documentation for tactic") [decreasing_tactic](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#decreasing_tactic "Documentation for tactic") `
```
Could not find a decreasing measure.
The basic measures relate at each recursive call as follows:
(<, ≤, =: relation proved, ? all proofs failed, _: no proof attempted)
           n m l
1) 32:6-25 = = =
2) 33:6-23 = < _
3) 34:6-23 < _ _
Please use `termination_by` to specify a decreasing measure.
```

The three recursive calls are identified by their source positions. This message conveys the following facts:
  * In the first recursive call, all arguments are (provably) equal to the parameters
  * In the second recursive call, the first argument is equal to the first parameter and the second argument is provably smaller than the second parameter. The third parameter was not checked for this recursive call, because it was not necessary to determine that no suitable termination argument exists.
  * In the third recursive call, the first argument decreases strictly, and the other arguments were not checked.


When termination proofs fail in this manner, a good technique to discover the problem is to explicitly indicate the expected termination argument using ``Lean.Parser.Command.declaration : command```termination_by`. This will surface the messages from the failing tactic.
Array Indexing
The purpose of considering expressions of the form `e₂ - e₁` as measures is to support the common idiom of counting up to some upper bound, in particular when traversing arrays in possibly interesting ways. In the following function, which performs binary search on a sorted array, this heuristic helps Lean to find the `j - i` measure.
`def binarySearch (x : [Int](Basic-Types/Integers/#Int___ofNat "Documentation for Int")) (xs : [Array](Basic-Types/Arrays/#Array___mk "Documentation for Array") [Int](Basic-Types/Integers/#Int___ofNat "Documentation for Int")) : [Option](Basic-Types/Optional-Values/#Option___none "Documentation for Option") [Nat](Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat") :=   [go](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#binarySearch___go-_LPAR_in-Array-Indexing_RPAR_ "Definition of example") 0 xs.[size](Basic-Types/Arrays/#Array___size "Documentation for Array.size") where   go (i j : [Nat](Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat")) (hj : j ≤ xs.[size](Basic-Types/Arrays/#Array___size "Documentation for Array.size") := by [omega](Tactic-Proofs/Tactic-Reference/#omega "Documentation for tactic")) :=     [if](Terms/Conditionals/#termDepIfThenElse "Documentation for syntax") h : i < j [then](Terms/Conditionals/#termDepIfThenElse "Documentation for syntax")       let mid := (i + j) / 2       let y := xs[mid]       [if](Terms/Conditionals/#termIfThenElse "Documentation for syntax") x = y [then](Terms/Conditionals/#termIfThenElse "Documentation for syntax")         [some](Basic-Types/Optional-Values/#Option___none "Documentation for Option.some") mid       [else](Terms/Conditionals/#termIfThenElse "Documentation for syntax") [if](Terms/Conditionals/#termIfThenElse "Documentation for syntax") x < y [then](Terms/Conditionals/#termIfThenElse "Documentation for syntax")         [go](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#binarySearch___go-_LPAR_in-Array-Indexing_RPAR_ "Definition of example") i mid       [else](Terms/Conditionals/#termIfThenElse "Documentation for syntax")         [go](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#binarySearch___go-_LPAR_in-Array-Indexing_RPAR_ "Definition of example") (mid + 1) j (j, j - i)`termination_by? `
The fact that the inferred termination argument uses some arbitrary measure, rather than an optimal or minimal one, is visible in the inferred measure, which contains a redundant `j`:

```
Try this:
  [apply] termination_by (j, j - i)
```

[Live ↪](javascript:openLiveLink\("CYUwZgBARglgdgQwE4E8DKJkGMAWEAUAHhAFwQCScALgJQGEDOpEAgkkgihdXWQPIAHKjAD2cCADkEVUgF4AUBAgBzERAAMERgDoGMAF4h5AdxwgkRpaoIwIAK2ZTaBHA7IPAJkRaGugyDnQXCIAtiDKCLwKSkowkHhktgA89hBUZnCK0UoANiAywTDAAfi2ANT2dAD0EABMmVm5Mlwkst4A2gXAALr10bFaEK1caSAZWVkMIf6dvUog2Qz+/cTJw+mz0da2M+MQ84sbVmr4nRDlAIx0dr37luNwYndU5gWIwmIA+lAoAPxAA"\))
Termination Proof Tactics During Inference
The tactic indicated by ``Lean.Parser.Command.declaration : command```decreasing_by` is used slightly differently when inferring the termination [measure](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#--tech-term-measure) than it is in the actual termination proof.
  * During inference, it is applied to a _single_ goal, attempting to prove `[<](Type-Classes/Basic-Classes/#LT___mk "Documentation for LT.lt")` or `[≤](Type-Classes/Basic-Classes/#LE___mk "Documentation for LE.le")` on `[Nat](Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat")`.
  * During the termination proof, it is applied to many simultaneous goals (one per recursive call), and the goals may involve the lexicographic ordering of pairs.


A consequence is that a ``Lean.Parser.Command.declaration : command```decreasing_by` block that addresses goals individually and which works successfully with an explicit termination argument can cause inference of the termination measure to fail:
``Could not find a decreasing measure. The basic measures relate at each recursive call as follows: (<, ≤, =: relation proved, ? all proofs failed, _: no proof attempted)              x1 x2 1) 633:16-23  ?  ? 2) 634:27-40  _  _ 3) 634:20-41  _  _ Please use `termination_by` to specify a decreasing measure.`def ack : [Nat](Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat") → [Nat](Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat") → [Nat](Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat") | 0, n => n + 1 | m + 1, 0 => [ack](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#ack-_LPAR_in-Termination-Proof-Tactics-During-Inference_RPAR_ "Definition of example") m 1 | m + 1, n + 1 => [ack](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#ack-_LPAR_in-Termination-Proof-Tactics-During-Inference_RPAR_ "Definition of example") m ([ack](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#ack-_LPAR_in-Termination-Proof-Tactics-During-Inference_RPAR_ "Definition of example") (m + 1) n) decreasing_by · [apply](Tactic-Proofs/Tactic-Reference/#apply "Documentation for tactic") Prod.Lex.left [omega](Tactic-Proofs/Tactic-Reference/#omega "Documentation for tactic") · [apply](Tactic-Proofs/Tactic-Reference/#apply "Documentation for tactic") Prod.Lex.right [omega](Tactic-Proofs/Tactic-Reference/#omega "Documentation for tactic") · [apply](Tactic-Proofs/Tactic-Reference/#apply "Documentation for tactic") Prod.Lex.left [omega](Tactic-Proofs/Tactic-Reference/#omega "Documentation for tactic") `
It is advisable to always include a ``Lean.Parser.Command.declaration : command```termination_by` clause whenever an explicit ``Lean.Parser.Command.declaration : command```decreasing_by` proof is given.
Inference too powerful
Because `[decreasing_tactic](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#decreasing_tactic "Documentation for tactic")` avoids the need to backtrack by being incomplete with regard to lexicographic ordering, Lean may infer a termination [measure](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#--tech-term-measure) that leads to goals that the tactic cannot prove. In this case, the error message is the one that results from the failing tactic rather than the one that results from being unable to find a measure. This is what happens in `[notAck](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#notAck-_LPAR_in-Inference-too-powerful_RPAR_ "Definition of example")`:
`def notAck : [Nat](Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat") → [Nat](Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat") → [Nat](Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat")   | 0, n => n + 1   | m + 1, 0 => [notAck](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#notAck-_LPAR_in-Inference-too-powerful_RPAR_ "Definition of example") m 1   | m + 1, n + 1 => [notAck](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#notAck-_LPAR_in-Inference-too-powerful_RPAR_ "Definition of example") m ([notAck](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#notAck-_LPAR_in-Inference-too-powerful_RPAR_ "Definition of example") (m / 2 + 1) n) decreasing_by [all_goals](Tactic-Proofs/The-Tactic-Language/#all_goals "Documentation for tactic") `failed to prove termination, possible solutions:   - Use `have`-expressions to prove the remaining goals   - Use `termination_by` to specify a different well-founded relation   - Use `decreasing_by` to specify your own tactic for discharging this kind of goal hm n:[Nat](Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat")⊢ m [/](Type-Classes/Basic-Classes/#HDiv___mk "Documentation for HDiv.hDiv") 2 [+](Type-Classes/Basic-Classes/#HAdd___mk "Documentation for HAdd.hAdd") 1 [<](Type-Classes/Basic-Classes/#LT___mk "Documentation for LT.lt") m [+](Type-Classes/Basic-Classes/#HAdd___mk "Documentation for HAdd.hAdd") 1`[decreasing_tactic](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#decreasing_tactic "Documentation for tactic")All goals completed! 🐙 `
```
failed to prove termination, possible solutions:
  - Use `have`-expressions to prove the remaining goals
  - Use `termination_by` to specify a different well-founded relation
  - Use `decreasing_by` to specify your own tactic for discharging this kind of goal
hm n:[Nat](Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat")⊢ m [/](Type-Classes/Basic-Classes/#HDiv___mk "Documentation for HDiv.hDiv") 2 [+](Type-Classes/Basic-Classes/#HAdd___mk "Documentation for HAdd.hAdd") 1 [<](Type-Classes/Basic-Classes/#LT___mk "Documentation for LT.lt") m [+](Type-Classes/Basic-Classes/#HAdd___mk "Documentation for HAdd.hAdd") 1
```

In this case, explicitly stating the termination [measure](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#--tech-term-measure) helps.
###  7.6.3.5. Mutual Well-Founded Recursion[🔗](find/?domain=Verso.Genre.Manual.section&name=mutual-well-founded-recursion "Permalink")
Lean supports the definition of [mutually recursive](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#--tech-term-mutually-recursive) functions using [well-founded recursion](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#--tech-term-well-founded-recursion). Mutual recursion may be introduced using a [mutual block](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#--tech-term-mutual-block), but it also results from ``Lean.Parser.Term.letrec : term```let rec` expressions and ``Lean.Parser.Command.declaration : command```where` blocks. The rules for mutual well-founded recursion are applied to a group of actually mutually recursive, lifted definitions, that results from the [elaboration steps](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#mutual-syntax) for mutual groups.
If any function in the mutual group has a ``Lean.Parser.Command.declaration : command```termination_by` or ``Lean.Parser.Command.declaration : command```decreasing_by` clause, well-founded recursion is attempted. If a termination [measure](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#--tech-term-measure) is specified using ``Lean.Parser.Command.declaration : command```termination_by` for _any_ function in the mutual group, then _all_ functions in the group must specify a termination measure, and they have to have the same type.
If no termination argument is specified, the termination argument is [inferred, as described above](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#inferring-well-founded-recursion). In the case of mutual recursion, a third class of basic measures is considered during inference, namely for each function in the mutual group the measure that is `1` for that function and `0` for the others. This allows Lean to order the functions so that some calls from one function to another are allowed even if the parameters do not decrease.
Mutual recursion without parameter decrease
In the following mutual function definitions, the parameter does not decrease in the call from `[g](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#g-_LPAR_in-Mutual-recursion-without-parameter-decrease_RPAR_ "Definition of example")` to `[f](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#f-_LPAR_in-Mutual-recursion-without-parameter-decrease_RPAR_ "Definition of example")`. Nonetheless, the definition is accepted due to the ordering imposed on the functions themselves by the additional basic measure.
`[mutual](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#Lean___Parser___Command___mutual "Documentation for syntax")   def f : (n : [Nat](Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat")) → [Nat](Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat")     | 0 => 0     | n + 1 => [g](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#g-_LPAR_in-Mutual-recursion-without-parameter-decrease_RPAR_ "Definition of example") n   `Try this:   [apply] termination_by n => (n, 0)`termination_by? def g (n : [Nat](Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat")) : [Nat](Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat") := ([f](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#f-_LPAR_in-Mutual-recursion-without-parameter-decrease_RPAR_ "Definition of example") n) + 1 `Try this:   [apply] termination_by (n, 1)`termination_by? [end](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#Lean___Parser___Command___mutual "Documentation for syntax") `
The inferred termination argument for `[f](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#f-_LPAR_in-Mutual-recursion-without-parameter-decrease_RPAR_ "Definition of example")` is:

```
Try this:
  [apply] termination_by n => (n, 0)
```

The inferred termination argument for `[g](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#g-_LPAR_in-Mutual-recursion-without-parameter-decrease_RPAR_ "Definition of example")` is:

```
Try this:
  [apply] termination_by (n, 1)
```

###  7.6.3.6. Preprocessing Function Definitions[🔗](find/?domain=Verso.Genre.Manual.section&name=well-founded-preprocessing "Permalink")
Lean _preprocesses_ the function's body before determining the proof obligations at each call site, transforming it into an equivalent definition that may include additional information. This preprocessing step is primarily used to enrich the local context with additional assumptions that may be necessary in order to solve the termination proof obligations, freeing users from the need to perform equivalent transformations by hand. Preprocessing uses the [simplifier](The-Simplifier/#the-simplifier) and is extensible by the user.
The preprocessing happens in three steps:
  1. Lean annotates occurrences of a function's parameter, or a subterm of a parameter, with the `[wfParam](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#wfParam "Documentation for wfParam")` [gadget](Type-Classes/Class-Declarations/#--tech-term-gadgets).
`[wfParam](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#wfParam "Documentation for wfParam") {α} (a : α) : α`
More precisely, every occurrence of the function's parameters is wrapped in `[wfParam](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#wfParam "Documentation for wfParam")`. Whenever a ``Lean.Parser.Term.match : term`
Pattern matching. `match e, ... with | p, ... => f | ...` matches each given term `e` against each pattern `p` of a match alternative. When all patterns of an alternative match, the `match` term evaluates to the value of the corresponding right-hand side `f` with the pattern variables bound to the respective matched values. If used as `match h : e, ... with | p, ... => f | ...`, `h : e = p` is available within `f`.
When not constructing a proof, `match` does not automatically substitute variables matched on in dependent variables' types. Use `match (generalizing := true) ...` to enforce this.
Syntax quotations can also be used in a pattern match. This matches a `Syntax` value against quotations, pattern variables, or `_`.
Quoted identifiers only match identical identifiers - custom matching such as by the preresolved names only should be done explicitly.
`Syntax.atom`s are ignored during matching by default except when part of a built-in literal. For users introducing new atoms, we recommend wrapping them in dedicated syntax kinds if they should participate in matching. For example, in

```
syntax "c" ("foo" <|> "bar") ...

```

`foo` and `bar` are indistinguishable during matching, but in

```
syntax foo := "foo"
syntax "c" (foo <|> "bar") ...

```

they are not.
`[`match`](Terms/Pattern-Matching/#Lean___Parser___Term___match) expression has _any_ discriminant wrapped in `[wfParam](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#wfParam "Documentation for wfParam")`, the gadget is removed and every occurrence of a pattern match variable (regardless of whether it comes from the discriminant with the `[wfParam](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#wfParam "Documentation for wfParam")` gadget) is wrapped in `[wfParam](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#wfParam "Documentation for wfParam")`. The `[wfParam](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#wfParam "Documentation for wfParam")` gadget is additionally floated out of [projection function](The-Type-System/Inductive-Types/#--tech-term-projection-function) applications.
  2. The annotated function body is simplified using [the simplifier](The-Simplifier/#the-simplifier), using only simplification rules from the `wf_preprocess` [custom simp set](The-Simplifier/Simp-sets/#--tech-term-Custom-simp-sets).
  3. Finally, any left-over `[wfParam](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#wfParam "Documentation for wfParam")` markers are removed.


Annotating function parameters that are used for well-founded recursion allows the preprocessing simplification rules to distinguish between parameters and other terms.
attributePreprocessing Simp Set for Well-Founded Recursion

```
attr ::= ...
    | 


Theorems tagged with the wf_preprocess attribute are used during the processing of functions defined
by well-founded recursion. They are applied to the function's body to add additional hypotheses,
such as replacing if c then _ else _ with if h : c then _ else _ or xs.map with
xs.attach.map. Also see wfParam.


Warning: These rewrites are only applied to the declaration for the purpose of the logical
definition, but do not affect the compiled code. In particular they can cause a function definition
that diverges as compiled to be accepted without an explicit partial keyword, for example if they
remove irrelevant subterms or change the evaluation order by hiding terms under binders. Therefore
avoid tagging theorems with [wf_preprocess] unless they preserve also operational behavior.


wf_preprocess
```

Theorems tagged with the `[wf_preprocess](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#Lean___Parser___Attr___wf_preprocess "Documentation for syntax")` attribute are used during the processing of functions defined by well-founded recursion. They are applied to the function's body to add additional hypotheses, such as replacing `[if](Tactic-Proofs/The-Tactic-Language/#if "Documentation for tactic") c [then](Tactic-Proofs/The-Tactic-Language/#if "Documentation for tactic") _ [else](Tactic-Proofs/The-Tactic-Language/#if "Documentation for tactic") _` with `if h : c then _ else _` or `xs.map` with `xs.attach.map`. Also see `[wfParam](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#wfParam "Documentation for wfParam")`.
Warning: These rewrites are only applied to the declaration for the purpose of the logical definition, but do not affect the compiled code. In particular they can cause a function definition that diverges as compiled to be accepted without an explicit `partial` keyword, for example if they remove irrelevant subterms or change the evaluation order by hiding terms under binders. Therefore avoid tagging theorems with `[[wf_preprocess](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#Lean___Parser___Attr___wf_preprocess "Documentation for syntax")]` unless they preserve also operational behavior.
[🔗](find/?domain=Verso.Genre.Manual.doc&name=wfParam "Permalink")def
```


wfParam.{u} {α : Sort u} (a : α) : α


wfParam.{u} {α : Sort u} (a : α) : α


```

The `[wfParam](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#wfParam "Documentation for wfParam")` gadget is used internally during the construction of recursive functions by wellfounded recursion, to keep track of the parameter for which the automatic introduction of `[List.attach](Basic-Types/Linked-Lists/#List___attach "Documentation for List.attach")` (or similar) is plausible.
Some rewrite rules in the `wf_preprocess` simp set apply generally, without heeding the `[wfParam](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#wfParam "Documentation for wfParam")` marker. In particular, the theorem `ite_eq_dite` is used to extend the context of an [if-then-else](Terms/Conditionals/#if-then-else) expression branch with an assumption about the condition:This assumption's name should be an inaccessible name based on `h`, as is indicated by using `[binderNameHint](Tactic-Proofs/Naming-Bound-Variables/#binderNameHint "Documentation for binderNameHint")` with the term `()`. Binder name hints are described in the [tactic language reference](Tactic-Proofs/Naming-Bound-Variables/#bound-variable-name-hints).
`ite_eq_dite {P : Prop} {α : Sort u} {a b : α} [[Decidable](Type-Classes/Basic-Classes/#Decidable___isFalse "Documentation for Decidable") P]  :   ([if](Terms/Conditionals/#termIfThenElse "Documentation for syntax") P [then](Terms/Conditionals/#termIfThenElse "Documentation for syntax") a [else](Terms/Conditionals/#termIfThenElse "Documentation for syntax") b) =   [if](Terms/Conditionals/#termDepIfThenElse "Documentation for syntax") h : P [then](Terms/Conditionals/#termDepIfThenElse "Documentation for syntax")     [binderNameHint](Tactic-Proofs/Naming-Bound-Variables/#binderNameHint "Documentation for binderNameHint") h () a   [else](Terms/Conditionals/#termDepIfThenElse "Documentation for syntax")     [binderNameHint](Tactic-Proofs/Naming-Bound-Variables/#binderNameHint "Documentation for binderNameHint") h () b`
Other rewrite rules use the `[wfParam](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#wfParam "Documentation for wfParam")` marker to restrict their applicability; they are used only when a function (like `[List.map](Basic-Types/Linked-Lists/#List___map "Documentation for List.map")`) is applied to a parameter or subterm of a parameter, but not otherwise. This is typically done in two steps:
  1. A theorem such as `List.map_wfParam` recognizes a call of `[List.map](Basic-Types/Linked-Lists/#List___map "Documentation for List.map")` on a function parameter (or subterm), and uses `[List.attach](Basic-Types/Linked-Lists/#List___attach "Documentation for List.attach")` to enrich the type of the list elements with the assertion that they are indeed elements of that list:
`List.map_wfParam (xs : [List](Basic-Types/Linked-Lists/#List___nil "Documentation for List") α) (f : α → β) :   ([wfParam](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#wfParam "Documentation for wfParam") xs).[map](Basic-Types/Linked-Lists/#List___map "Documentation for List.map") f = xs.[attach](Basic-Types/Linked-Lists/#List___attach "Documentation for List.attach").[unattach](Basic-Types/Linked-Lists/#List___unattach "Documentation for List.unattach").[map](Basic-Types/Linked-Lists/#List___map "Documentation for List.map") f`
  2. A theorem such as `List.map_unattach` makes that assertion available to the function parameter of `[List.map](Basic-Types/Linked-Lists/#List___map "Documentation for List.map")`.
`List.map_unattach (P : α → Prop)   (xs : [List](Basic-Types/Linked-Lists/#List___nil "Documentation for List") { x : α // P x }) (f : α → β) :   xs.[unattach](Basic-Types/Linked-Lists/#List___unattach "Documentation for List.unattach").[map](Basic-Types/Linked-Lists/#List___map "Documentation for List.map") f = xs.[map](Basic-Types/Linked-Lists/#List___map "Documentation for List.map") fun ⟨x, h⟩ =>     [binderNameHint](Tactic-Proofs/Naming-Bound-Variables/#binderNameHint "Documentation for binderNameHint") x f <|     [binderNameHint](Tactic-Proofs/Naming-Bound-Variables/#binderNameHint "Documentation for binderNameHint") h () <|     f ([wfParam](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#wfParam "Documentation for wfParam") x)`
This theorem uses the `[binderNameHint](Tactic-Proofs/Naming-Bound-Variables/#binderNameHint "Documentation for binderNameHint")` gadget to preserve a user-chosen binder name, should `f` be a lambda expression.


By separating the introduction of `[List.attach](Basic-Types/Linked-Lists/#List___attach "Documentation for List.attach")` from the propagation of the introduced assumption, the desired the `x ∈ xs` assumption is made available to `f` even in chains such as `(xs.reverse.filter p).map f`.
This preprocessing can be disabled by setting the option `wf.preprocess` to `[false](Basic-Types/Booleans/#Bool___false "Documentation for Bool.false")`. To see the preprocessed function definition, before and after the removal of `[wfParam](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#wfParam "Documentation for wfParam")` markers, set the option `[trace.Elab.definition.wf](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#trace___Elab___definition___wf "Documentation for option trace.Elab.definition.wf")` to `[true](Basic-Types/Booleans/#Bool___false "Documentation for Bool.true")`.
[🔗](find/?domain=Verso.Genre.Manual.doc.option&name=trace.Elab.definition.wf "Permalink")option
```
trace.Elab.definition.wf
```

Default value: `[false](Basic-Types/Booleans/#Bool___false "Documentation for Bool.false")`
enable/disable tracing for the given module and submodules
Preprocessing for a custom data type
This example demonstrates what is necessary to enable automatic well-founded recursion for a custom container type. The structure type `[Pair](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#Pair-_LPAR_in-Preprocessing-for-a-custom-data-type_RPAR_ "Definition of example")` is a homogeneous pair: it contains precisely two elements, both of which have the same type. It can be thought of as being similar to a list or array that always contains precisely two elements.
As a container, `[Pair](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#Pair-_LPAR_in-Preprocessing-for-a-custom-data-type_RPAR_ "Definition of example")` can support a `[map](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#Pair___map-_LPAR_in-Preprocessing-for-a-custom-data-type_RPAR_ "Definition of example")` operation. To support well-founded recursion in which recursive calls occur in the body of a function being mapped over a `[Pair](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#Pair-_LPAR_in-Preprocessing-for-a-custom-data-type_RPAR_ "Definition of example")`, some additional definitions are required, including a membership predicate, a theorem that relates the size of a member to the size of the containing pair, helpers to introduce and eliminate assumptions about membership, `wf_preprocess` rules to insert these helpers, and an extension to the `[decreasing_trivial](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#decreasing_trivial "Documentation for tactic")` tactic. Each of these steps makes it easier to work with `[Pair](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#Pair-_LPAR_in-Preprocessing-for-a-custom-data-type_RPAR_ "Definition of example")`, but none are strictly necessary; there's no need to immediately implement all steps for every type.
`/-- A homogeneous pair -/ structure Pair (α : Type u) where   fst : α   snd : α  /-- Mapping a function over the elements of a pair -/ def Pair.map (f : α → β) (p : [Pair](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#Pair-_LPAR_in-Preprocessing-for-a-custom-data-type_RPAR_ "Definition of example") α) : [Pair](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#Pair-_LPAR_in-Preprocessing-for-a-custom-data-type_RPAR_ "Definition of example") β where   [fst](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#Pair___fst-_LPAR_in-Preprocessing-for-a-custom-data-type_RPAR_ "Definition of example") := f p.[fst](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#Pair___fst-_LPAR_in-Preprocessing-for-a-custom-data-type_RPAR_ "Definition of example")   [snd](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#Pair___snd-_LPAR_in-Preprocessing-for-a-custom-data-type_RPAR_ "Definition of example") := f p.[snd](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#Pair___snd-_LPAR_in-Preprocessing-for-a-custom-data-type_RPAR_ "Definition of example") `
Defining a nested inductive data type of binary trees that uses `[Pair](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#Pair-_LPAR_in-Preprocessing-for-a-custom-data-type_RPAR_ "Definition of example")` and attempting to define its `map` function demonstrates the need for preprocessing rules.
`/-- A binary tree defined using `Pair` -/ inductive Tree (α : Type u) where   | leaf : α → [Tree](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#Tree-_LPAR_in-Preprocessing-for-a-custom-data-type_RPAR_ "Definition of example") α   | node : [Pair](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#Pair-_LPAR_in-Preprocessing-for-a-custom-data-type_RPAR_ "Definition of example") ([Tree](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#Tree-_LPAR_in-Preprocessing-for-a-custom-data-type_RPAR_ "Definition of example") α) → [Tree](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#Tree-_LPAR_in-Preprocessing-for-a-custom-data-type_RPAR_ "Definition of example") α `
A straightforward definition of the `map` function fails:
`def Tree.map (f : α → β) : [Tree](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#Tree-_LPAR_in-Preprocessing-for-a-custom-data-type_RPAR_ "Definition of example") α → [Tree](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#Tree-_LPAR_in-Preprocessing-for-a-custom-data-type_RPAR_ "Definition of example") β   | [leaf](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#Tree___leaf-_LPAR_in-Preprocessing-for-a-custom-data-type_RPAR_ "Definition of example") x => [leaf](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#Tree___leaf-_LPAR_in-Preprocessing-for-a-custom-data-type_RPAR_ "Definition of example") (f x)   | [node](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#Tree___node-_LPAR_in-Preprocessing-for-a-custom-data-type_RPAR_ "Definition of example") p => [node](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#Tree___node-_LPAR_in-Preprocessing-for-a-custom-data-type_RPAR_ "Definition of example") (p.[map](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#Pair___map-_LPAR_in-Preprocessing-for-a-custom-data-type_RPAR_ "Definition of example") (fun t' => `failed to prove termination, possible solutions:   - Use `have`-expressions to prove the remaining goals   - Use `termination_by` to specify a different well-founded relation   - Use `decreasing_by` to specify your own tactic for discharging this kind of goal α:Type u_1p:[Pair](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#Pair-_LPAR_in-Preprocessing-for-a-custom-data-type_RPAR_ "Definition of example") ([Tree](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#Tree-_LPAR_in-Preprocessing-for-a-custom-data-type_RPAR_ "Definition of example") α)t':[Tree](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#Tree-_LPAR_in-Preprocessing-for-a-custom-data-type_RPAR_ "Definition of example") α⊢ [sizeOf](The-Type-System/Inductive-Types/#SizeOf___mk "Documentation for SizeOf.sizeOf") t' [<](Type-Classes/Basic-Classes/#LT___mk "Documentation for LT.lt") 1 [+](Type-Classes/Basic-Classes/#HAdd___mk "Documentation for HAdd.hAdd") [sizeOf](The-Type-System/Inductive-Types/#SizeOf___mk "Documentation for SizeOf.sizeOf") p`t'.map f)) termination_by t => t `
```
failed to prove termination, possible solutions:
  - Use `have`-expressions to prove the remaining goals
  - Use `termination_by` to specify a different well-founded relation
  - Use `decreasing_by` to specify your own tactic for discharging this kind of goal
α:Type u_1p:[Pair](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#Pair-_LPAR_in-Preprocessing-for-a-custom-data-type_RPAR_ "Definition of example") ([Tree](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#Tree-_LPAR_in-Preprocessing-for-a-custom-data-type_RPAR_ "Definition of example") α)t':[Tree](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#Tree-_LPAR_in-Preprocessing-for-a-custom-data-type_RPAR_ "Definition of example") α⊢ [sizeOf](The-Type-System/Inductive-Types/#SizeOf___mk "Documentation for SizeOf.sizeOf") t' [<](Type-Classes/Basic-Classes/#LT___mk "Documentation for LT.lt") 1 [+](Type-Classes/Basic-Classes/#HAdd___mk "Documentation for HAdd.hAdd") [sizeOf](The-Type-System/Inductive-Types/#SizeOf___mk "Documentation for SizeOf.sizeOf") p
```

Clearly the proof obligation is not solvable, because nothing connects `t'` to `p`.
The standard idiom to enable this kind of function definition is to have a function that enriches each element of a collection with a proof that they are, in fact, elements of the collection. Stating this property requires a membership predicate.
`inductive Pair.Mem (p : [Pair](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#Pair-_LPAR_in-Preprocessing-for-a-custom-data-type_RPAR_ "Definition of example") α) : α → Prop where   | fst : [Mem](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#Pair___Mem-_LPAR_in-Preprocessing-for-a-custom-data-type_RPAR_ "Definition of example") p p.[fst](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#Pair___fst-_LPAR_in-Preprocessing-for-a-custom-data-type_RPAR_ "Definition of example")   | snd : [Mem](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#Pair___Mem-_LPAR_in-Preprocessing-for-a-custom-data-type_RPAR_ "Definition of example") p p.[snd](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#Pair___snd-_LPAR_in-Preprocessing-for-a-custom-data-type_RPAR_ "Definition of example")  instance : Membership α ([Pair](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#Pair-_LPAR_in-Preprocessing-for-a-custom-data-type_RPAR_ "Definition of example") α) where   mem := [Pair.Mem](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#Pair___Mem-_LPAR_in-Preprocessing-for-a-custom-data-type_RPAR_ "Definition of example") `
Every inductive type automatically has a `[SizeOf](The-Type-System/Inductive-Types/#SizeOf___mk "Documentation for SizeOf")` instance. An element of a collection should be smaller than the collection, but this fact must be proved before it can be used to construct a termination proof:

The next step is to define `[attach](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#Pair___attach-_LPAR_in-Preprocessing-for-a-custom-data-type_RPAR_ "Definition of example")` and `[unattach](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#Pair___unattach-_LPAR_in-Preprocessing-for-a-custom-data-type_RPAR_ "Definition of example")` functions that enrich the elements of the pair with a proof that they are elements of the pair, or remove said proof. Here, the type of `[Pair.unattach](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#Pair___unattach-_LPAR_in-Preprocessing-for-a-custom-data-type_RPAR_ "Definition of example")` is more general and can be used with any [subtype](Basic-Types/Subtypes/#Subtype); this is a typical pattern.
`def Pair.attach (p : [Pair](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#Pair-_LPAR_in-Preprocessing-for-a-custom-data-type_RPAR_ "Definition of example") α) : [Pair](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#Pair-_LPAR_in-Preprocessing-for-a-custom-data-type_RPAR_ "Definition of example") {x : α // x ∈ p} where   [fst](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#Pair___fst-_LPAR_in-Preprocessing-for-a-custom-data-type_RPAR_ "Definition of example") := ⟨p.[fst](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#Pair___fst-_LPAR_in-Preprocessing-for-a-custom-data-type_RPAR_ "Definition of example"), [.fst](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#Pair___Mem___fst-_LPAR_in-Preprocessing-for-a-custom-data-type_RPAR_ "Definition of example")⟩   [snd](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#Pair___snd-_LPAR_in-Preprocessing-for-a-custom-data-type_RPAR_ "Definition of example") := ⟨p.[snd](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#Pair___snd-_LPAR_in-Preprocessing-for-a-custom-data-type_RPAR_ "Definition of example"), [.snd](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#Pair___Mem___snd-_LPAR_in-Preprocessing-for-a-custom-data-type_RPAR_ "Definition of example")⟩  def Pair.unattach {P : α → Prop} :     [Pair](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#Pair-_LPAR_in-Preprocessing-for-a-custom-data-type_RPAR_ "Definition of example") {x : α // P x} → [Pair](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#Pair-_LPAR_in-Preprocessing-for-a-custom-data-type_RPAR_ "Definition of example") α :=   [Pair.map](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#Pair___map-_LPAR_in-Preprocessing-for-a-custom-data-type_RPAR_ "Definition of example") [Subtype.val](Basic-Types/Subtypes/#Subtype___mk "Documentation for Subtype.val") `
`Tree.map` can now be defined by using `[Pair.attach](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#Pair___attach-_LPAR_in-Preprocessing-for-a-custom-data-type_RPAR_ "Definition of example")` and `[Pair.sizeOf_lt_of_mem](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#Pair___sizeOf_lt_of_mem-_LPAR_in-Preprocessing-for-a-custom-data-type_RPAR_ "Definition of example")` explicitly:

This transformation can be made fully automatic. The preprocessing feature of well-founded recursion can be used to automate the introduction of the `[Pair.attach](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#Pair___attach-_LPAR_in-Preprocessing-for-a-custom-data-type_RPAR_ "Definition of example")` function. This is done in two stages. First, when `[Pair.map](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#Pair___map-_LPAR_in-Preprocessing-for-a-custom-data-type_RPAR_ "Definition of example")` is applied to one of the function's parameters, it is rewritten to an `[attach](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#Pair___attach-_LPAR_in-Preprocessing-for-a-custom-data-type_RPAR_ "Definition of example")`/`[unattach](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#Pair___unattach-_LPAR_in-Preprocessing-for-a-custom-data-type_RPAR_ "Definition of example")` composition. Then, when a function is mapped over the result of `[Pair.unattach](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#Pair___unattach-_LPAR_in-Preprocessing-for-a-custom-data-type_RPAR_ "Definition of example")`, the function is rewritten to accept the proof of membership and bring it into scope.
`@[[wf_preprocess](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#Lean___Parser___Attr___wf_preprocess "Documentation for syntax")] theorem Pair.map_wfParam (f : α → β) (p : [Pair](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#Pair-_LPAR_in-Preprocessing-for-a-custom-data-type_RPAR_ "Definition of example") α) :     ([wfParam](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#wfParam "Documentation for wfParam") p).[map](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#Pair___map-_LPAR_in-Preprocessing-for-a-custom-data-type_RPAR_ "Definition of example") f = p.[attach](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#Pair___attach-_LPAR_in-Preprocessing-for-a-custom-data-type_RPAR_ "Definition of example").[unattach](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#Pair___unattach-_LPAR_in-Preprocessing-for-a-custom-data-type_RPAR_ "Definition of example").[map](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#Pair___map-_LPAR_in-Preprocessing-for-a-custom-data-type_RPAR_ "Definition of example") f := byα:Type u_1β:Type u_2f:α → βp:[Pair](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#Pair-_LPAR_in-Preprocessing-for-a-custom-data-type_RPAR_ "Definition of example") α⊢ [map](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#Pair___map-_LPAR_in-Preprocessing-for-a-custom-data-type_RPAR_ "Definition of example") f ([wfParam](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#wfParam "Documentation for wfParam") p) [=](Basic-Propositions/Propositional-Equality/#Eq___refl "Documentation for Eq") Now the function body can be written without extra considerations, and the membership assumption is still available to the termination proof.
