The proof can be made fully automatic by adding `[sizeOf_lt_of_mem](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#Pair___sizeOf_lt_of_mem-_LPAR_in-Preprocessing-for-a-custom-data-type_RPAR_ "Definition of example")` to the `[decreasing_trivial](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#decreasing_trivial "Documentation for tactic")` tactic, as is done for similar built-in theorems.
`[macro](Notations-and-Macros/Macros/#Lean___Parser___Command___macro "Documentation for syntax") "sizeOf_pair_dec" : tactic =>   `(tactic| with_reducible     have := Pair.sizeOf_lt_of_mem ‹_›     [omega](Tactic-Proofs/Tactic-Reference/#omega "Documentation for tactic")     [done](Tactic-Proofs/Tactic-Reference/#done "Documentation for tactic"))  [macro_rules](Notations-and-Macros/Macros/#Lean___Parser___Command___macro_rules "Documentation for syntax")   | `(tactic| [decreasing_trivial](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#decreasing_trivial "Documentation for tactic")) =>     `(tactic| sizeOf_pair_dec)  def Tree.map (f : α → β) : [Tree](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#Tree-_LPAR_in-Preprocessing-for-a-custom-data-type_RPAR_ "Definition of example") α → [Tree](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#Tree-_LPAR_in-Preprocessing-for-a-custom-data-type_RPAR_ "Definition of example") β   | [leaf](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#Tree___leaf-_LPAR_in-Preprocessing-for-a-custom-data-type_RPAR_ "Definition of example") x => [leaf](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#Tree___leaf-_LPAR_in-Preprocessing-for-a-custom-data-type_RPAR_ "Definition of example") (f x)   | [node](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#Tree___node-_LPAR_in-Preprocessing-for-a-custom-data-type_RPAR_ "Definition of example") p => [node](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#Tree___node-_LPAR_in-Preprocessing-for-a-custom-data-type_RPAR_ "Definition of example") (p.[map](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#Pair___map-_LPAR_in-Preprocessing-for-a-custom-data-type_RPAR_ "Definition of example") (fun t' => t'.map f)) termination_by t => t `
To keep the example short, the `sizeOf_pair_dec` tactic is tailored to this particular recursion pattern and isn't really general enough for a general-purpose container library. It does, however, demonstrate that libraries can be just as convenient in practice as the container types in the standard library.

###  7.6.3.7. Theory and Construction[🔗](find/?domain=Verso.Genre.Manual.section&name=The-Lean-Language-Reference--Definitions--Recursive-Definitions--Well-Founded-Recursion--Theory-and-Construction "Permalink")
This section gives a very brief glimpse into the mathematical constructions that underlie termination proofs via [well-founded recursion](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#--tech-term-well-founded-recursion), which may surface occasionally. The elaboration of functions defined by well-founded recursion is based on the `[WellFounded.fix](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#WellFounded___fix "Documentation for WellFounded.fix")` operator.
[🔗](find/?domain=Verso.Genre.Manual.doc&name=WellFounded.fix "Permalink")def
```


WellFounded.fix.{u, v} {α : Sort u} {C : α → Sort v} {r : α → α → Prop}
  (hwf : [WellFounded](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#WellFounded___intro "Documentation for WellFounded") r) (F : (x : α) → ((y : α) → r y x → C y) → C x)
  (x : α) : C x


WellFounded.fix.{u, v} {α : Sort u}
  {C : α → Sort v} {r : α → α → Prop}
  (hwf : [WellFounded](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#WellFounded___intro "Documentation for WellFounded") r)
  (F :
    (x : α) →
      ((y : α) → r y x → C y) → C x)
  (x : α) : C x


```

A well-founded fixpoint. If satisfying the motive `C` for all values that are smaller according to a well-founded relation allows it to be satisfied for the current value, then it is satisfied for all values.
This function is used as part of the elaboration of well-founded recursion.
The type `α` is instantiated with the function's (varying) parameters, packed into one type using `[PSigma](Basic-Types/Tuples/#PSigma___mk "Documentation for PSigma")`. The `[WellFounded](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#WellFounded___intro "Documentation for WellFounded")` relation is constructed from the termination [measure](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#--tech-term-measure) via `[invImage](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#invImage "Documentation for invImage")`.
[🔗](find/?domain=Verso.Genre.Manual.doc&name=invImage "Permalink")def
```


invImage.{u_1, u_2} {α : Sort u_1} {β : Sort u_2} (f : α → β)
  (h : [WellFoundedRelation](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#WellFoundedRelation___mk "Documentation for WellFoundedRelation") β) : [WellFoundedRelation](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#WellFoundedRelation___mk "Documentation for WellFoundedRelation") α


invImage.{u_1, u_2} {α : Sort u_1}
  {β : Sort u_2} (f : α → β)
  (h : [WellFoundedRelation](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#WellFoundedRelation___mk "Documentation for WellFoundedRelation") β) :
  [WellFoundedRelation](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#WellFoundedRelation___mk "Documentation for WellFoundedRelation") α


```

The inverse image of a well-founded relation is well-founded.
The function's body is passed to `[WellFounded.fix](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#WellFounded___fix "Documentation for WellFounded.fix")`, with parameters suitably packed and unpacked, and recursive calls are replaced with a call to the value provided by `[WellFounded.fix](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#WellFounded___fix "Documentation for WellFounded.fix")`. The termination proofs generated by the ``Lean.Parser.Command.declaration : command```decreasing_by` tactics are inserted in the right place.
Finally, the equational and unfolding theorems for the recursive function are proved from `WellFounded.fix_eq`. These theorems hide the details of packing and unpacking arguments and describe the function's behavior in terms of the original definition.
In the case of mutual recursion, an equivalent non-mutual function is constructed by combining the function's arguments using `[PSum](Basic-Types/Sum-Types/#PSum___inl "Documentation for PSum")`, and pattern-matching on that sum type in the result type and the body.
The definition of `[WellFounded](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#WellFounded___intro "Documentation for WellFounded")` builds on the notion of _accessible elements_ of the relation:
[🔗](find/?domain=Verso.Genre.Manual.doc&name=WellFounded.intro "Permalink")inductive predicate
```


WellFounded.{u} {α : Sort u} (r : α → α → Prop) : Prop


WellFounded.{u} {α : Sort u}
  (r : α → α → Prop) : Prop


```

A relation `r` is `[WellFounded](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#WellFounded___intro "Documentation for WellFounded")` if all elements of `α` are accessible within `r`. If a relation is `[WellFounded](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#WellFounded___intro "Documentation for WellFounded")`, it does not allow for an infinite descent along the relation.
If the arguments of the recursive calls in a function definition decrease according to a well founded relation, then the function terminates. Well-founded relations are sometimes called _Artinian_ or said to satisfy the “descending chain condition”.
#  Constructors

```
intro.{u} {α : Sort u} {r : α → α → Prop}
  (h : ∀ (a : α), [Acc](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#Acc___intro "Documentation for Acc") r a) : [WellFounded](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#WellFounded___intro "Documentation for WellFounded") r
```

If all elements are accessible via `r`, then `r` is well-founded.
[🔗](find/?domain=Verso.Genre.Manual.doc&name=Acc.intro "Permalink")inductive predicate
```


Acc.{u} {α : Sort u} (r : α → α → Prop) : α → Prop


Acc.{u} {α : Sort u} (r : α → α → Prop) :
  α → Prop


```

`[Acc](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#Acc___intro "Documentation for Acc")` is the accessibility predicate. Given some relation `r` (e.g. `<`) and a value `x`, `[Acc](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#Acc___intro "Documentation for Acc") r x` means that `x` is accessible through `r`:
`x` is accessible if there exists no infinite sequence `... < y₂ < y₁ < y₀ < x`.
#  Constructors

```
intro.{u} {α : Sort u} {r : α → α → Prop} (x : α)
  (h : ∀ (y : α), r y x → [Acc](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#Acc___intro "Documentation for Acc") r y) : [Acc](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#Acc___intro "Documentation for Acc") r x
```

A value is accessible if for all `y` such that `r y x`, `y` is also accessible. Note that if there exists no `y` such that `r y x`, then `x` is accessible. Such an `x` is called a _base case_.
Division by Iterated Subtraction: Termination Proof
The definition of division by iterated subtraction can be written explicitly using well-founded recursion.
`noncomputable def div (n k : [Nat](Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat")) : [Nat](Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat") :=   ([inferInstanceAs](Type-Classes/Instance-Synthesis/#inferInstanceAs "Documentation for inferInstanceAs") ([WellFoundedRelation](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#WellFoundedRelation___mk "Documentation for WellFoundedRelation") [Nat](Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat"))).[wf](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#WellFoundedRelation___mk "Documentation for WellFoundedRelation.wf").[fix](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#WellFounded___fix "Documentation for WellFounded.fix")     (fun n r =>       [if](Terms/Conditionals/#termDepIfThenElse "Documentation for syntax") h : k = 0 [then](Terms/Conditionals/#termDepIfThenElse "Documentation for syntax") 0       [else](Terms/Conditionals/#termDepIfThenElse "Documentation for syntax") [if](Terms/Conditionals/#termDepIfThenElse "Documentation for syntax") h : k > n [then](Terms/Conditionals/#termDepIfThenElse "Documentation for syntax") 0       [else](Terms/Conditionals/#termDepIfThenElse "Documentation for syntax") 1 + (r (n - k) <| byα:Type un✝:[Nat](Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat")k:[Nat](Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat")n:[Nat](Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat")r:(y : [Nat](Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat")) → [WellFoundedRelation.rel](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#WellFoundedRelation___mk "Documentation for WellFoundedRelation.rel") y n → [Nat](Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat")h✝:[¬](Basic-Propositions/Logical-Connectives/#Not "Documentation for Not")k [=](Basic-Propositions/Propositional-Equality/#Eq___refl "Documentation for Eq") 0h:[¬](Basic-Propositions/Logical-Connectives/#Not "Documentation for Not")k > n⊢ [WellFoundedRelation.rel](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#WellFoundedRelation___mk "Documentation for WellFoundedRelation.rel") [(](Type-Classes/Basic-Classes/#HSub___mk "Documentation for HSub.hSub")n [-](Type-Classes/Basic-Classes/#HSub___mk "Documentation for HSub.hSub") k[)](Type-Classes/Basic-Classes/#HSub___mk "Documentation for HSub.hSub") n         [show](Tactic-Proofs/Tactic-Reference/#show "Documentation for tactic") (n - k) < nα:Type un✝:[Nat](Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat")k:[Nat](Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat")n:[Nat](Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat")r:(y : [Nat](Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat")) → [WellFoundedRelation.rel](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#WellFoundedRelation___mk "Documentation for WellFoundedRelation.rel") y n → [Nat](Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat")h✝:[¬](Basic-Propositions/Logical-Connectives/#Not "Documentation for Not")k [=](Basic-Propositions/Propositional-Equality/#Eq___refl "Documentation for Eq") 0h:[¬](Basic-Propositions/Logical-Connectives/#Not "Documentation for Not")k > n⊢ n [-](Type-Classes/Basic-Classes/#HSub___mk "Documentation for HSub.hSub") k [<](Type-Classes/Basic-Classes/#LT___mk "Documentation for LT.lt") n         [omega](Tactic-Proofs/Tactic-Reference/#omega "Documentation for tactic")All goals completed! 🐙))     n `
The definition must be marked ``Lean.Parser.Command.declaration : command```noncomputable` because well-founded recursion is not supported by the compiler. Like [recursors](The-Type-System/Inductive-Types/#--tech-term-recursor), it is part of Lean's logic.
The definition of division should satisfy the following equations:
  * `∀{n k : [Nat](Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat")}, (k = 0) → [div](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#div-_LPAR_in-Division-by-Iterated-Subtraction___-Termination-Proof_RPAR_ "Definition of example") n k = 0`
  * `∀{n k : [Nat](Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat")}, (k > n) → [div](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#div-_LPAR_in-Division-by-Iterated-Subtraction___-Termination-Proof_RPAR_ "Definition of example") n k = 0`
  * `∀{n k : [Nat](Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat")}, (k ≠ 0) → (¬ k > n) → [div](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#div-_LPAR_in-Division-by-Iterated-Subtraction___-Termination-Proof_RPAR_ "Definition of example") n k = 1 + [div](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#div-_LPAR_in-Division-by-Iterated-Subtraction___-Termination-Proof_RPAR_ "Definition of example") (n - k) k`


This reduction behavior does not hold [definitionally](The-Type-System/#--tech-term-definitional-equality):
`theorem div.eq0 : [div](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#div-_LPAR_in-Division-by-Iterated-Subtraction___-Termination-Proof_RPAR_ "Definition of example") n 0 = 0 := byn:[Nat](Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat")⊢ [div](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#div-_LPAR_in-Division-by-Iterated-Subtraction___-Termination-Proof_RPAR_ "Definition of example") n 0 [=](Basic-Propositions/Propositional-Equality/#Eq___refl "Documentation for Eq") 0 `Tactic `rfl` failed: The left-hand side   [div](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#div-_LPAR_in-Division-by-Iterated-Subtraction___-Termination-Proof_RPAR_ "Definition of example") n 0 is not definitionally equal to the right-hand side   0  n:[Nat](Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat")⊢ [div](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#div-_LPAR_in-Division-by-Iterated-Subtraction___-Termination-Proof_RPAR_ "Definition of example") n 0 [=](Basic-Propositions/Propositional-Equality/#Eq___refl "Documentation for Eq") 0`[rfl](Tactic-Proofs/Tactic-Reference/#rfl "Documentation for tactic")n:[Nat](Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat")⊢ [div](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#div-_LPAR_in-Division-by-Iterated-Subtraction___-Termination-Proof_RPAR_ "Definition of example") n 0 [=](Basic-Propositions/Propositional-Equality/#Eq___refl "Documentation for Eq") 0 `
```
Tactic `rfl` failed: The left-hand side
  [div](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#div-_LPAR_in-Division-by-Iterated-Subtraction___-Termination-Proof_RPAR_ "Definition of example") n 0
is not definitionally equal to the right-hand side
  0

n:[Nat](Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat")⊢ [div](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#div-_LPAR_in-Division-by-Iterated-Subtraction___-Termination-Proof_RPAR_ "Definition of example") n 0 [=](Basic-Propositions/Propositional-Equality/#Eq___refl "Documentation for Eq") 0
```

However, using `WellFounded.fix_eq` to unfold the well-founded recursion, the three equations can be proved to hold:

##  7.6.4. Partial Fixpoint Recursion[🔗](find/?domain=Verso.Genre.Manual.section&name=partial-fixpoint "Permalink")
All definitions are fundamentally equations: the new constant being defined is equal to the right-hand side of the definition. For functions defined by [structural recursion](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#structural-recursion), this equation holds [definitionally](The-Type-System/#--tech-term-definitional-equality), and there is a unique value returned by application of the function. For functions defined by [well-founded recursion](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#well-founded-recursion), the equation may hold only [propositionally](The-Type-System/Propositions/#--tech-term-Propositions), but all type-correct applications of the function to arguments are equal to the respective values prescribed by the definition. In both cases, the fact that the function terminates for all inputs means that the value computed by applying the function is always uniquely determined.
In some cases where a function does not terminate for all arguments, the equation may not _uniquely_ determine the function's return value for each input, but there are nonetheless functions for which the defining equation holds. In these cases, a definition as a _partial fixpoint_ may still be possible. Any function that satisfies the defining equation can be used to demonstrate that the equation does not create a logical contradiction, and the equation can then be proven as a theorem about this function. As with the other strategies for defining recursive functions, compiled code uses the function as it was originally written; like definitions in terms of eliminators or recursion over accessibility proofs, the function used to define the partial fixpoint is used only to justify the function's equations in Lean's logic for purposes of mathematical reasoning.
The term [_partial fixpoint_](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#--tech-term-partial-fixpoint) is specific to Lean. Functions declared ``Lean.Parser.Command.declaration : command```partial` do not require termination proofs, so long as the type of their return values is inhabited, but they are completely opaque from the perspective of Lean's logic. Partial fixpoints, on the other hand, can be rewritten using their defining equations while writing proofs. Logically speaking, partial fixpoints are total functions that don't reduce [definitionally](The-Type-System/#--tech-term-definitional-equality) when applied, but for which equational rewrite rule are provided. They are _partial_ in the sense that the defining equation does not necessarily specify a value for all possible arguments.
While partial fixpoints do allow functions to be defined that cannot be expressed using structural or well-founded recursion, the technique is also useful in other cases. Even in cases where the defining equation fully describes the function's behavior and a termination proof using [well-founded recursion](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#well-founded-recursion) would be possible, it may simply be more convenient to define the function as a partial fixpoint to avoid a having to write a termination proof.
Defining recursive functions as partial fixpoints only occurs when explicitly requested by annotating the definition with ``Lean.Parser.Command.declaration : command```partial_fixpoint`.
There are two classes of functions that can be defined as partial fixpoints:
  * Tail-recursive functions whose return type is inhabited type
  * Functions that return values in a suitable monad, such as the `[Option](Basic-Types/Optional-Values/#Option___none "Documentation for Option")` monad


Both classes are backed by the same theory and construction: least fixpoints of monotone equations in chain-complete partial orders.
Just as with structural and well-founded recursion, Lean allows [mutually recursive](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#--tech-term-mutually-recursive) functions to be defined as partial fixpoints. To use this feature, every function definition in a [mutual block](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#--tech-term-mutual-block) must be annotated with the ``Lean.Parser.Command.declaration : command```partial_fixpoint` modifier.
Definition by Partial Fixpoint
The following function finds the least natural number for which the predicate `p` holds. If `p` never holds, then this equation does not specify the behavior: the function `[find](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#find-_LPAR_in-Definition-by-Partial-Fixpoint_RPAR_ "Definition of example")` could return `42` or any other `[Nat](Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat")` in that case and still satisfy the equation.
`def find (p : [Nat](Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat") → [Bool](Basic-Types/Booleans/#Bool___false "Documentation for Bool")) (i : [Nat](Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat") := 0) : [Nat](Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat") :=   [if](Terms/Conditionals/#termIfThenElse "Documentation for syntax") p i [then](Terms/Conditionals/#termIfThenElse "Documentation for syntax")     i   [else](Terms/Conditionals/#termIfThenElse "Documentation for syntax")     [find](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#find-_LPAR_in-Definition-by-Partial-Fixpoint_RPAR_ "Definition of example") p (i + 1) partial_fixpoint `
The elaborator can prove that functions satisfying the equation exist. Within Lean's logic, `[find](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#find-_LPAR_in-Definition-by-Partial-Fixpoint_RPAR_ "Definition of example")` is defined to be an arbitrary such function.
[Live ↪](javascript:openLiveLink\("CYUwZgBGCWB2wQBQAcIC4IDkCGAXCgSYQQBCA9qQDYCUS06We6AvBAAw0Y75pMBQEEaJFR1cACxCx+AwdJAUAziGkCY8CKkR0A1BACMVXsmwAnXNGwUA+jAAeyUnFxA"\))
###  7.6.4.1. Tail-Recursive Functions[🔗](find/?domain=Verso.Genre.Manual.section&name=partial-fixpoint-tailrec "Permalink")
A recursive function can be defined as a partial fixpoint if the following two conditions hold:
  1. The function's return type is inhabited (as with [functions marked ``Lean.Parser.Command.declaration : command```partial`](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#partial-unsafe))—either a `[Nonempty](Type-Classes/Basic-Classes/#Nonempty___intro "Documentation for Nonempty")` or `[Inhabited](Type-Classes/Basic-Classes/#Inhabited___mk "Documentation for Inhabited")` instance works.
  2. All recursive calls are in [tail position](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#--tech-term-tail-position) of the function.


An expression is in _tail position_ in the function body if it is:
  * the function body itself,
  * the branches of a ``Lean.Parser.Term.match : term`
Pattern matching. `match e, ... with | p, ... => f | ...` matches each given term `e` against each pattern `p` of a match alternative. When all patterns of an alternative match, the `match` term evaluates to the value of the corresponding right-hand side `f` with the pattern variables bound to the respective matched values. If used as `match h : e, ... with | p, ... => f | ...`, `h : e = p` is available within `f`.
When not constructing a proof, `match` does not automatically substitute variables matched on in dependent variables' types. Use `match (generalizing := true) ...` to enforce this.
Syntax quotations can also be used in a pattern match. This matches a `Syntax` value against quotations, pattern variables, or `_`.
Quoted identifiers only match identical identifiers - custom matching such as by the preresolved names only should be done explicitly.
`Syntax.atom`s are ignored during matching by default except when part of a built-in literal. For users introducing new atoms, we recommend wrapping them in dedicated syntax kinds if they should participate in matching. For example, in

```
syntax "c" ("foo" <|> "bar") ...

```

`foo` and `bar` are indistinguishable during matching, but in

```
syntax foo := "foo"
syntax "c" (foo <|> "bar") ...

```

they are not.
`[`match`](Terms/Pattern-Matching/#Lean___Parser___Term___match) expression that is in tail position,
  * the branches of an ``termIfThenElse : term`
`if c then t else e` is notation for `ite c t e`, "if-then-else", which decides to return `t` or `e` depending on whether `c` is true or false. The explicit argument `c : Prop` does not have any actual computational content, but there is an additional `[Decidable c]` argument synthesized by typeclass inference which actually determines how to evaluate `c` to true or false. Write `if h : c then t else e` instead for a "dependent if-then-else" `dite`, which allows `t`/`e` to use the fact that `c` is true/false.
`[`if`](Terms/Conditionals/#termIfThenElse) expression that is in tail position, and
  * the body of a ``Lean.Parser.Term.let : term`
`let` is used to declare a local definition. Example:

```
let x := 1
let y := x + 1
x + y

```

Since functions are first class citizens in Lean, you can use `let` to declare local functions too.

```
let double := fun x => 2*x
double (double 3)

```

For recursive definitions, you should use `let rec`. You can also perform pattern matching using `let`. For example, assume `p` has type `Nat × Nat`, then you can write

```
let (x, y) := p
x + y

```

The _anaphoric let_ `let := v` defines a variable called `this`.
``let` expression that is in tail position.


In particular, the [discriminant](Terms/Pattern-Matching/#--tech-term-match-discriminants) of a ``Lean.Parser.Term.match : term`
Pattern matching. `match e, ... with | p, ... => f | ...` matches each given term `e` against each pattern `p` of a match alternative. When all patterns of an alternative match, the `match` term evaluates to the value of the corresponding right-hand side `f` with the pattern variables bound to the respective matched values. If used as `match h : e, ... with | p, ... => f | ...`, `h : e = p` is available within `f`.
When not constructing a proof, `match` does not automatically substitute variables matched on in dependent variables' types. Use `match (generalizing := true) ...` to enforce this.
Syntax quotations can also be used in a pattern match. This matches a `Syntax` value against quotations, pattern variables, or `_`.
Quoted identifiers only match identical identifiers - custom matching such as by the preresolved names only should be done explicitly.
`Syntax.atom`s are ignored during matching by default except when part of a built-in literal. For users introducing new atoms, we recommend wrapping them in dedicated syntax kinds if they should participate in matching. For example, in

```
syntax "c" ("foo" <|> "bar") ...

```

`foo` and `bar` are indistinguishable during matching, but in

```
syntax foo := "foo"
syntax "c" (foo <|> "bar") ...

```

they are not.
`[`match`](Terms/Pattern-Matching/#Lean___Parser___Term___match) expression, the condition of an ``termIfThenElse : term`
`if c then t else e` is notation for `ite c t e`, "if-then-else", which decides to return `t` or `e` depending on whether `c` is true or false. The explicit argument `c : Prop` does not have any actual computational content, but there is an additional `[Decidable c]` argument synthesized by typeclass inference which actually determines how to evaluate `c` to true or false. Write `if h : c then t else e` instead for a "dependent if-then-else" `dite`, which allows `t`/`e` to use the fact that `c` is true/false.
`[`if`](Terms/Conditionals/#termIfThenElse) expression and the arguments of functions are not tail positions.
Loops are Tail Recursive Functions
Because the function body itself is a [tail position](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#--tech-term-tail-position), the infinitely looping function `[loop](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#loop-_LPAR_in-Loops-are-Tail-Recursive-Functions_RPAR_ "Definition of example")` is tail recursive. It can be defined as a partial fixpoint.
`def loop (x : [Nat](Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat")) : [Nat](Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat") := [loop](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#loop-_LPAR_in-Loops-are-Tail-Recursive-Functions_RPAR_ "Definition of example") (x + 1) partial_fixpoint `
[Live ↪](javascript:openLiveLink\("CYUwZgBANg9jAOEAUAPCAuCA5AhgFwEoNt8MBeaORVCAaggEYCAoeHAJzwEscoB9MFxTwYXAHZ4gA"\))
Tail Recursion with Branching
`[Array.find](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#Array___find-_LPAR_in-Tail-Recursion-with-Branching_RPAR_ "Definition of example")` could also be constructed using well-founded recursion with a termination proof, but may be more convenient to define using ``Lean.Parser.Command.declaration : command```partial_fixpoint`, where no termination proof is needed.
`def Array.find (xs : [Array](Basic-Types/Arrays/#Array___mk "Documentation for Array") α) (p : α → [Bool](Basic-Types/Booleans/#Bool___false "Documentation for Bool"))     (i : [Nat](Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat") := 0) : [Option](Basic-Types/Optional-Values/#Option___none "Documentation for Option") α :=   [if](Terms/Conditionals/#termDepIfThenElse "Documentation for syntax") h : i < xs.[size](Basic-Types/Arrays/#Array___size "Documentation for Array.size") [then](Terms/Conditionals/#termDepIfThenElse "Documentation for syntax")     [if](Terms/Conditionals/#termIfThenElse "Documentation for syntax") p xs[i] [then](Terms/Conditionals/#termIfThenElse "Documentation for syntax")       [some](Basic-Types/Optional-Values/#Option___none "Documentation for Option.some") xs[i]     [else](Terms/Conditionals/#termIfThenElse "Documentation for syntax")       [Array.find](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#Array___find-_LPAR_in-Tail-Recursion-with-Branching_RPAR_ "Definition of example") xs p (i + 1)   [else](Terms/Conditionals/#termDepIfThenElse "Documentation for syntax")     [none](Basic-Types/Optional-Values/#Option___none "Documentation for Option.none") partial_fixpoint `
If the result of the recursive call is not just returned, but passed to another function, it is not in tail position and this definition fails.
`def List.findIndex (xs : [List](Basic-Types/Linked-Lists/#List___nil "Documentation for List") α) (p : α → [Bool](Basic-Types/Booleans/#Bool___false "Documentation for Bool")) : [Int](Basic-Types/Integers/#Int___ofNat "Documentation for Int") :=   [match](Terms/Pattern-Matching/#Lean___Parser___Term___match "Documentation for syntax") xs [with](Terms/Pattern-Matching/#Lean___Parser___Term___match "Documentation for syntax")   | [] => -1   | x::ys =>     [if](Terms/Conditionals/#termIfThenElse "Documentation for syntax") p x [then](Terms/Conditionals/#termIfThenElse "Documentation for syntax")       0     [else](Terms/Conditionals/#termIfThenElse "Documentation for syntax")       have r := `Could not prove 'List.findIndex' to be monotone in its recursive calls:   Cannot eliminate recursive call `List.findIndex ys p` enclosed in     if ys✝.[findIndex](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#List___findIndex-_LPAR_in-Tail-Recursion-with-Branching_RPAR_ "Definition of example") p [=](Basic-Propositions/Propositional-Equality/#Eq___refl "Documentation for Eq") -1 then -1 else ys✝.[findIndex](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#List___findIndex-_LPAR_in-Tail-Recursion-with-Branching_RPAR_ "Definition of example") p [+](Type-Classes/Basic-Classes/#HAdd___mk "Documentation for HAdd.hAdd") 1   Tried to apply 'monotone_ite', but failed.   Possible cause: A missing `MonoBind` instance.   Use `set_option trace.Elab.Tactic.monotonicity true` to debug.`[List.findIndex](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#List___findIndex-_LPAR_in-Tail-Recursion-with-Branching_RPAR_ "Definition of example") ys p [if](Terms/Conditionals/#termIfThenElse "Documentation for syntax") r = -1 [then](Terms/Conditionals/#termIfThenElse "Documentation for syntax") -1 [else](Terms/Conditionals/#termIfThenElse "Documentation for syntax") r + 1 partial_fixpoint `
The error message on the recursive call is:

```
Could not prove 'List.findIndex' to be monotone in its recursive calls:
  Cannot eliminate recursive call `List.findIndex ys p` enclosed in
    if ys✝.[findIndex](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#List___findIndex-_LPAR_in-Tail-Recursion-with-Branching_RPAR_ "Definition of example") p [=](Basic-Propositions/Propositional-Equality/#Eq___refl "Documentation for Eq") -1 then -1 else ys✝.[findIndex](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#List___findIndex-_LPAR_in-Tail-Recursion-with-Branching_RPAR_ "Definition of example") p [+](Type-Classes/Basic-Classes/#HAdd___mk "Documentation for HAdd.hAdd") 1

  Possible cause: A missing `MonoBind` instance.
  Use `set_option trace.Elab.Tactic.monotonicity true` to debug.
```

###  7.6.4.2. Monadic functions[🔗](find/?domain=Verso.Genre.Manual.section&name=partial-fixpoint-monadic "Permalink")
Defining a function as a partial fixpoint is more powerful if the function's return type is a monad that is an instance of `Lean.Order.MonoBind`, such as `[Option](Basic-Types/Optional-Values/#Option___none "Documentation for Option")`. In this case, recursive call are not restricted to tail-positions, but may also occur inside higher-order monadic functions such as `[bind](Functors___-Monads-and--do--Notation/#Bind___mk "Documentation for Bind.bind")` and `[List.mapM](Basic-Types/Linked-Lists/#List___mapM "Documentation for List.mapM")`.
The set of higher-order functions for which this works is [extensible](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#partial-fixpoint-theory), so no exhaustive list is given here. The aspiration is that a monadic recursive function definition that is built using abstract monadic operations like `[bind](Functors___-Monads-and--do--Notation/#Bind___mk "Documentation for Bind.bind")`, but that does not open the abstraction of the monad (e.g. by matching on the `[Option](Basic-Types/Optional-Values/#Option___none "Documentation for Option")` value), is accepted. In particular, using [``Lean.Parser.Term.do : term``](Functors___-Monads-and--do--Notation/Syntax/#--tech-term-do-notation)[`do`](Functors___-Monads-and--do--Notation/Syntax/#Lean___Parser___Term___do)-notation should work.
Monadic functions
The following function implements the Ackermann function in the `[Option](Basic-Types/Optional-Values/#Option___none "Documentation for Option")` monad, and is accepted without an (explicit or implicit) termination proof:
`def ack : (n m : [Nat](Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat")) → [Option](Basic-Types/Optional-Values/#Option___none "Documentation for Option") [Nat](Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat")   | 0,   y   => [some](Basic-Types/Optional-Values/#Option___none "Documentation for Option.some") (y+1)   | x+1, 0   => [ack](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#ack-_LPAR_in-Monadic-functions_RPAR_ "Definition of example") x 1   | x+1, y+1 => [do](Functors___-Monads-and--do--Notation/Syntax/#Lean___Parser___Term___do "Documentation for syntax") [ack](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#ack-_LPAR_in-Monadic-functions_RPAR_ "Definition of example") x (← [ack](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#ack-_LPAR_in-Monadic-functions_RPAR_ "Definition of example") (x+1) y) partial_fixpoint `
Recursive calls may also occur within higher-order functions such as `[List.mapM](Basic-Types/Linked-Lists/#List___mapM "Documentation for List.mapM")`, if they are set up appropriately, and [``Lean.Parser.Term.do : term``](Functors___-Monads-and--do--Notation/Syntax/#--tech-term-do-notation)[`do`](Functors___-Monads-and--do--Notation/Syntax/#Lean___Parser___Term___do)-notation:
`structure Tree where cs : [List](Basic-Types/Linked-Lists/#List___nil "Documentation for List") [Tree](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#Tree-_LPAR_in-Monadic-functions_RPAR_ "Definition of example")  def Tree.rev (t : [Tree](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#Tree-_LPAR_in-Monadic-functions_RPAR_ "Definition of example")) : [Option](Basic-Types/Optional-Values/#Option___none "Documentation for Option") [Tree](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#Tree-_LPAR_in-Monadic-functions_RPAR_ "Definition of example") := [do](Functors___-Monads-and--do--Notation/Syntax/#Lean___Parser___Term___do "Documentation for syntax")   Tree.mk (← t.[cs](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#Tree___cs-_LPAR_in-Monadic-functions_RPAR_ "Definition of example").[reverse](Basic-Types/Linked-Lists/#List___reverse "Documentation for List.reverse").[mapM](Basic-Types/Linked-Lists/#List___mapM "Documentation for List.mapM") ([Tree.rev](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#Tree___rev-_LPAR_in-Monadic-functions_RPAR_ "Definition of example") ·)) partial_fixpoint  def Tree.rev' (t : [Tree](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#Tree-_LPAR_in-Monadic-functions_RPAR_ "Definition of example")) : [Option](Basic-Types/Optional-Values/#Option___none "Documentation for Option") [Tree](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#Tree-_LPAR_in-Monadic-functions_RPAR_ "Definition of example") := [do](Functors___-Monads-and--do--Notation/Syntax/#Lean___Parser___Term___do "Documentation for syntax")   let mut cs := []   for c in t.[cs](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#Tree___cs-_LPAR_in-Monadic-functions_RPAR_ "Definition of example") do     cs := (← c.[rev'](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#Tree___rev___-_LPAR_in-Monadic-functions_RPAR_ "Definition of example")) :: cs   return Tree.mk cs partial_fixpoint `
Pattern matching on the result of the recursive call will prevent the definition by partial fixpoint from going through:
`def List.findIndex (xs : [List](Basic-Types/Linked-Lists/#List___nil "Documentation for List") α) (p : α → [Bool](Basic-Types/Booleans/#Bool___false "Documentation for Bool")) : [Option](Basic-Types/Optional-Values/#Option___none "Documentation for Option") [Nat](Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat") :=   [match](Terms/Pattern-Matching/#Lean___Parser___Term___match "Documentation for syntax") xs [with](Terms/Pattern-Matching/#Lean___Parser___Term___match "Documentation for syntax")   | [] => [none](Basic-Types/Optional-Values/#Option___none "Documentation for Option.none")   | x::ys =>     [if](Terms/Conditionals/#termIfThenElse "Documentation for syntax") p x [then](Terms/Conditionals/#termIfThenElse "Documentation for syntax")       [some](Basic-Types/Optional-Values/#Option___none "Documentation for Option.some") 0     [else](Terms/Conditionals/#termIfThenElse "Documentation for syntax")       [match](Terms/Pattern-Matching/#Lean___Parser___Term___match "Documentation for syntax") `Could not prove 'List.findIndex' to be monotone in its recursive calls:   Cannot eliminate recursive call `List.findIndex ys p` enclosed in     match ys✝.findIndex p with     | [none](Basic-Types/Optional-Values/#Option___none "Documentation for Option.none") => [none](Basic-Types/Optional-Values/#Option___none "Documentation for Option.none")     | [some](Basic-Types/Optional-Values/#Option___none "Documentation for Option.some") r => [some](Basic-Types/Optional-Values/#Option___none "Documentation for Option.some") [(](Type-Classes/Basic-Classes/#HAdd___mk "Documentation for HAdd.hAdd")r [+](Type-Classes/Basic-Classes/#HAdd___mk "Documentation for HAdd.hAdd") 1[)](Type-Classes/Basic-Classes/#HAdd___mk "Documentation for HAdd.hAdd")   `List.findIndex ys p [with](Terms/Pattern-Matching/#Lean___Parser___Term___match "Documentation for syntax") | [none](Basic-Types/Optional-Values/#Option___none "Documentation for Option.none") => [none](Basic-Types/Optional-Values/#Option___none "Documentation for Option.none") | [some](Basic-Types/Optional-Values/#Option___none "Documentation for Option.some") r => [some](Basic-Types/Optional-Values/#Option___none "Documentation for Option.some") (r + 1) partial_fixpoint `
```
Could not prove 'List.findIndex' to be monotone in its recursive calls:
  Cannot eliminate recursive call `List.findIndex ys p` enclosed in
    match ys✝.findIndex p with
    | [none](Basic-Types/Optional-Values/#Option___none "Documentation for Option.none") => [none](Basic-Types/Optional-Values/#Option___none "Documentation for Option.none")
    | [some](Basic-Types/Optional-Values/#Option___none "Documentation for Option.some") r => [some](Basic-Types/Optional-Values/#Option___none "Documentation for Option.some") [(](Type-Classes/Basic-Classes/#HAdd___mk "Documentation for HAdd.hAdd")r [+](Type-Classes/Basic-Classes/#HAdd___mk "Documentation for HAdd.hAdd") 1[)](Type-Classes/Basic-Classes/#HAdd___mk "Documentation for HAdd.hAdd")
  
```

In this particular case, using `[Functor.map](Functors___-Monads-and--do--Notation/#Functor___mk "Documentation for Functor.map")` instead of explicit pattern matching helps:
`def List.findIndex (xs : [List](Basic-Types/Linked-Lists/#List___nil "Documentation for List") α) (p : α → [Bool](Basic-Types/Booleans/#Bool___false "Documentation for Bool")) : [Option](Basic-Types/Optional-Values/#Option___none "Documentation for Option") [Nat](Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat") :=   [match](Terms/Pattern-Matching/#Lean___Parser___Term___match "Documentation for syntax") xs [with](Terms/Pattern-Matching/#Lean___Parser___Term___match "Documentation for syntax")   | [] => [none](Basic-Types/Optional-Values/#Option___none "Documentation for Option.none")   | x::ys =>     [if](Terms/Conditionals/#termIfThenElse "Documentation for syntax") p x [then](Terms/Conditionals/#termIfThenElse "Documentation for syntax")       [some](Basic-Types/Optional-Values/#Option___none "Documentation for Option.some") 0     [else](Terms/Conditionals/#termIfThenElse "Documentation for syntax")       (· + 1) <$> List.findIndex ys p partial_fixpoint `
[Live ↪](javascript:openLiveLink\("CYUwZgBAMglgzgFwHRhgO2ASQyAHhAClzggC5p4EJBG4AEpCAHMmiQJMIIAhAey4Bt7yAeQYIYXNBAByAQyqkAvACgIEALayAxgAsIxCAHcYCLcogAfCAG0AuhHkA+CGnEhTF3KVIBPEg9MqYSCZ8YxA0fxUIOC5VEAgABgiQXjhXSMiCAHaIAGoIAEZ6AB4AEkdYRBR0LBx8HwgGRQZpACdRaV4AfVRcBi50BCA"\))
###  7.6.4.3. Partial Correctness Theorems[🔗](find/?domain=Verso.Genre.Manual.section&name=partial-correctness-theorem "Permalink")
For every function defined as a partial fixpoint, Lean proves that the defining equation is satisfied. This enables proofs by rewriting. However, these equational theorems are not sufficient for reasoning about the behavior of the function on arguments for which the function specification does not terminate. Code paths that lead to infinite recursion at runtime would end up as infinite chains of rewrites in a potential proof.
Partial fixpoints in suitable monads, on the other hand, provide additional theorems that map the undefined values from non-termination to suitable values in the monad. In the `[Option](Basic-Types/Optional-Values/#Option___none "Documentation for Option")` monad, then partial fixpoint equals `[Option.none](Basic-Types/Optional-Values/#Option___none "Documentation for Option.none")` on all function inputs for which the defining equation specifies non-termination. From this fact, Lean proves a _partial correctness theorem_ for the function which allows facts to be concluded when the function's result is `[Option.some](Basic-Types/Optional-Values/#Option___none "Documentation for Option.some")`.
Partial Correctness Theorem
Recall `[List.findIndex](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#List___findIndex-_LPAR_in-Partial-Correctness-Theorem_RPAR_ "Definition of example")` from an earlier example:
`def List.findIndex (xs : [List](Basic-Types/Linked-Lists/#List___nil "Documentation for List") α) (p : α → [Bool](Basic-Types/Booleans/#Bool___false "Documentation for Bool")) : [Option](Basic-Types/Optional-Values/#Option___none "Documentation for Option") [Nat](Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat") :=   [match](Terms/Pattern-Matching/#Lean___Parser___Term___match "Documentation for syntax") xs [with](Terms/Pattern-Matching/#Lean___Parser___Term___match "Documentation for syntax")   | [] => [none](Basic-Types/Optional-Values/#Option___none "Documentation for Option.none")   | x::ys =>     [if](Terms/Conditionals/#termIfThenElse "Documentation for syntax") p x [then](Terms/Conditionals/#termIfThenElse "Documentation for syntax")       [some](Basic-Types/Optional-Values/#Option___none "Documentation for Option.some") 0     [else](Terms/Conditionals/#termIfThenElse "Documentation for syntax")       (· + 1) <$> [List.findIndex](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#List___findIndex-_LPAR_in-Partial-Correctness-Theorem_RPAR_ "Definition of example") ys p partial_fixpoint `
With this function definition, Lean automatically proves the following partial correctness theorem:
`List.findIndex.partial_correctness.{u_1} {α : Type u_1}   (p : α → [Bool](Basic-Types/Booleans/#Bool___false "Documentation for Bool"))   (motive : [List](Basic-Types/Linked-Lists/#List___nil "Documentation for List") α → [Nat](Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat") → Prop)   (h :     ∀ (findIndex : [List](Basic-Types/Linked-Lists/#List___nil "Documentation for List") α → [Option](Basic-Types/Optional-Values/#Option___none "Documentation for Option") [Nat](Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat")),       (∀ (xs : [List](Basic-Types/Linked-Lists/#List___nil "Documentation for List") α) (r : [Nat](Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat")), findIndex xs = [some](Basic-Types/Optional-Values/#Option___none "Documentation for Option.some") r → motive xs r) →         ∀ (xs : [List](Basic-Types/Linked-Lists/#List___nil "Documentation for List") α) (r : [Nat](Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat")),           ([match](Terms/Pattern-Matching/#Lean___Parser___Term___match "Documentation for syntax") xs [with](Terms/Pattern-Matching/#Lean___Parser___Term___match "Documentation for syntax")               | [] => [none](Basic-Types/Optional-Values/#Option___none "Documentation for Option.none")               | x :: ys =>                 [if](Terms/Conditionals/#termIfThenElse "Documentation for syntax") p x = [true](Basic-Types/Booleans/#Bool___false "Documentation for Bool.true") [then](Terms/Conditionals/#termIfThenElse "Documentation for syntax") [some](Basic-Types/Optional-Values/#Option___none "Documentation for Option.some") 0                 [else](Terms/Conditionals/#termIfThenElse "Documentation for syntax") (fun x => x + 1) <$> findIndex ys) = [some](Basic-Types/Optional-Values/#Option___none "Documentation for Option.some") r →             motive xs r)   (xs : [List](Basic-Types/Linked-Lists/#List___nil "Documentation for List") α) (r : [Nat](Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat")) :   xs.[findIndex](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#List___findIndex-_LPAR_in-Partial-Correctness-Theorem_RPAR_ "Definition of example") p = [some](Basic-Types/Optional-Values/#Option___none "Documentation for Option.some") r →     motive xs r`
Here, the motive is a relation between the parameter and return types of `[List.findIndex](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#List___findIndex-_LPAR_in-Partial-Correctness-Theorem_RPAR_ "Definition of example")`, with the `[Option](Basic-Types/Optional-Values/#Option___none "Documentation for Option")` removed from the return type. If, when given an arbitrary partial function with a signature that's compatible with `[List.findIndex](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#List___findIndex-_LPAR_in-Partial-Correctness-Theorem_RPAR_ "Definition of example")`, the following hold:
  * the motive is satisfied for all inputs for which the arbitrary function returns a value (rather than `[none](Basic-Types/Optional-Values/#Option___none "Documentation for Option.none")`),
  * taking one rewriting step with the defining equation, in which the recursive calls are replaced by the arbitrary function, also implies the satisfaction of the motive


then the motive is satisfied for all inputs for which the `[List.findIndex](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#List___findIndex-_LPAR_in-Partial-Correctness-Theorem_RPAR_ "Definition of example")` returns `[some](Basic-Types/Optional-Values/#Option___none "Documentation for Option.some")`.
The partial correctness theorem is a reasoning principle. It can be used to prove that the resulting number is a valid index in the list and that the predicate holds for that index:
`theorem List.findIndex_implies_pred     (xs : [List](Basic-Types/Linked-Lists/#List___nil "Documentation for List") α) (p : α → [Bool](Basic-Types/Booleans/#Bool___false "Documentation for Bool")) :     xs.[findIndex](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#List___findIndex-_LPAR_in-Partial-Correctness-Theorem_RPAR_ "Definition of example") p = [some](Basic-Types/Optional-Values/#Option___none "Documentation for Option.some") i →     ∃x, xs[i]? = [some](Basic-Types/Optional-Values/#Option___none "Documentation for Option.some") x ∧ p x := byα:Type u_1i:[Nat](Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat")xs:[List](Basic-Types/Linked-Lists/#List___nil "Documentation for List") αp:α → [Bool](Basic-Types/Booleans/#Bool___false "Documentation for Bool")⊢ xs.[findIndex](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#List___findIndex-_LPAR_in-Partial-Correctness-Theorem_RPAR_ "Definition of example") p [=](Basic-Propositions/Propositional-Equality/#Eq___refl "Documentation for Eq") [some](Basic-Types/Optional-Values/#Option___none "Documentation for Option.some") i → [∃](Basic-Propositions/Quantifiers/#Exists___intro "Documentation for Exists") x[,](Basic-Propositions/Quantifiers/#Exists___intro "Documentation for Exists") xs[[](Type-Classes/Basic-Classes/#GetElem______mk "Documentation for GetElem?.getElem?")i[]](Type-Classes/Basic-Classes/#GetElem______mk "Documentation for GetElem?.getElem?")[?](Type-Classes/Basic-Classes/#GetElem______mk "Documentation for GetElem?.getElem?") ###  7.6.4.4. Mutual Recursion with Partial Fixpoints[🔗](find/?domain=Verso.Genre.Manual.section&name=mutual-partial-fixpoint "Permalink")
Lean supports the definition of [mutually recursive](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#--tech-term-mutually-recursive) functions using [partial fixpoint](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#--tech-term-partial-fixpoint). Mutual recursion may be introduced using a [mutual block](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#--tech-term-mutual-block), but it also results from ``Lean.Parser.Term.letrec : term```let rec` expressions and ``Lean.Parser.Command.declaration : command```where` blocks. The rules for mutual well-founded recursion are applied to a group of actually mutually recursive, lifted definitions, that results from the [elaboration steps](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#mutual-syntax) for mutual groups.
If all functions in the mutual group have the ``Lean.Parser.Command.declaration : command```partial_fixpoint` clause, then this strategy is used.
###  7.6.4.5. Theory and Construction[🔗](find/?domain=Verso.Genre.Manual.section&name=partial-fixpoint-theory "Permalink")
The construction builds on a variant of the Knaster–Tarski theorem: In a chain-complete partial order, every monotone function has a least fixed point.
The necessary theory is found in the `Lean.Order` namespace. This is not meant to be a general purpose library of order theoretic results. Instead, the definitions and theorems in `Lean.Order` are only intended as implementation details of the ``Lean.Parser.Command.declaration : command```partial_fixpoint` feature, and they should be considered a private API that may change without notice.
The notion of a partial order, and that of a chain-complete partial order, are represented by the type classes `[Lean.Order.PartialOrder](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#Lean___Order___PartialOrder___mk "Documentation for Lean.Order.PartialOrder")` and `[Lean.Order.CCPO](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#Lean___Order___CCPO___mk "Documentation for Lean.Order.CCPO")`, respectively.
[🔗](find/?domain=Verso.Genre.Manual.doc&name=Lean.Order.PartialOrder.mk "Permalink")type class
```


Lean.Order.PartialOrder.{u} (α : Sort u) : Sort (max 1 u)


Lean.Order.PartialOrder.{u} (α : Sort u) :
  Sort (max 1 u)


```

A partial order is a reflexive, transitive and antisymmetric relation.
This is intended to be used in the construction of `partial_fixpoint`, and not meant to be used otherwise.

```

A “less-or-equal-to” or “approximates” relation.
This is intended to be used in the construction of `partial_fixpoint`, and not meant to be used otherwise.

```

```

The “less-or-equal-to” or “approximates” relation is reflexive.

```
rel_trans : ∀ {x y z : α}, x [⊑](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#Lean___Order___PartialOrder___mk "Documentation for Lean.Order.PartialOrder.rel") y → y [⊑](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#Lean___Order___PartialOrder___mk "Documentation for Lean.Order.PartialOrder.rel") z → x [⊑](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#Lean___Order___PartialOrder___mk "Documentation for Lean.Order.PartialOrder.rel") z
```

The “less-or-equal-to” or “approximates” relation is transitive.

```
rel_antisymm : ∀ {x y : α}, x [⊑](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#Lean___Order___PartialOrder___mk "Documentation for Lean.Order.PartialOrder.rel") y → y [⊑](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#Lean___Order___PartialOrder___mk "Documentation for Lean.Order.PartialOrder.rel") x → x [=](Basic-Propositions/Propositional-Equality/#Eq___refl "Documentation for Eq") y
```

The “less-or-equal-to” or “approximates” relation is antisymmetric.

Lean.Order.CCPO.{u} (α : Sort u) : Sort (max 1 u)

  Sort (max 1 u)


```

A chain-complete partial order (CCPO) is a partial order where every chain has a least upper bound.
This is intended to be used in the construction of `partial_fixpoint`, and not meant to be used otherwise.
#  Instance Constructor

```
[Lean.Order.CCPO.mk](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#Lean___Order___CCPO___mk "Documentation for Lean.Order.CCPO.mk").{u}

The least upper bound of chains exists.
A function is monotone if it preserves partial orders. That is, if `x ⊑ y` then `f x ⊑ f y`. The operator `⊑` represent `[Lean.Order.PartialOrder.rel](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#Lean___Order___PartialOrder___mk "Documentation for Lean.Order.PartialOrder.rel")`.
[🔗](find/?domain=Verso.Genre.Manual.doc&name=Lean.Order.monotone "Permalink")def
```


Lean.Order.monotone.{u, v} {α : Sort u} [[PartialOrder](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#Lean___Order___PartialOrder___mk "Documentation for Lean.Order.PartialOrder") α] {β : Sort v}
  [[PartialOrder](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#Lean___Order___PartialOrder___mk "Documentation for Lean.Order.PartialOrder") β] (f : α → β) : Prop


Lean.Order.monotone.{u, v} {α : Sort u}
  [[PartialOrder](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#Lean___Order___PartialOrder___mk "Documentation for Lean.Order.PartialOrder") α] {β : Sort v}
  [[PartialOrder](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#Lean___Order___PartialOrder___mk "Documentation for Lean.Order.PartialOrder") β] (f : α → β) : Prop


```

A function is monotone if it maps related elements to related elements.
This is intended to be used in the construction of `partial_fixpoint`, and not meant to be used otherwise.
The fixpoint of a monotone function can be taken using `[fix](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#Lean___Order___fix "Documentation for Lean.Order.fix")`, which indeed constructs a fixpoint, as shown by `[fix_eq](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#Lean___Order___fix_eq "Documentation for Lean.Order.fix_eq")`,
[🔗](find/?domain=Verso.Genre.Manual.doc&name=Lean.Order.fix "Permalink")def
```


Lean.Order.fix.{u} {α : Sort u} [[CCPO](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#Lean___Order___CCPO___mk "Documentation for Lean.Order.CCPO") α] (f : α → α)
  (hmono : [monotone](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#Lean___Order___monotone "Documentation for Lean.Order.monotone") f) : α


Lean.Order.fix.{u} {α : Sort u} [[CCPO](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#Lean___Order___CCPO___mk "Documentation for Lean.Order.CCPO") α]
  (f : α → α) (hmono : [monotone](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#Lean___Order___monotone "Documentation for Lean.Order.monotone") f) : α


```

The least fixpoint of a monotone function is the least upper bound of its transfinite iteration.
The `[monotone](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#Lean___Order___monotone "Documentation for Lean.Order.monotone") f` assumption is not strictly necessarily for the definition, but without this the definition is not very meaningful and it simplifies applying theorems like `[fix_eq](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#Lean___Order___fix_eq "Documentation for Lean.Order.fix_eq")` if every use of `[fix](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#Lean___Order___fix "Documentation for Lean.Order.fix")` already has the monotonicity requirement.
This is intended to be used in the construction of `partial_fixpoint`, and not meant to be used otherwise.
[🔗](find/?domain=Verso.Genre.Manual.doc&name=Lean.Order.fix_eq "Permalink")theorem
```


Lean.Order.fix_eq.{u} {α : Sort u} [[CCPO](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#Lean___Order___CCPO___mk "Documentation for Lean.Order.CCPO") α] {f : α → α}
  (hf : [monotone](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#Lean___Order___monotone "Documentation for Lean.Order.monotone") f) : [fix](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#Lean___Order___fix "Documentation for Lean.Order.fix") f hf [=](Basic-Propositions/Propositional-Equality/#Eq___refl "Documentation for Eq") f ([fix](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#Lean___Order___fix "Documentation for Lean.Order.fix") f hf)


Lean.Order.fix_eq.{u} {α : Sort u}
  [[CCPO](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#Lean___Order___CCPO___mk "Documentation for Lean.Order.CCPO") α] {f : α → α} (hf : [monotone](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#Lean___Order___monotone "Documentation for Lean.Order.monotone") f) :
  [fix](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#Lean___Order___fix "Documentation for Lean.Order.fix") f hf [=](Basic-Propositions/Propositional-Equality/#Eq___refl "Documentation for Eq") f ([fix](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#Lean___Order___fix "Documentation for Lean.Order.fix") f hf)


```

The main fixpoint theorem for fixed points of monotone functions in chain-complete partial orders.
This is intended to be used in the construction of `partial_fixpoint`, and not meant to be used otherwise.
To construct the partial fixpoint, Lean first synthesizes a suitable `[CCPO](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#Lean___Order___CCPO___mk "Documentation for Lean.Order.CCPO")` instance.
  * If the function's result type has a dedicated instance, like `[Option](Basic-Types/Optional-Values/#Option___none "Documentation for Option")` has with `instCCPOOption`, this is used together with the instance for the function type, `instCCPOPi`, to construct an instance for the whole function's type.
  * Otherwise, if the function's type can be shown to be inhabited by a witness `w`, then the instance `FlatOrder.instCCPO` for the wrapper type `FlatOrder w` is used. In this order, `w` is a least element and all other elements are incomparable.


Next, the recursive calls in the right-hand side of the function definitions are abstracted; this turns into the argument `f` of `[fix](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#Lean___Order___fix "Documentation for Lean.Order.fix")`. The monotonicity requirement is solved by the `monotonicity` tactic, which applies compositional monotonicity lemmas in a syntax-driven way.
The tactic solves goals of the form `[monotone](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#Lean___Order___monotone "Documentation for Lean.Order.monotone") (fun x => … x …)` using the following steps:
  * Applying `monotone_const` when there is no dependency on `x` left.
  * Splitting on ``Lean.Parser.Term.match : term`
Pattern matching. `match e, ... with | p, ... => f | ...` matches each given term `e` against each pattern `p` of a match alternative. When all patterns of an alternative match, the `match` term evaluates to the value of the corresponding right-hand side `f` with the pattern variables bound to the respective matched values. If used as `match h : e, ... with | p, ... => f | ...`, `h : e = p` is available within `f`.
When not constructing a proof, `match` does not automatically substitute variables matched on in dependent variables' types. Use `match (generalizing := true) ...` to enforce this.
Syntax quotations can also be used in a pattern match. This matches a `Syntax` value against quotations, pattern variables, or `_`.
Quoted identifiers only match identical identifiers - custom matching such as by the preresolved names only should be done explicitly.
`Syntax.atom`s are ignored during matching by default except when part of a built-in literal. For users introducing new atoms, we recommend wrapping them in dedicated syntax kinds if they should participate in matching. For example, in

```
syntax "c" ("foo" <|> "bar") ...

```

`foo` and `bar` are indistinguishable during matching, but in

```
syntax foo := "foo"
syntax "c" (foo <|> "bar") ...

```

they are not.
`[`match`](Terms/Pattern-Matching/#Lean___Parser___Term___match) expressions.
  * Splitting on ``termIfThenElse : term`
`if c then t else e` is notation for `ite c t e`, "if-then-else", which decides to return `t` or `e` depending on whether `c` is true or false. The explicit argument `c : Prop` does not have any actual computational content, but there is an additional `[Decidable c]` argument synthesized by typeclass inference which actually determines how to evaluate `c` to true or false. Write `if h : c then t else e` instead for a "dependent if-then-else" `dite`, which allows `t`/`e` to use the fact that `c` is true/false.
`[`if`](Terms/Conditionals/#termIfThenElse) expressions.
  * Moving ``Lean.Parser.Term.let : term`
`let` is used to declare a local definition. Example:

```
let x := 1
let y := x + 1
x + y

```

Since functions are first class citizens in Lean, you can use `let` to declare local functions too.

```
let double := fun x => 2*x
double (double 3)

```

For recursive definitions, you should use `let rec`. You can also perform pattern matching using `let`. For example, assume `p` has type `Nat × Nat`, then you can write

```
let (x, y) := p
x + y

```

The _anaphoric let_ `let := v` defines a variable called `this`.
``let` expression to the context, if the value and type do not depend on `x`.
  * Zeta-reducing a ``Lean.Parser.Term.let : term`
`let` is used to declare a local definition. Example:

```
let x := 1
let y := x + 1
x + y

```

Since functions are first class citizens in Lean, you can use `let` to declare local functions too.

```
let double := fun x => 2*x
double (double 3)

```

For recursive definitions, you should use `let rec`. You can also perform pattern matching using `let`. For example, assume `p` has type `Nat × Nat`, then you can write

```
let (x, y) := p
x + y

```

The _anaphoric let_ `let := v` defines a variable called `this`.
``let` expression when value and type do depend on `x`.
  * Applying lemmas annotated with `partial_fixpoint_monotone`


The following monotonicity lemmas are registered, and should allow recursive calls under the given higher-order functions in the arguments indicated by `·` (but not the other arguments, shown as `_`).
