##  7.6.5. Partial and Unsafe Definitions[🔗](find/?domain=Verso.Genre.Manual.section&name=partial-unsafe "Permalink")
While most Lean functions can be reasoned about in Lean's type theory as well as compiled and run, definitions marked `partial` or `unsafe` cannot be meaningfully reasoned about. From the perspective of the logic, `partial` functions are opaque constants, and theorems that refer to `unsafe` definitions are summarily rejected. In exchange for the inability to use these functions for reasoning, there are far fewer requirements placed on them; this can make it possible to write programs that would be impractical or cost-prohibitive to prove anything about, while not giving up formal reasoning for the rest. In essence, the `partial` subset of Lean is a traditional functional programming language that is nonetheless deeply integrated with the theorem proving features, and the `unsafe` subset features the ability to break Lean's runtime invariants in certain rare situations, at the cost of less integration with Lean's theorem-proving features. Analogously, `noncomputable` definitions may use features that don't make sense in programs, but are meaningful in the logic.
###  7.6.5.1. Partial Functions[🔗](find/?domain=Verso.Genre.Manual.section&name=partial-functions "Permalink")
The `partial` modifier may only be applied to function definitions. Partial functions are not required to demonstrate termination, and Lean does not attempt to do so. These functions are “partial” in the sense that they do not necessarily specify a mapping from each element of the domain to an element of the codomain, because they might fail to terminate for some or all elements of the domain. They are elaborated into [pre-definitions](Elaboration-and-Compilation/#--tech-term-pre-definition) that contain explicit recursion, and type checked using the kernel; however, they are subsequently treated as opaque constants by the logic.
The function's return type must be inhabited; this ensures soundness. Otherwise, a partial function could have a type such as `[Unit](Basic-Types/The-Unit-Type/#Unit "Documentation for Unit") → [Empty](Basic-Types/The-Empty-Type/#Empty "Documentation for Empty")`. Together with `[Empty.elim](Basic-Types/The-Empty-Type/#Empty___elim "Documentation for Empty.elim")`, the existence of such a function could be used to prove `[False](Basic-Propositions/Truth/#False "Documentation for False")` even if it does not reduce.
With partial definitions, the kernel is responsible for the following:
  * It ensures that the pre-definition's type is indeed a well-formed type.
  * It checks that the pre-definition's type is a function type.
  * It ensures that the function's codomain is inhabited by demanding a `[Nonempty](Type-Classes/Basic-Classes/#Nonempty___intro "Documentation for Nonempty")` or `[Inhabited](Type-Classes/Basic-Classes/#Inhabited___mk "Documentation for Inhabited")` instance.
  * It checks that the resulting term would be type-correct if Lean had recursive definitions.


Even though recursive definitions are not part of the kernel's type theory, the kernel can still be used to check that the body of the definition has the right type. This works the same way as in other functional languages: uses of recursion are type checked by checking the body in an environment in which the definition is already associated with its type. Having ensured that it type checks, the body is discarded and only the opaque constant is retained by the kernel. As with all Lean functions, the compiler generates code from the elaborated [pre-definition](Elaboration-and-Compilation/#--tech-term-pre-definition).
Even though partial functions are not unfolded by the kernel, it is still possible to reason about other functions that call them so long as this reasoning doesn't depend on the implementation of the partial function itself.
Partial Functions in Proofs
The recursive function `[nextPrime](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#nextPrime-_LPAR_in-Partial-Functions-in-Proofs_RPAR_ "Definition of example")` inefficiently computes the next prime number after a given number by repeatedly testing candidates with trial division. Because there are infinitely many prime numbers, it always terminates; however, formulating this proof would be nontrivial. It is thus marked `partial`.
`def isPrime (n : [Nat](Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat")) : [Bool](Basic-Types/Booleans/#Bool___false "Documentation for Bool") := [Id.run](Functors___-Monads-and--do--Notation/Varieties-of-Monads/#Id___run "Documentation for Id.run") [do](Functors___-Monads-and--do--Notation/Syntax/#Lean___Parser___Term___do "Documentation for syntax")   for i in [2:n] do     if i * i > n then return [true](Basic-Types/Booleans/#Bool___false "Documentation for Bool.true")     if n % i = 0 then return [false](Basic-Types/Booleans/#Bool___false "Documentation for Bool.false")   return [true](Basic-Types/Booleans/#Bool___false "Documentation for Bool.true")  partial def nextPrime (n : [Nat](Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat")) : [Nat](Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat") :=   let n := n + 1   [if](Terms/Conditionals/#termIfThenElse "Documentation for syntax") [isPrime](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#isPrime-_LPAR_in-Partial-Functions-in-Proofs_RPAR_ "Definition of example") n [then](Terms/Conditionals/#termIfThenElse "Documentation for syntax") n [else](Terms/Conditionals/#termIfThenElse "Documentation for syntax") [nextPrime](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#nextPrime-_LPAR_in-Partial-Functions-in-Proofs_RPAR_ "Definition of example") n `
It is nonetheless possible to prove that the following two functions are equal:
`def answerUser (n : [Nat](Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat")) : [String](Basic-Types/Strings/#String___ofByteArray "Documentation for String") :=   s!"The next prime is {[nextPrime](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#nextPrime-_LPAR_in-Partial-Functions-in-Proofs_RPAR_ "Definition of example") n}"  def answerOtherUser (n : [Nat](Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat")) : [String](Basic-Types/Strings/#String___ofByteArray "Documentation for String") :=   " ".[intercalate](Basic-Types/Strings/#String___intercalate "Documentation for String.intercalate") [     "The",     "next",     "prime",     "is",     toString ([nextPrime](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#nextPrime-_LPAR_in-Partial-Functions-in-Proofs_RPAR_ "Definition of example") n)   ] `
In fact, the proof is by `[rfl](Tactic-Proofs/Tactic-Reference/#rfl "Documentation for tactic")`:
`theorem answer_eq_other : [answerUser](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#answerUser-_LPAR_in-Partial-Functions-in-Proofs_RPAR_ "Definition of example") = [answerOtherUser](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#answerOtherUser-_LPAR_in-Partial-Functions-in-Proofs_RPAR_ "Definition of example") := by⊢ [answerUser](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#answerUser-_LPAR_in-Partial-Functions-in-Proofs_RPAR_ "Definition of example") [=](Basic-Propositions/Propositional-Equality/#Eq___refl "Documentation for Eq") [answerOtherUser](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#answerOtherUser-_LPAR_in-Partial-Functions-in-Proofs_RPAR_ "Definition of example")   [rfl](Tactic-Proofs/Tactic-Reference/#rfl "Documentation for tactic")All goals completed! 🐙 `
[Live ↪](javascript:openLiveLink\("CYUwZgBAlgzgCgJygWxBAFAOwgLggOQEMAXASlwgCEB7agG1wF4IBJYAOgQFdthqAoCBDDUE0aNgDaAJhyYAuhD6Ch0SFAgAqcQD4I2YgAsQ2BCGJcEB7iBVCokbAFJxzAAwQjJiGYtXhhHQwtkK+ltZctvwADoQIxFCBSuD6IAAexIgoaFgURGR5JEwqdOb6TOUA1BAAjCoO0PBIqOVe2NggQWiY6ZnN3fz8oJCEmDAA7iAIAKrBYrl4+eR4AMrESJgA5sVCMACEAEQAKsapGRDR/Y0QAN49GVktmAC+B4PDEKMTUwDyXjNzDDYRYkZYQNYbbY4RgqA4QA7sKCYYhTADGgRIaEkdnhJxABwANDiDvdiITiZdsuTVPDYNTVMRqBCkdssL1Ht1SCp5IMvKIQMhPmNJggAPogACOouo/woXxFsymEGY8t+/0VYmhEAARgBPFQIMB0IA"\))
###  7.6.5.2. Unsafe Definitions[🔗](find/?domain=Verso.Genre.Manual.section&name=unsafe "Permalink")
Unsafe definitions have even fewer safeguards than partial functions. Their codomains do not need to be inhabited, they are not restricted to function definitions, and they have access to features of Lean that might violate internal invariants or break abstractions. As a result, they cannot be used at all as part of mathematical reasoning.
While partial functions are treated as opaque constants by the type theory, unsafe definitions may only be referenced from other unsafe definitions. As a consequence, any function that calls an unsafe function must be unsafe itself. Theorems are not allowed to be declared unsafe.
In addition to unrestricted use of recursion, unsafe functions can cast from one type to another, check whether two values are the very same object in memory, retrieve pointer values, and run `[IO](IO/Logical-Model/#IO "Documentation for IO")` actions from otherwise-pure code. Using these operators requires a thorough understanding of the Lean implementation.
[🔗](find/?domain=Verso.Genre.Manual.doc&name=unsafeCast "Permalink")unsafe def
```


unsafeCast.{u, v} {α : Sort u} {β : Sort v} (a : α) : β


unsafeCast.{u, v} {α : Sort u}
  {β : Sort v} (a : α) : β


```

This function will cast a value of type `α` to type `β`, and is a no-op in the compiler. This function is **extremely dangerous** because there is no guarantee that types `α` and `β` have the same data representation, and this can lead to memory unsafety. It is also logically unsound, since you could just cast `[True](Basic-Propositions/Truth/#True___intro "Documentation for True")` to `[False](Basic-Propositions/Truth/#False "Documentation for False")`. For all those reasons this function is marked as `unsafe`.
It is implemented by lifting both `α` and `β` into a common universe, and then using `cast (lcProof : ULift (PLift α) = ULift (PLift β))` to actually perform the cast. All these operations are no-ops in the compiler.
Using this function correctly requires some knowledge of the data representation of the source and target types. Some general classes of casts which are safe in the current runtime:
  * `[Array](Basic-Types/Arrays/#Array___mk "Documentation for Array") α` to `[Array](Basic-Types/Arrays/#Array___mk "Documentation for Array") β` where `α` and `β` have compatible representations, or more generally for other inductive types.
  * `[Quot](The-Type-System/Quotients/#Quot "Documentation for Quot") α r` and `α`.
  * `@[Subtype](Basic-Types/Subtypes/#Subtype___mk "Documentation for Subtype") α p` and `α`, or generally any structure containing only one non-`Prop` field of type `α`.
  * Casting `α` to/from `NonScalar` when `α` is a boxed generic type (i.e. a function that accepts an arbitrary type `α` and is not specialized to a scalar type like `[UInt8](Basic-Types/Fixed-Precision-Integers/#UInt8___ofBitVec "Documentation for UInt8")`).


[🔗](find/?domain=Verso.Genre.Manual.doc&name=ptrEq "Permalink")unsafe def
```


ptrEq.{u_1} {α : Type u_1} (a b : α) : [Bool](Basic-Types/Booleans/#Bool___false "Documentation for Bool")


ptrEq.{u_1} {α : Type u_1} (a b : α) :
  [Bool](Basic-Types/Booleans/#Bool___false "Documentation for Bool")


```

Compares two objects for pointer equality.
Two objects are pointer-equal if, at runtime, they are allocated at exactly the same address. This function is unsafe because it can distinguish between definitionally equal values.
[🔗](find/?domain=Verso.Genre.Manual.doc&name=ptrEqList "Permalink")unsafe def
```


ptrEqList.{u_1} {α : Type u_1} (as bs : [List](Basic-Types/Linked-Lists/#List___nil "Documentation for List") α) : [Bool](Basic-Types/Booleans/#Bool___false "Documentation for Bool")


ptrEqList.{u_1} {α : Type u_1}
  (as bs : [List](Basic-Types/Linked-Lists/#List___nil "Documentation for List") α) : [Bool](Basic-Types/Booleans/#Bool___false "Documentation for Bool")


```

Compares two lists of objects for element-wise pointer equality. Returns `[true](Basic-Types/Booleans/#Bool___false "Documentation for Bool.true")` if both lists are the same length and the objects at the corresponding indices of each list are pointer-equal.
Two objects are pointer-equal if, at runtime, they are allocated at exactly the same address. This function is unsafe because it can distinguish between definitionally equal values.
[🔗](find/?domain=Verso.Genre.Manual.doc&name=ptrAddrUnsafe "Permalink")unsafe opaque
```


ptrAddrUnsafe.{u} {α : Type u} (a : α) : [USize](Basic-Types/Fixed-Precision-Integers/#USize___ofBitVec "Documentation for USize")


ptrAddrUnsafe.{u} {α : Type u} (a : α) :
  [USize](Basic-Types/Fixed-Precision-Integers/#USize___ofBitVec "Documentation for USize")


```

Returns the address at which an object is allocated.
This function is unsafe because it can distinguish between definitionally equal values.
[🔗](find/?domain=Verso.Genre.Manual.doc&name=isExclusiveUnsafe "Permalink")unsafe opaque
```


isExclusiveUnsafe.{u} {α : Type u} (a : α) : [Bool](Basic-Types/Booleans/#Bool___false "Documentation for Bool")


isExclusiveUnsafe.{u} {α : Type u}
  (a : α) : [Bool](Basic-Types/Booleans/#Bool___false "Documentation for Bool")


```

Returns `[true](Basic-Types/Booleans/#Bool___false "Documentation for Bool.true")` if `a` is an exclusive object.
An object is exclusive if it is single-threaded and its reference counter is 1. This function is unsafe because it can distinguish between definitionally equal values.
[🔗](find/?domain=Verso.Genre.Manual.doc&name=unsafeIO "Permalink")unsafe def
```


unsafeIO {α : Type} (fn : [IO](IO/Logical-Model/#IO "Documentation for IO") α) : [Except](Functors___-Monads-and--do--Notation/Varieties-of-Monads/#Except___error "Documentation for Except") [IO.Error](IO/Logical-Model/#IO___Error___alreadyExists "Documentation for IO.Error") α


unsafeIO {α : Type} (fn : [IO](IO/Logical-Model/#IO "Documentation for IO") α) :
  [Except](Functors___-Monads-and--do--Notation/Varieties-of-Monads/#Except___error "Documentation for Except") [IO.Error](IO/Logical-Model/#IO___Error___alreadyExists "Documentation for IO.Error") α


```

Executes arbitrary side effects in a pure context, with exceptions indicated via `[Except](Functors___-Monads-and--do--Notation/Varieties-of-Monads/#Except___error "Documentation for Except")`. This a **dangerous** operation that can easily undermine important assumptions about the meaning of Lean programs, and it should only be used with great care and a thorough understanding of compiler internals, and even then only to implement observationally pure operations.
This function is not a good way to convert an `[EIO](IO/Logical-Model/#EIO "Documentation for EIO") α` or `[IO](IO/Logical-Model/#IO "Documentation for IO") α` into an `α`. Instead, use [`do`-notation](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.29.0-rc6/find/?domain=Verso.Genre.Manual.section&name=do-notation).
Because the resulting value is treated as a side-effect-free term, the compiler may re-order, duplicate, or delete calls to this function. The side effect may even be hoisted into a constant, causing the side effect to occur at initialization time, even if it would otherwise never be called.
[🔗](find/?domain=Verso.Genre.Manual.doc&name=unsafeEIO "Permalink")unsafe def
```


unsafeEIO {ε α : Type} (fn : [EIO](IO/Logical-Model/#EIO "Documentation for EIO") ε α) : [Except](Functors___-Monads-and--do--Notation/Varieties-of-Monads/#Except___error "Documentation for Except") ε α


unsafeEIO {ε α : Type} (fn : [EIO](IO/Logical-Model/#EIO "Documentation for EIO") ε α) :
  [Except](Functors___-Monads-and--do--Notation/Varieties-of-Monads/#Except___error "Documentation for Except") ε α


```

Executes arbitrary side effects in a pure context, with exceptions indicated via `[Except](Functors___-Monads-and--do--Notation/Varieties-of-Monads/#Except___error "Documentation for Except")`. This a **dangerous** operation that can easily undermine important assumptions about the meaning of Lean programs, and it should only be used with great care and a thorough understanding of compiler internals, and even then only to implement observationally pure operations.
This function is not a good way to convert an `[EIO](IO/Logical-Model/#EIO "Documentation for EIO") α` or `[IO](IO/Logical-Model/#IO "Documentation for IO") α` into an `α`. Instead, use [`do`-notation](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.29.0-rc6/find/?domain=Verso.Genre.Manual.section&name=do-notation).
Because the resulting value is treated as a side-effect-free term, the compiler may re-order, duplicate, or delete calls to this function. The side effect may even be hoisted into a constant, causing the side effect to occur at initialization time, even if it would otherwise never be called.
[🔗](find/?domain=Verso.Genre.Manual.doc&name=unsafeBaseIO "Permalink")unsafe def
```


unsafeBaseIO {α : Type} (fn : [BaseIO](IO/Logical-Model/#BaseIO "Documentation for BaseIO") α) : α


unsafeBaseIO {α : Type} (fn : [BaseIO](IO/Logical-Model/#BaseIO "Documentation for BaseIO") α) :
  α


```

Executes arbitrary side effects in a pure context. This a **dangerous** operation that can easily undermine important assumptions about the meaning of Lean programs, and it should only be used with great care and a thorough understanding of compiler internals, and even then only to implement observationally pure operations.
This function is not a good way to convert a `[BaseIO](IO/Logical-Model/#BaseIO "Documentation for BaseIO") α` into an `α`. Instead, use [`do`-notation](https://lean-lang.org/doc/reference/4.29.0-rc6/find/?domain=Verso.Genre.Manual.section&name=do-notation).
Because the resulting value is treated as a side-effect-free term, the compiler may re-order, duplicate, or delete calls to this function. The side effect may even be hoisted into a constant, causing the side effect to occur at initialization time, even if it would otherwise never be called.
Frequently, unsafe operators are used to write fast code that takes advantage of low-level details. Just as Lean code may be replaced at runtime with C code via the FFI, safe Lean code may be replaced with unsafe Lean code for runtime programs. This is accomplished by adding the `implemented_by` attribute to the function that is to be replaced, which is often an `opaque` definition. While this does not threaten Lean's soundness as a logic because the constant to be replaced has already been checked by the kernel and the unsafe replacement is only used in run-time code, it is still risky. Both C code and unsafe code may execute arbitrary side effects.
attributeReplacing Run-Time Implementations
The `implemented_by` attribute instructs the compiler to replace one constant with another in compiled code. The replacement constant may be unsafe.

```
attr ::= ...
    | implemented_by ident
```

Checking Equality with Pointers
Ordinarily, a `[BEq](Type-Classes/Basic-Classes/#BEq___mk "Documentation for BEq")` instance's equality predicate must fully traverse both of its arguments to determine whether they are equal. If they are, in fact, the very same object in memory, this is wasteful indeed. A pointer equality test can be used prior to the traversal to catch this case.
The type being compared is `[Tree](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#Tree-_LPAR_in-Checking-Equality-with-Pointers_RPAR_ "Definition of example")`, a type of binary trees.
`inductive Tree α where   | empty   | branch (left : [Tree](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#Tree-_LPAR_in-Checking-Equality-with-Pointers_RPAR_ "Definition of example") α) (val : α) (right : [Tree](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#Tree-_LPAR_in-Checking-Equality-with-Pointers_RPAR_ "Definition of example") α) `
An unsafe function may use pointer equality to terminate the structural equality test more quickly, falling back to structural checks when pointer equality fails.
`unsafe def Tree.fastBEq [[BEq](Type-Classes/Basic-Classes/#BEq___mk "Documentation for BEq") α] (t1 t2 : [Tree](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#Tree-_LPAR_in-Checking-Equality-with-Pointers_RPAR_ "Definition of example") α) : [Bool](Basic-Types/Booleans/#Bool___false "Documentation for Bool") :=   [if](Terms/Conditionals/#termIfThenElse "Documentation for syntax") [ptrEq](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#ptrEq "Documentation for ptrEq") t1 t2 [then](Terms/Conditionals/#termIfThenElse "Documentation for syntax")     [true](Basic-Types/Booleans/#Bool___false "Documentation for Bool.true")   [else](Terms/Conditionals/#termIfThenElse "Documentation for syntax")     [match](Terms/Pattern-Matching/#Lean___Parser___Term___match "Documentation for syntax") t1, t2 [with](Terms/Pattern-Matching/#Lean___Parser___Term___match "Documentation for syntax")     | [.empty](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#Tree___empty-_LPAR_in-Checking-Equality-with-Pointers_RPAR_ "Definition of example"), [.empty](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#Tree___empty-_LPAR_in-Checking-Equality-with-Pointers_RPAR_ "Definition of example") => [true](Basic-Types/Booleans/#Bool___false "Documentation for Bool.true")     | [.branch](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#Tree___branch-_LPAR_in-Checking-Equality-with-Pointers_RPAR_ "Definition of example") l1 x r1, [.branch](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#Tree___branch-_LPAR_in-Checking-Equality-with-Pointers_RPAR_ "Definition of example") l2 y r2 =>       [if](Terms/Conditionals/#termIfThenElse "Documentation for syntax") [ptrEq](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#ptrEq "Documentation for ptrEq") x y || x == y [then](Terms/Conditionals/#termIfThenElse "Documentation for syntax")         l1.[fastBEq](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#Tree___fastBEq-_LPAR_in-Checking-Equality-with-Pointers_RPAR_ "Definition of example") l2 && r1.[fastBEq](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#Tree___fastBEq-_LPAR_in-Checking-Equality-with-Pointers_RPAR_ "Definition of example") r2       [else](Terms/Conditionals/#termIfThenElse "Documentation for syntax") [false](Basic-Types/Booleans/#Bool___false "Documentation for Bool.false")     | _, _ => [false](Basic-Types/Booleans/#Bool___false "Documentation for Bool.false") `
An `implemented_by` attribute on an opaque definition bridges the worlds of safe and unsafe code.
`@[implemented_by [Tree.fastBEq](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#Tree___fastBEq-_LPAR_in-Checking-Equality-with-Pointers_RPAR_ "Definition of example")] opaque Tree.beq [[BEq](Type-Classes/Basic-Classes/#BEq___mk "Documentation for BEq") α] (t1 t2 : [Tree](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#Tree-_LPAR_in-Checking-Equality-with-Pointers_RPAR_ "Definition of example") α) : [Bool](Basic-Types/Booleans/#Bool___false "Documentation for Bool")  instance [[BEq](Type-Classes/Basic-Classes/#BEq___mk "Documentation for BEq") α] : [BEq](Type-Classes/Basic-Classes/#BEq___mk "Documentation for BEq") ([Tree](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#Tree-_LPAR_in-Checking-Equality-with-Pointers_RPAR_ "Definition of example") α) where   [beq](Type-Classes/Basic-Classes/#BEq___mk "Documentation for BEq.beq") := [Tree.beq](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#Tree___beq-_LPAR_in-Checking-Equality-with-Pointers_RPAR_ "Definition of example") `
[Live ↪](javascript:openLiveLink\("JYOwJgrgxgLsBuBTABAFQE6JYRuBkHcALRTAKGWQB9lEBbABxgE8zLkAjdAQxCgOQAoANogBmMZAC40mHAEoB8ToMnJs8/umABzAuKkYsq2SRIQQAZ04iUYUdKwA6EZ3MwAQgFEAjsgDann2wAXQEYAEZkGAAmFQM5FTcAe0TlCQBeFmARZAZ0b0iI6MiiEBZyGHQIRBZEQXNq8nIaThheAoAaSJi8YBgCMtYHWgZGTqH6JmQ0gD5IyobGqgcObjbBCIAPZHQwsZWePkEYxm2YmYHyLJyK/K2TiiottLTkE77EUsav5HWnF3d8kdkAAyYHbMJ/VwBU4Xah1FDOeEDKgAfU6KKms0R9RMAAFfMB6MIaB8YIgwCi2Cc4pCAV4giREnROF4qvZEMtED5/PlgqFCjF9DIjAlkoITKBXKsUDzAiEpND+HERYRiAs2FzJC8aRqvEA"\))
Taking Advantage of Run-Time Representations
Because a `[Fin](Basic-Types/Finite-Natural-Numbers/#Fin___mk "Documentation for Fin")` is represented identically to its underlying `[Nat](Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat")`, `[List.map](Basic-Types/Linked-Lists/#List___map "Documentation for List.map") [Fin.val](Basic-Types/Finite-Natural-Numbers/#Fin___mk "Documentation for Fin.val")` can be replaced by `[unsafeCast](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#unsafeCast "Documentation for unsafeCast")` to avoid a linear-time traversal that, in practice, does nothing:
`unsafe def unFinImpl (xs : [List](Basic-Types/Linked-Lists/#List___nil "Documentation for List") ([Fin](Basic-Types/Finite-Natural-Numbers/#Fin___mk "Documentation for Fin") n)) : [List](Basic-Types/Linked-Lists/#List___nil "Documentation for List") [Nat](Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat") :=   [unsafeCast](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#unsafeCast "Documentation for unsafeCast") xs  @[implemented_by [unFinImpl](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#unFinImpl-_LPAR_in-Taking-Advantage-of-Run-Time-Representations_RPAR_ "Definition of example")] def unFin (xs : [List](Basic-Types/Linked-Lists/#List___nil "Documentation for List") ([Fin](Basic-Types/Finite-Natural-Numbers/#Fin___mk "Documentation for Fin") n)) : [List](Basic-Types/Linked-Lists/#List___nil "Documentation for List") [Nat](Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat") :=   xs.[map](Basic-Types/Linked-Lists/#List___map "Documentation for List.map") [Fin.val](Basic-Types/Finite-Natural-Numbers/#Fin___mk "Documentation for Fin.val") `
From the perspective of the Lean kernel, `[unFin](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#unFin-_LPAR_in-Taking-Advantage-of-Run-Time-Representations_RPAR_ "Definition of example")` is defined using `[List.map](Basic-Types/Linked-Lists/#List___map "Documentation for List.map")`:
`theorem unFin_length_eq_length {xs : [List](Basic-Types/Linked-Lists/#List___nil "Documentation for List") ([Fin](Basic-Types/Finite-Natural-Numbers/#Fin___mk "Documentation for Fin") n)} :     ([unFin](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#unFin-_LPAR_in-Taking-Advantage-of-Run-Time-Representations_RPAR_ "Definition of example") xs).[length](Basic-Types/Linked-Lists/#List___length "Documentation for List.length") = xs.[length](Basic-Types/Linked-Lists/#List___length "Documentation for List.length") := byn:[Nat](Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat")xs:[List](Basic-Types/Linked-Lists/#List___nil "Documentation for List") ([Fin](Basic-Types/Finite-Natural-Numbers/#Fin___mk "Documentation for Fin") n)⊢ ([unFin](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#unFin-_LPAR_in-Taking-Advantage-of-Run-Time-Representations_RPAR_ "Definition of example") xs).[length](Basic-Types/Linked-Lists/#List___length "Documentation for List.length") [=](Basic-Propositions/Propositional-Equality/#Eq___refl "Documentation for Eq") xs.[length](Basic-Types/Linked-Lists/#List___length "Documentation for List.length")   [simp](Tactic-Proofs/Tactic-Reference/#simp "Documentation for tactic") [[unFin](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#unFin-_LPAR_in-Taking-Advantage-of-Run-Time-Representations_RPAR_ "Definition of example")]All goals completed! 🐙 `
In compiled code, there is no traversal of the list.
This kind of replacement is risky: the correspondence between the proof and the compiled code depends fully on the equivalence of the two implementations, which cannot be proved in Lean. The correspondence relies on details of Lean's implementation. These “escape hatches” should be used very carefully.
[Live ↪](javascript:openLiveLink\("K4OwzghgZgpgBAExlOoBiBLEBJAtgBwBs4AKADzDgC44AZDMAF1MxDhAEoPq6HmA5CMyoBeAFBxU4aDADCEJnApixAAQDaGAoRi4YIRjAQB9AEYBPKazxEAumKQp0WUhR71FJVuy7u+cQWFxSQoAOlwIfDhWUIA3CEIgA"\))
##  7.6.6. Controlling Reduction[🔗](find/?domain=Verso.Genre.Manual.section&name=reducibility "Permalink")
While checking proofs and programs, Lean takes _reducibility_ , also known as _transparency_ , into account. A definition's reducibility controls the contexts in which it is unfolded during elaboration and proof execution.
There are three levels of reducibility: 

Reducible 
    
Reducible definitions are unfolded essentially everywhere, on demand. Type class instance synthesis, definitional equality checks, and the rest of the language treat the definition as being essentially an abbreviation. This is the setting applied by the ``Lean.Parser.Command.declaration : command```abbrev` command. 

Semireducible 
    
Semireducible definitions are not unfolded by potentially expensive automation such as type class instance synthesis or `[simp](Tactic-Proofs/Tactic-Reference/#simp "Documentation for tactic")`, but they are unfolded while checking definitional equality and while resolving [generalized field notation](Terms/Function-Application/#--tech-term-generalized-field-notation). The ``Lean.Parser.Command.declaration : command```def` command generally creates semireducible definitions unless a different reducibility level is specified with an attribute; however, definitions that use [well-founded recursion](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#--tech-term-well-founded-recursion) are irreducible by default. 

Irreducible 
    
Irreducible definitions are not unfolded at all during elaboration. Definitions can be made irreducible by applying the `irreducible` attribute. Reducibility and Instance Synthesis
These three aliases for `[String](Basic-Types/Strings/#String___ofByteArray "Documentation for String")` are respectively reducible, semireducible, and irreducible.
`abbrev Phrase := [String](Basic-Types/Strings/#String___ofByteArray "Documentation for String")  def Clause := [String](Basic-Types/Strings/#String___ofByteArray "Documentation for String")  @[irreducible] def Utterance := [String](Basic-Types/Strings/#String___ofByteArray "Documentation for String") `
The reducible and semireducible aliases are unfolded during the elaborator's definitional equality check, causing them to be considered equivalent to `[String](Basic-Types/Strings/#String___ofByteArray "Documentation for String")`:
`def hello : [Phrase](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#Phrase-_LPAR_in-Reducibility-and-Instance-Synthesis_RPAR_ "Definition of example") := "Hello"  def goodMorning : [Clause](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#Clause-_LPAR_in-Reducibility-and-Instance-Synthesis_RPAR_ "Definition of example") := "Good morning" `
The irreducible alias, on the other hand, is rejected as the type for a string, because the elaborator's definitional equality test does not unfold it:
`def goodEvening : [Utterance](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#Utterance-_LPAR_in-Reducibility-and-Instance-Synthesis_RPAR_ "Definition of example") := `Type mismatch   "Good evening" has type   [String](Basic-Types/Strings/#String___ofByteArray "Documentation for String") but is expected to have type   [Utterance](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#Utterance-_LPAR_in-Reducibility-and-Instance-Synthesis_RPAR_ "Definition of example")`"Good evening" `
```
Type mismatch
  "Good evening"
has type
  [String](Basic-Types/Strings/#String___ofByteArray "Documentation for String")
but is expected to have type
  [Utterance](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#Utterance-_LPAR_in-Reducibility-and-Instance-Synthesis_RPAR_ "Definition of example")
```

Because `[Phrase](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#Phrase-_LPAR_in-Reducibility-and-Instance-Synthesis_RPAR_ "Definition of example")` is reducible, the `ToString [String](Basic-Types/Strings/#String___ofByteArray "Documentation for String")` instance can be used as a `ToString [Phrase](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#Phrase-_LPAR_in-Reducibility-and-Instance-Synthesis_RPAR_ "Definition of example")` instance:
``instToStringString`[#synth](Interacting-with-Lean/#Lean___Parser___Command___synth "Documentation for syntax") ToString [Phrase](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#Phrase-_LPAR_in-Reducibility-and-Instance-Synthesis_RPAR_ "Definition of example") `
However, `[Clause](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#Clause-_LPAR_in-Reducibility-and-Instance-Synthesis_RPAR_ "Definition of example")` is semireducible, so the `ToString [String](Basic-Types/Strings/#String___ofByteArray "Documentation for String")` instance cannot be used:
``failed to synthesize   ToString [Clause](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#Clause-_LPAR_in-Reducibility-and-Instance-Synthesis_RPAR_ "Definition of example")  Hint: Additional diagnostic information may be available using the `set_option diagnostics true` command.`[#synth](Interacting-with-Lean/#Lean___Parser___Command___synth "Documentation for syntax") ToString [Clause](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#Clause-_LPAR_in-Reducibility-and-Instance-Synthesis_RPAR_ "Definition of example") `
```
failed to synthesize
  ToString [Clause](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#Clause-_LPAR_in-Reducibility-and-Instance-Synthesis_RPAR_ "Definition of example")

Hint: Additional diagnostic information may be available using the `set_option diagnostics true` command.
```

The instance can be explicitly enabled by creating a `ToString [Clause](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#Clause-_LPAR_in-Reducibility-and-Instance-Synthesis_RPAR_ "Definition of example")` instance that reduces to the `ToString [String](Basic-Types/Strings/#String___ofByteArray "Documentation for String")` instance. This example works because semireducible definitions are unfolded while checking definitional equality:
`instance : ToString [Clause](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#Clause-_LPAR_in-Reducibility-and-Instance-Synthesis_RPAR_ "Definition of example") := [inferInstanceAs](Type-Classes/Instance-Synthesis/#inferInstanceAs "Documentation for inferInstanceAs") (ToString [String](Basic-Types/Strings/#String___ofByteArray "Documentation for String")) `
[Live ↪](javascript:openLiveLink\("IYIxCcFMDcAIAUAW5gGdKwFwF5YGUAXcASwDsBzAKEoBNIAzWAYQBtgBXdLXQki6gAIBtYuCg12AY2IgWkALq0GsAKoECkFKUkYc+ImSpLGiSCxYB7LAmRpduAEQAJM5YfU6jchYs0AshbgpIbWrBxceg4A4j40sAC2gcEU7pQAxKgAnqQEiLAAKha8IUgo6NRkqATA2roFRQYUzGyc9rBk9JoAkqRVNToAgqiwABSFxU0T5ACUQA"\))
Reducibility and Generalized Field Notation
[Generalized field notation](Terms/Function-Application/#--tech-term-generalized-field-notation) unfolds reducible and semireducible declarations while searching for matching names. Given the semireducible alias `[Sequence](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#Sequence-_LPAR_in-Reducibility-and-Generalized-Field-Notation_RPAR_ "Definition of example")` for `[List](Basic-Types/Linked-Lists/#List___nil "Documentation for List")`:
`def Sequence := [List](Basic-Types/Linked-Lists/#List___nil "Documentation for List")  def Sequence.ofList (xs : [List](Basic-Types/Linked-Lists/#List___nil "Documentation for List") α) : [Sequence](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#Sequence-_LPAR_in-Reducibility-and-Generalized-Field-Notation_RPAR_ "Definition of example") α := xs `
generalized field notation allows `[List.reverse](Basic-Types/Linked-Lists/#List___reverse "Documentation for List.reverse")` to be accessed from a term of type `[Sequence](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#Sequence-_LPAR_in-Reducibility-and-Generalized-Field-Notation_RPAR_ "Definition of example") [Nat](Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat")`.
``let xs := [Sequence.ofList](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#Sequence___ofList-_LPAR_in-Reducibility-and-Generalized-Field-Notation_RPAR_ "Definition of example") [[](Basic-Types/Linked-Lists/#List___nil "Documentation for List.cons")1[,](Basic-Types/Linked-Lists/#List___nil "Documentation for List.cons") 2[,](Basic-Types/Linked-Lists/#List___nil "Documentation for List.cons") 3[]](Basic-Types/Linked-Lists/#List___nil "Documentation for List.cons"); [List.reverse](Basic-Types/Linked-Lists/#List___reverse "Documentation for List.reverse") xs : [List](Basic-Types/Linked-Lists/#List___nil "Documentation for List") [Nat](Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat")`[#check](Interacting-with-Lean/#Lean___Parser___Command___check "Documentation for syntax") let xs : [Sequence](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#Sequence-_LPAR_in-Reducibility-and-Generalized-Field-Notation_RPAR_ "Definition of example") [Nat](Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat") := [.ofList](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#Sequence___ofList-_LPAR_in-Reducibility-and-Generalized-Field-Notation_RPAR_ "Definition of example") [1,2,3]; xs.[reverse](Basic-Types/Linked-Lists/#List___reverse "Documentation for List.reverse") `
However, declaring `[Sequence](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#Sequence-_LPAR_in-Reducibility-and-Generalized-Field-Notation_RPAR_ "Definition of example")` to be irreducible prevents the unfolding:
`[attribute](Attributes/#Lean___Parser___Command___attribute "Documentation for syntax") [irreducible] [Sequence](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#Sequence-_LPAR_in-Reducibility-and-Generalized-Field-Notation_RPAR_ "Definition of example")  `let xs := [Sequence.ofList](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#Sequence___ofList-_LPAR_in-Reducibility-and-Generalized-Field-Notation_RPAR_ "Definition of example") [[](Basic-Types/Linked-Lists/#List___nil "Documentation for List.cons")1[,](Basic-Types/Linked-Lists/#List___nil "Documentation for List.cons") 2[,](Basic-Types/Linked-Lists/#List___nil "Documentation for List.cons") 3[]](Basic-Types/Linked-Lists/#List___nil "Documentation for List.cons"); sorry : ?m.13`[#check](Interacting-with-Lean/#Lean___Parser___Command___check "Documentation for syntax") let xs : [Sequence](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#Sequence-_LPAR_in-Reducibility-and-Generalized-Field-Notation_RPAR_ "Definition of example") [Nat](Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat") := [.ofList](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#Sequence___ofList-_LPAR_in-Reducibility-and-Generalized-Field-Notation_RPAR_ "Definition of example") [1,2,3]; xs.`Invalid field `reverse`: The environment does not contain `Sequence.reverse`, so it is not possible to project the field `reverse` from an expression   xs of type `[Sequence](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#Sequence-_LPAR_in-Reducibility-and-Generalized-Field-Notation_RPAR_ "Definition of example") [Nat](Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat")``reverse `
```
Invalid field `reverse`: The environment does not contain `Sequence.reverse`, so it is not possible to project the field `reverse` from an expression
  xs
of type `[Sequence](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#Sequence-_LPAR_in-Reducibility-and-Generalized-Field-Notation_RPAR_ "Definition of example") [Nat](Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat")`
```

[Live ↪](javascript:openLiveLink\("CYUwZgBAyiCOCuIB2BjEEBcBeCAZAlgM4AuAUKaJDAsmgHQD2YBJEAFAB6GZ5HESBG4ACUPaolToBmHF3IBiFAAsQKANYQANiH5dRccWggA5AIb9sERsz4QA2gEYANACZHAZgC6Abghc6AJxAANxB/QhAgA"\))
attributeReducibility Annotations
A definition's reducibility can be set using one of the three reducibility attributes:

```
attr ::= ...
    | reducible
```

```
attr ::= ...
    | semireducible
```

```
attr ::= ...
    | irreducible
```

These attributes can only be applied globally in the same file as the definition being modified, but they may be ``Lean.Parser.Term.attrKind```local`ly applied anywhere.
###  7.6.6.1. Reducibility and Tactics[🔗](find/?domain=Verso.Genre.Manual.section&name=The-Lean-Language-Reference--Definitions--Recursive-Definitions--Controlling-Reduction--Reducibility-and-Tactics "Permalink")
The tactics `with_reducible`, `with_reducible_and_instances`, and `with_unfolding_all` control which definitions are unfolded by most tactics.
Reducibility and Tactics
The functions `[plus](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#plus-_LPAR_in-Reducibility-and-Tactics_RPAR_ "Definition of example")`, `[sum](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#sum-_LPAR_in-Reducibility-and-Tactics_RPAR_ "Definition of example")`, and `[tally](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#tally-_LPAR_in-Reducibility-and-Tactics_RPAR_ "Definition of example")` are all synonyms for `[Nat.add](Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___add "Documentation for Nat.add")` that are respectively reducible, semireducible, and irreducible:
`abbrev plus := [Nat.add](Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___add "Documentation for Nat.add")  def sum := [Nat.add](Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___add "Documentation for Nat.add")  @[irreducible] def tally := [Nat.add](Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___add "Documentation for Nat.add") `
The reducible synonym is unfolded by `[simp](Tactic-Proofs/Tactic-Reference/#simp "Documentation for tactic")`:
`theorem plus_eq_add : [plus](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#plus-_LPAR_in-Reducibility-and-Tactics_RPAR_ "Definition of example") x y = x + y := byx:[Nat](Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat")y:[Nat](Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat")⊢ [plus](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#plus-_LPAR_in-Reducibility-and-Tactics_RPAR_ "Definition of example") x y [=](Basic-Propositions/Propositional-Equality/#Eq___refl "Documentation for Eq") x [+](Type-Classes/Basic-Classes/#HAdd___mk "Documentation for HAdd.hAdd") y [simp](Tactic-Proofs/Tactic-Reference/#simp "Documentation for tactic")All goals completed! 🐙 `
The semireducible synonym is not, however, unfolded by `[simp](Tactic-Proofs/Tactic-Reference/#simp "Documentation for tactic")`:
`theorem sum_eq_add : [sum](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#sum-_LPAR_in-Reducibility-and-Tactics_RPAR_ "Definition of example") x y = x + y := byx:[Nat](Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat")y:[Nat](Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat")⊢ [sum](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#sum-_LPAR_in-Reducibility-and-Tactics_RPAR_ "Definition of example") x y [=](Basic-Propositions/Propositional-Equality/#Eq___refl "Documentation for Eq") x [+](Type-Classes/Basic-Classes/#HAdd___mk "Documentation for HAdd.hAdd") y ``simp` made no progress`[simp](Tactic-Proofs/Tactic-Reference/#simp "Documentation for tactic")x:[Nat](Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat")y:[Nat](Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat")⊢ [sum](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#sum-_LPAR_in-Reducibility-and-Tactics_RPAR_ "Definition of example") x y [=](Basic-Propositions/Propositional-Equality/#Eq___refl "Documentation for Eq") x [+](Type-Classes/Basic-Classes/#HAdd___mk "Documentation for HAdd.hAdd") y `
Nonetheless, the definitional equality check induced by `[rfl](Tactic-Proofs/Tactic-Reference/#rfl "Documentation for tactic")` unfolds the `[sum](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#sum-_LPAR_in-Reducibility-and-Tactics_RPAR_ "Definition of example")`:
`theorem sum_eq_add : [sum](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#sum-_LPAR_in-Reducibility-and-Tactics_RPAR_ "Definition of example") x y = x + y := byx:[Nat](Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat")y:[Nat](Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat")⊢ [sum](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#sum-_LPAR_in-Reducibility-and-Tactics_RPAR_ "Definition of example") x y [=](Basic-Propositions/Propositional-Equality/#Eq___refl "Documentation for Eq") x [+](Type-Classes/Basic-Classes/#HAdd___mk "Documentation for HAdd.hAdd") y [rfl](Tactic-Proofs/Tactic-Reference/#rfl "Documentation for tactic")All goals completed! 🐙 `
The irreducible `[tally](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#tally-_LPAR_in-Reducibility-and-Tactics_RPAR_ "Definition of example")`, however, is not reduced by definitional equality.
`theorem tally_eq_add : [tally](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#tally-_LPAR_in-Reducibility-and-Tactics_RPAR_ "Definition of example") x y = x + y := byx:[Nat](Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat")y:[Nat](Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat")⊢ [tally](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#tally-_LPAR_in-Reducibility-and-Tactics_RPAR_ "Definition of example") x y [=](Basic-Propositions/Propositional-Equality/#Eq___refl "Documentation for Eq") x [+](Type-Classes/Basic-Classes/#HAdd___mk "Documentation for HAdd.hAdd") y `Tactic `rfl` failed: The left-hand side   [tally](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#tally-_LPAR_in-Reducibility-and-Tactics_RPAR_ "Definition of example") x y is not definitionally equal to the right-hand side   x [+](Type-Classes/Basic-Classes/#HAdd___mk "Documentation for HAdd.hAdd") y  x y:[Nat](Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat")⊢ [tally](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#tally-_LPAR_in-Reducibility-and-Tactics_RPAR_ "Definition of example") x y [=](Basic-Propositions/Propositional-Equality/#Eq___refl "Documentation for Eq") x [+](Type-Classes/Basic-Classes/#HAdd___mk "Documentation for HAdd.hAdd") y`[rfl](Tactic-Proofs/Tactic-Reference/#rfl "Documentation for tactic")x:[Nat](Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat")y:[Nat](Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat")⊢ [tally](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#tally-_LPAR_in-Reducibility-and-Tactics_RPAR_ "Definition of example") x y [=](Basic-Propositions/Propositional-Equality/#Eq___refl "Documentation for Eq") x [+](Type-Classes/Basic-Classes/#HAdd___mk "Documentation for HAdd.hAdd") y `
The `[simp](Tactic-Proofs/Tactic-Reference/#simp "Documentation for tactic")` tactic can unfold any definition, even irreducible ones, when they are explicitly provided:
`theorem tally_eq_add : [tally](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#tally-_LPAR_in-Reducibility-and-Tactics_RPAR_ "Definition of example") x y = x + y := byx:[Nat](Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat")y:[Nat](Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat")⊢ [tally](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#tally-_LPAR_in-Reducibility-and-Tactics_RPAR_ "Definition of example") x y [=](Basic-Propositions/Propositional-Equality/#Eq___refl "Documentation for Eq") x [+](Type-Classes/Basic-Classes/#HAdd___mk "Documentation for HAdd.hAdd") y [simp](Tactic-Proofs/Tactic-Reference/#simp "Documentation for tactic") [[tally](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#tally-_LPAR_in-Reducibility-and-Tactics_RPAR_ "Definition of example")]All goals completed! 🐙 `
Similarly, part of a proof can be instructed to ignore irreducibility by placing it in a `with_unfolding_all` block:
`theorem tally_eq_add : [tally](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#tally-_LPAR_in-Reducibility-and-Tactics_RPAR_ "Definition of example") x y = x + y := byx:[Nat](Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat")y:[Nat](Basic-Types/Natural-Numbers/#Nat___zero "Documentation for Nat")⊢ [tally](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#tally-_LPAR_in-Reducibility-and-Tactics_RPAR_ "Definition of example") x y [=](Basic-Propositions/Propositional-Equality/#Eq___refl "Documentation for Eq") x [+](Type-Classes/Basic-Classes/#HAdd___mk "Documentation for HAdd.hAdd") y with_unfolding_all [rfl](Tactic-Proofs/Tactic-Reference/#rfl "Documentation for tactic")All goals completed! 🐙 `
[Live ↪](javascript:openLiveLink\("IYIxCcFMDcAIAcA2BXAzrAXAXlgOWAC4B0wAJqQFAWmQBmsqyAtpjvsWZRQAIDaAluCilkAY34hEkALrU6sAsESIAnqzyES5KgQAWkAPZQWSNAH1IARzOdMCFOgAesNTmcBqF+pBrU/JvA6+kaQLIxMFta2GAzMsM6u8bCeatiwPrDgtIhBhsYKSqqRNuR2ispqCbBuyV5pGQDu/HpmyAB2tAaIpPxtAOY2ypnZQA"\))
###  7.6.6.2. Modifying Reducibility[🔗](find/?domain=Verso.Genre.Manual.section&name=The-Lean-Language-Reference--Definitions--Recursive-Definitions--Controlling-Reduction--Modifying-Reducibility "Permalink")
The reducibility of a definition can be globally modified in the module in which it is defined by applying the appropriate attribute with the ``Lean.Parser.Command.attribute : command``[`attribute`](Attributes/#Lean___Parser___Command___attribute) command. In other modules, the reducibility of imported definitions can be modified by applying the attribute with the `local` modifier. The ``Lean.Parser.commandSeal__ : command`
The `seal foo` command ensures that the definition of `foo` is sealed, meaning it is marked as `[irreducible]`. This command is particularly useful in contexts where you want to prevent the reduction of `foo` in proofs.
In terms of functionality, `seal foo` is equivalent to `attribute [local irreducible] foo`. This attribute specifies that `foo` should be treated as irreducible only within the local scope, which helps in maintaining the desired abstraction level without affecting global settings.
`[`seal`](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#Lean___Parser___commandSeal__) and ``Lean.Parser.commandUnseal__ : command`
The `unseal foo` command ensures that the definition of `foo` is unsealed, meaning it is marked as `[semireducible]`, the default reducibility setting. This command is useful when you need to allow some level of reduction of `foo` in proofs.
Functionally, `unseal foo` is equivalent to `attribute [local semireducible] foo`. Applying this attribute makes `foo` semireducible only within the local scope.
`[`unseal`](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#Lean___Parser___commandUnseal__) commands are a shorthand for this process.
syntaxLocal Irreducibility
The `seal foo` command ensures that the definition of `foo` is sealed, meaning it is marked as `[irreducible]`. This command is particularly useful in contexts where you want to prevent the reduction of `foo` in proofs.
In terms of functionality, `seal foo` is equivalent to `attribute [local irreducible] foo`. This attribute specifies that `foo` should be treated as irreducible only within the local scope, which helps in maintaining the desired abstraction level without affecting global settings.

```
command ::= ...
    | 


The seal foo command ensures that the definition of foo is sealed, meaning it is marked as [irreducible].
This command is particularly useful in contexts where you want to prevent the reduction of foo in proofs.


In terms of functionality, seal foo is equivalent to attribute [local irreducible] foo.
This attribute specifies that foo should be treated as irreducible only within the local scope,
which helps in maintaining the desired abstraction level without affecting global settings.


seal ident ident*
```

syntaxLocal Reducibility
The `unseal foo` command ensures that the definition of `foo` is unsealed, meaning it is marked as `[semireducible]`, the default reducibility setting. This command is useful when you need to allow some level of reduction of `foo` in proofs.
Functionally, `unseal foo` is equivalent to `attribute [local semireducible] foo`. Applying this attribute makes `foo` semireducible only within the local scope.

```
command ::= ...
    | 


The unseal foo command ensures that the definition of foo is unsealed, meaning it is marked as [semireducible], the
default reducibility setting. This command is useful when you need to allow some level of reduction of foo in proofs.


Functionally, unseal foo is equivalent to attribute [local semireducible] foo.
Applying this attribute makes foo semireducible only within the local scope.


unseal ident ident*
```

###  7.6.6.3. Options[🔗](find/?domain=Verso.Genre.Manual.section&name=The-Lean-Language-Reference--Definitions--Recursive-Definitions--Controlling-Reduction--Options "Permalink")
For performance, the elaborator and many tactics construct indices and caches. Many of these take reducibility into account, and there's no way to invalidate and regenerate them if reducibility changes globally. Unsafe changes to reducibility settings that could have unpredictable results are disallowed by default, but they can be enabled by using the `[allowUnsafeReducibility](Definitions/Recursive-Definitions/#allowUnsafeReducibility "Documentation for option allowUnsafeReducibility")` option.
[🔗](find/?domain=Verso.Genre.Manual.doc.option&name=allowUnsafeReducibility "Permalink")option
```
allowUnsafeReducibility
```

Default value: `[false](Basic-Types/Booleans/#Bool___false "Documentation for Bool.false")`
enables users to modify the reducibility settings for declarations even when such changes are deemed potentially hazardous. For example, `[simp](Tactic-Proofs/Tactic-Reference/#simp "Documentation for tactic")` and type class resolution maintain term indices where reducible declarations are expanded.
[←7.5. Example Declarations](Definitions/Example-Declarations/#The-Lean-Language-Reference--Definitions--Example-Declarations "7.5. Example Declarations")[8. Axioms→](Axioms/#axioms "8. Axioms")
